<h1 class="firstHeading" id="firstHeading" lang="en">Portal:Current events/November 2004</h1>
<div class="mw-body-content" id="bodyContent">
<div id="siteSub">From Wikipedia, the free encyclopedia</div>

<p><b><a href="/wiki/November" title="November">November</a></b> <b><a href="/wiki/2004" title="2004">2004</a></b> was the eleventh month of that leap year. The month, which began on a <a href="/wiki/Monday" title="Monday">Monday</a>, ended on a <a href="/wiki/Tuesday" title="Tuesday">Tuesday</a> after 30 days.</p>
<p></p>

<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="November_1.2C_2004_.28Monday.29">November 1, 2004 (Monday)</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Portal:Current_events/November_2004&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: November 1, 2004 (Monday)">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<ul>
<li>The <a href="/wiki/Gr%C3%ADmsv%C3%B6tn" title="Grímsvötn">Grímsvötn</a> volcano under the <a href="/wiki/Vatnaj%C3%B6kull" title="Vatnajökull">Vatnajökull</a> glacier in <a href="/wiki/Iceland" title="Iceland">Iceland</a> erupts <a class="external text" href="http://news.bbc.co.uk/1/hi/sci/tech/3982273.stm" rel="nofollow">(BBC)</a>.</li>
<li>An inquiry by the Egyptian Interior Ministry into last month's bombings of hotels in the <a href="/wiki/Sinai_Peninsula" title="Sinai Peninsula">Sinai</a> concludes that the perpetrators received no external help, contradicting assertions by Israeli officials that the blasts were linked to <a href="/wiki/Al-Qaeda" title="Al-Qaeda">al-Qaeda</a>. <a class="external text" href="http://reuters.com/newsArticle.jhtml?type=worldNews&amp;storyID=6676122&amp;section=news" rel="nofollow">(Reuters)</a> <a class="external text" href="http://news.bbc.co.uk/2/hi/middle_east/3972635.stm" rel="nofollow">(BBC)</a></li>
<li><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Conflict_in_Iraq" title="Conflict in Iraq">Conflict in Iraq</a>:
<ul>
<li>The deputy <a href="/wiki/Governor" title="Governor">governor</a> of <a href="/wiki/Baghdad" title="Baghdad">Baghdad</a>, <a href="/wiki/Hatem_Kamil" title="Hatem Kamil">Hatem Kamil</a>, is <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Assassinated" title="Assassinated">assassinated</a>. The <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Insurgent" title="Insurgent">militant</a> group <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Army_of_Ansar_al-Sunna" title="Army of Ansar al-Sunna">Army of Ansar al-Sunna</a> claims responsibility. <a class="external text" href="http://reuters.com/newsArticle.jhtml?type=worldNews&amp;storyID=6678472&amp;pageNumber=1" rel="nofollow">(Reuters)</a><a class="external text" href="http://news.bbc.co.uk/2/hi/middle_east/3972569.stm" rel="nofollow">(BBC)</a></li>
<li>A <a href="/wiki/Reuters" title="Reuters">Reuters</a> cameraman is shot dead by suspected <a href="/wiki/Sniper" title="Sniper">sniper</a> fire. In <a href="/wiki/Ramadi" title="Ramadi">Ramadi</a>, hospital officials report six dead from fighting between <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/United_States_armed_forces" title="United States armed forces">United States armed forces</a> and rebels. A U.S. citizen, an unidentified <a href="/wiki/Nepal" title="Nepal">Nepali</a> and four <a href="/wiki/Iraq" title="Iraq">Iraqi</a> workers are taken hostage at gunpoint from their office in <a href="/wiki/Baghdad" title="Baghdad">Baghdad</a>. <a class="external text" href="http://reuters.com/newsArticle.jhtml?type=worldNews&amp;storyID=6678472&amp;pageNumber=1" rel="nofollow">(Reuters)</a><a class="external text" href="http://news.bbc.co.uk/2/hi/middle_east/3972569.stm" rel="nofollow">(BBC)</a></li>
</ul>
</li>
<li>Over 300 mm of rain fall on <a href="/wiki/Venice" title="Venice">Venice</a>, Italy, flooding an estimated 80% of the city and shutting down the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Public_transit" title="Public transit">public transit</a> system. <a class="external text" href="http://www.reuters.co.uk/newsArticle.jhtml?type=scienceNews&amp;storyID=6668269&amp;section=news" rel="nofollow">(Reuters)</a> <a class="external text" href="http://www9.sbs.com.au/theworldnews/region.php?id=97898&amp;region=3" rel="nofollow">(SBS)</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Chief_Justice_of_the_United_States" title="Chief Justice of the United States">Chief Justice</a> of the U.S. <a href="/wiki/Supreme_Court_of_the_United_States" title="Supreme Court of the United States">Supreme Court</a> <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/William_H._Rehnquist" title="William H. Rehnquist">William H. Rehnquist</a>, who has been undergoing <a href="/wiki/Radiation_therapy" title="Radiation therapy">radiation</a> and <a href="/wiki/Chemotherapy" title="Chemotherapy">chemotherapy</a> treatments for <a href="/wiki/Thyroid_cancer" title="Thyroid cancer">thyroid cancer</a>, announces he will delay his return to the courtroom on the advice of his doctors. <a class="external text" href="http://www.cnn.com/2004/LAW/11/01/rehnquist.cancer.ap/index.html" rel="nofollow">(CNN)</a></li>
<li><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Israeli-Palestinian_conflict" title="Israeli-Palestinian conflict">Israeli-Palestinian conflict</a>: A <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Suicide_bombing" title="Suicide bombing">suicide bombing</a> by a 16-year-old <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Palestinian_people" title="Palestinian people">Palestinian</a> boy in <a href="/wiki/Tel_Aviv" title="Tel Aviv">Tel Aviv</a> kills three and wounds over 30 people. The <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Marxist" title="Marxist">Marxist</a> <a href="/wiki/Popular_Front_for_the_Liberation_of_Palestine" title="Popular Front for the Liberation of Palestine">Popular Front for the Liberation of Palestine</a> claims responsibility. <a class="external text" href="http://reuters.com/newsArticle.jhtml?type=worldNews&amp;storyID=6679582&amp;section=news" rel="nofollow">(Reuters)</a><a class="external text" href="http://news.bbc.co.uk/2/hi/middle_east/3970995.stm" rel="nofollow">(BBC)</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Martial_law" title="Martial law">Martial law</a> is imposed in parts of China's <a href="/wiki/Henan" title="Henan">Henan</a> province after fighting between <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Hui_Chinese" title="Hui Chinese">Hui Chinese</a> and <a href="/wiki/Han_Chinese" title="Han Chinese">Han Chinese</a> ethnic groups kills between 7 and 148 people. <a class="external text" href="http://www.time.com/time/asia/magazine/article/0,13673,501041115-750858,00.html" rel="nofollow">(<i>Time</i>)</a><a class="external text" href="http://news.bbc.co.uk/2/hi/asia-pacific/3970611.stm" rel="nofollow">(BBC)</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Bank_of_Japan" title="Bank of Japan">Bank of Japan</a> began to issue new <a href="/wiki/Japanese_yen" title="Japanese yen">Japanese yen</a> <a href="/wiki/Banknote" title="Banknote">banknotes</a>, known as <a href="/wiki/Japanese_yen#Series_E_.282004.2C_the_current_issue.29" title="Japanese yen"><i>Series E</i></a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-1"><a href="#cite_note-1">[1]</a></sup></li>
</ul>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="November_2.2C_2004_.28Tuesday.29">November 2, 2004 (Tuesday)</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Portal:Current_events/November_2004&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: November 2, 2004 (Tuesday)">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<ul>
<li><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Conflict_in_Iraq" title="Conflict in Iraq">Conflict in Iraq</a>: Iraqi officials report at least eight dead in a <a href="/wiki/Car_bomb" title="Car bomb">car bomb</a> outside the education ministry in <a href="/wiki/Baghdad" title="Baghdad">Baghdad</a>. In <a href="/wiki/Mosul" title="Mosul">Mosul</a>, another car bomb kills two and wounds four <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Iraqi_National_Guard" title="Iraqi National Guard">Iraqi National Guard</a>. <a class="external text" href="http://reuters.com/newsArticle.jhtml?type=worldNews&amp;storyID=6692993&amp;pageNumber=1" rel="nofollow">(Reuters)</a><a class="external text" href="http://news.bbc.co.uk/2/hi/americas/3975195.stm" rel="nofollow">(BBC)</a></li>
<li><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Darfur_conflict" title="Darfur conflict">Darfur conflict</a>: <a href="/wiki/United_Nations" title="United Nations">United Nations</a> officials say <a href="/wiki/Sudan" title="Sudan">Sudanese</a> troops have surrounded two <a href="/wiki/Refugee_camp" title="Refugee camp">refugee camps</a> in <a href="/wiki/Darfur" title="Darfur">Darfur</a> and are blocking access. The Sudanese military say they were asked to protect refugees and evict imposters. <a class="external text" href="http://reuters.com/newsArticle.jhtml;jsessionid=EVZE42F4WFOF2CRBAE0CFEY?type=worldNews&amp;storyID=6692960" rel="nofollow">(Reuters)</a><a class="external text" href="http://news.bbc.co.uk/2/hi/africa/3974289.stm" rel="nofollow">(BBC)</a></li>
<li>Attempts to totally outlaw parents <a href="/wiki/Spanking" title="Spanking">spanking</a> children in <a href="/wiki/England_and_Wales" title="England and Wales">England and Wales</a> fail as a majority of 424 to 75 <a href="/wiki/Member_of_parliament" title="Member of parliament">members of parliament</a> vote against the ban. <a class="external text" href="http://news.bbc.co.uk/1/hi/uk_politics/3972453.stm" rel="nofollow">(BBC)</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/NASA" title="NASA">NASA</a> says it will resume its <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Space_shuttle_program" title="Space shuttle program">space shuttle program</a> next May or early June after a lengthy investigation of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Columbia_disaster" title="Columbia disaster">Columbia disaster</a> in 2003, and a setback of a March date due to an active <a href="/wiki/2004_Atlantic_hurricane_season" title="2004 Atlantic hurricane season">2004 Atlantic hurricane season</a>. <a class="external text" href="http://news.bbc.co.uk/1/hi/sci/tech/3967045.stm" rel="nofollow">(BBC)</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/United_Arab_Emirates" title="United Arab Emirates">UAE</a> president and founding father <a href="/wiki/Zayed_bin_Sultan_Al_Nahyan" title="Zayed bin Sultan Al Nahyan">Sheikh Zayed</a> dies. Vice-President and Prime Minister <a href="/wiki/Maktoum_bin_Rashid_Al_Maktoum" title="Maktoum bin Rashid Al Maktoum">Sheikh Maktoum</a> temporarily assumes presidential role. <a class="external text" href="http://www.reuters.co.uk/newsPackageArticle.jhtml?type=worldNews&amp;storyID=613984&amp;section=news" rel="nofollow">(Reuters)</a></li>
<li>Controversial Dutch filmmaker <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Theo_van_Gogh_(Film_director)" title="Theo van Gogh (Film director)">Theo van Gogh</a> is stabbed and shot dead in <a href="/wiki/Amsterdam" title="Amsterdam">Amsterdam</a>; the suspected murderer is arrested after a firefight with police. van Gogh had received numerous death threats after his movie <i><a href="/wiki/Submission_(2004_film)" title="Submission (2004 film)">Submission</a></i> elicited criticism among the Dutch Muslim community. <a class="external text" href="http://www.reuters.com/newsArticle.jhtml?type=worldNews&amp;storyID=6686490&amp;section=news" rel="nofollow">(Reuters)</a> <a class="external text" href="http://abcnews.go.com/Entertainment/wireStory?id=217865" rel="nofollow">(ABC US)</a></li>
<li><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/US_presidential_election,_2004" title="US presidential election, 2004">U.S. presidential election</a>:
<ul>
<li>U.S. civil rights organizations report on a number of misleading voter fliers and phone calls aimed at <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/African-American" title="African-American">African-American</a> voters, alleging that these are an attempt to suppress the African-American vote in today's <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/US_presidential_election,_2004" title="US presidential election, 2004">U.S. presidential election</a>. <a class="external text" href="http://www.reuters.co.uk/newsPackageArticle.jhtml?type=worldNews&amp;storyID=613416&amp;section=news" rel="nofollow">(Reuters)</a></li>
<li><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/U.S._presidential_election,_2004_timeline" title="U.S. presidential election, 2004 timeline">U.S. presidential election, 2004 timeline</a>: Voting begins for the 2004 U.S. <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/US_presidential_election,_2004" title="US presidential election, 2004">presidential election</a>, as well as for <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/U.S._Congress_election,_2004" title="U.S. Congress election, 2004">elections to the U.S. Congress</a> and many <a href="/wiki/U.S._state" title="U.S. state">state</a> and local offices. The incumbent, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/United_States_Republican_Party" title="United States Republican Party">Republican</a> <a href="/wiki/George_W._Bush" title="George W. Bush">George W. Bush</a>, and the challenger, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/United_States_Democratic_Party" title="United States Democratic Party">Democrat</a> <a href="/wiki/John_Kerry" title="John Kerry">John Kerry</a>, are statistically tied in the latest opinion polls.</li>
</ul>
</li>
<li><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Puerto_Rico_General_Elections_of_2004" title="Puerto Rico General Elections of 2004">Puerto Rico General Elections</a>:
<ul>
<li><a href="/wiki/An%C3%ADbal_Acevedo_Vil%C3%A1" title="Aníbal Acevedo Vilá">Aníbal Acevedo Vilá</a> leads with 3,880 votes of advantage against <a href="/wiki/Pedro_Rossell%C3%B3" title="Pedro Rosselló">Pedro Rosselló</a> with 98.27% of the total votes counted. By law, a recount must be performed when the winning margin is less than 0.5%. The official winner will be certified on December 31 after the recount is finished. <a class="external text" href="http://www.ceepur.org/" rel="nofollow">(CEE-PUR)</a></li>
<li>The <a href="/wiki/Puerto_Rican_Independence_Party" title="Puerto Rican Independence Party">Puerto Rican Independence Party</a> has been unable to reach 3% of the total votes so far, putting in danger their franchise as a principal political party by Puerto Rican electoral laws. Because of this, the party may not receive funds from the <a href="/wiki/Government_of_Puerto_Rico" title="Government of Puerto Rico">government of Puerto Rico</a> nor have a separate column in <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Ballot_paper" title="Ballot paper">ballot papers</a> on the following elections. However, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Maria_de_Lourdes_Santiago" title="Maria de Lourdes Santiago">Maria de Lourdes Santiago</a> makes history by becoming the first woman to be elected <a href="/wiki/Senate_of_Puerto_Rico" title="Senate of Puerto Rico">Senator</a> in the party's history. <a class="external text" href="http://endi.com/elecciones2004/noticia.asp?newsid=7CDB9A33-E61B-4B42-909D-79B79FEF8F98" rel="nofollow">(El Nuevo Dia)</a></li>
</ul>
</li>
</ul>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="November_3.2C_2004_.28Wednesday.29">November 3, 2004 (Wednesday)</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Portal:Current_events/November_2004&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: November 3, 2004 (Wednesday)">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<ul>
<li><a href="/wiki/Khalifa_bin_Zayed_Al_Nahyan" title="Khalifa bin Zayed Al Nahyan">Khalifa bin Zayed Al Nahyan</a>, the son of <a href="/wiki/Zayed_bin_Sultan_Al_Nahyan" title="Zayed bin Sultan Al Nahyan">Sheikh Zayed bin Sultan Al Nahyan</a> who died yesterday, is elected President by the <a href="/wiki/United_Arab_Emirates" title="United Arab Emirates">United Arab Emirates</a>' federal council. <a class="external text" href="http://www.reuters.com/newsArticle.jhtml?type=worldNews&amp;storyID=6703716&amp;section=news" rel="nofollow">(Reuters)</a></li>
<li><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/2004_U.S._Presidential_election" title="2004 U.S. Presidential election">2004 U.S. Presidential election</a>:
<ul>
<li>Senator <a href="/wiki/John_Kerry" title="John Kerry">John Kerry</a> concedes to President <a href="/wiki/George_W._Bush" title="George W. Bush">George W. Bush</a> "The outcome should be decided by voters, not a protracted legal process", Kerry said. "I would not give up if there was a chance we could prevail." <a class="external text" href="http://reuters.com/newsArticle.jhtml?type=topNews&amp;storyID=6703896" rel="nofollow">(Reuters)</a> <a class="external text" href="http://news.bbc.co.uk/1/hi/world/americas/3980533.stm" rel="nofollow">(BBC)</a></li>
<li><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/United_States_Republican_Party" title="United States Republican Party">Republican</a> President <a href="/wiki/George_W._Bush" title="George W. Bush">George W. Bush</a> wins the popular vote, receiving <span class="nowrap">3.58 million</span> more votes than <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/United_States_Democratic_Party" title="United States Democratic Party">Democratic</a> <a href="/wiki/United_States_Senate" title="United States Senate">Senator</a> <a href="/wiki/John_Kerry" title="John Kerry">John Kerry</a>. (51.6% to 48.4%, <span class="nowrap">59.0 million</span> to <span class="nowrap">55.4 million</span>) Claiming victory in the <a href="/wiki/Swing_state" title="Swing state">swing state</a> of <a href="/wiki/Ohio" title="Ohio">Ohio</a>, Bush will probably have more than the 270 votes needed when the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/U.S._Electoral_College" title="U.S. Electoral College">U.S. Electoral College</a> meets on December 13. <a class="external text" href="http://www.cnn.com/ELECTION/2004/" rel="nofollow">(CNN)</a></li>
<li>The <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/United_States_Republican_Party" title="United States Republican Party">Republican Party</a> widens its majority in the <a href="/wiki/United_States_Senate" title="United States Senate">Senate</a> and <a href="/wiki/United_States_House_of_Representatives" title="United States House of Representatives">House of Representatives</a>. Democratic Senate Minority Leader <a href="/wiki/Tom_Daschle" title="Tom Daschle">Tom Daschle</a> concedes defeat to Republican challenger <a href="/wiki/John_Thune" title="John Thune">John Thune</a>, thus becoming the first Senate leader in 52 years to lose a re-election bid and leaving the leadership of the Democratic Party in the Senate open. <a class="external text" href="http://www.cnn.com/2004/ALLPOLITICS/11/02/senate.main/index.html" rel="nofollow">(CNN)</a></li>
<li>The <a href="/wiki/Electronic_Frontier_Foundation" title="Electronic Frontier Foundation">Electronic Frontier Foundation</a> (EFF) reports that on November 2, touch-screen <a href="/wiki/Electronic_voting" title="Electronic voting">electronic voting</a> machines in at least six U.S. states had incorrectly recorded their choices, including for the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/U.S._presidential_election,_2004" title="U.S. presidential election, 2004">presidential election</a>. Incorrectly recorded votes make up roughly 20 percent of the e-voting problems. <a class="external text" href="http://www.eff.org/news/archives/2004_11.php#002062" rel="nofollow">(EFF)</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Same-sex_marriage_in_the_United_States" title="Same-sex marriage in the United States">Same-sex marriage in the United States</a>: <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Gay_rights" title="Gay rights">Gay rights</a> activists suffer a severe setback when <a href="/wiki/U.S._state_constitutional_amendments_banning_same-sex_unions" title="U.S. state constitutional amendments banning same-sex unions">state constitutional amendments</a> prohibiting <a href="/wiki/Same-sex_marriage" title="Same-sex marriage">same-sex marriage</a> are passed in eleven states: <a href="/wiki/Arkansas" title="Arkansas">Arkansas</a>, <a href="/wiki/Georgia_(U.S._state)" title="Georgia (U.S. state)">Georgia</a>, <a href="/wiki/Kentucky" title="Kentucky">Kentucky</a>, <a href="/wiki/Michigan" title="Michigan">Michigan</a>, <a href="/wiki/Mississippi" title="Mississippi">Mississippi</a>, <a href="/wiki/Montana" title="Montana">Montana</a>, <a href="/wiki/North_Dakota" title="North Dakota">North Dakota</a>, <a href="/wiki/Oklahoma" title="Oklahoma">Oklahoma</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ohio" title="Ohio">Ohio</a>, <a href="/wiki/Oregon" title="Oregon">Oregon</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Utah" title="Utah">Utah</a>. The measures in Oregon, Mississippi, and Montana ban same-sex marriage only, while Arkansas, Georgia, Kentucky, North Dakota, Oklahoma, Ohio, and Utah ban both same-sex marriage and <a href="/wiki/Civil_union" title="Civil union">civil unions</a> and Michigan bans granting any benefits whatsoever to same-sex couples.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-2"><a href="#cite_note-2">[2]</a></sup></li>
</ul>
</li>
<li><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Conflict_in_Iraq" title="Conflict in Iraq">Conflict in Iraq</a>:
<ul>
<li>A roadside bomb kills a U.S. soldier and wounds another in <a href="/wiki/Salman_Pak" title="Salman Pak">Salman Pak</a>, south of <a href="/wiki/Baghdad" title="Baghdad">Baghdad</a>. An <a href="/wiki/Iraq" title="Iraq">Iraqi</a> Oil Ministry official is shot dead while leaving his house in Baghdad. The <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Insurgent" title="Insurgent">militant</a> group <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Jaish_Ansar_al-Sunna" title="Jaish Ansar al-Sunna">Army of Ansar al-Sunna</a> release a video on their website confirming the beheading of an Iraqi officer kidnapped in <a href="/wiki/Mosul" title="Mosul">Mosul</a>. In <a href="/wiki/Tikrit" title="Tikrit">Tikrit</a>, fires continue to burn from major oil wells and a pipeline attacked earlier, halting oil exports. The militant <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Brigades_of_Iraq%27s_Honorable_People&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Brigades of Iraq's Honorable People (page does not exist)">Brigades of Iraq's Honorable People</a> release videos showing beheadings of three Iraqi security guards kidnapped in Baghdad. <a class="external text" href="http://reuters.com/newsArticle.jhtml?type=worldNews&amp;storyID=6704830&amp;pageNumber=0" rel="nofollow">(Reuters)</a> <a class="external text" href="http://news.bbc.co.uk/1/hi/world/middle_east/3977379.stm" rel="nofollow">(BBC)</a></li>
<li>The <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Court_martial" title="Court martial">court martial</a> begins for nine U.S. <a href="/wiki/United_States_Marine_Corps" title="United States Marine Corps">marines</a> charged with the death of an Iraqi prisoner who died after being dragged by his neck to a pen at <a href="/wiki/Camp_Whitehorse" title="Camp Whitehorse">Camp Whitehorse</a> jail near <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Nassiriyah" title="Nassiriyah">Nassiriyah</a>. <a class="external text" href="http://reuters.com/newsArticle.jhtml?type=topNews&amp;storyID=6704982&amp;section=news" rel="nofollow">(Reuters)</a></li>
<li>Hungary announces the withdrawal of its 300 troops by the end of next March. Poland says it will scale back the 2,500 troops stationed in Iraq early next year. <a class="external text" href="http://reuters.com/newsArticle.jhtml?type=worldNews&amp;storyID=6703743" rel="nofollow">(Reuters)</a><a class="external text" href="http://news.bbc.co.uk/1/hi/world/europe/3979349.stm" rel="nofollow">(BBC)</a></li>
</ul>
</li>
<li>Sgt. <a href="/wiki/Charles_Robert_Jenkins" title="Charles Robert Jenkins">Charles Robert Jenkins</a>, who crossed over the <a href="/wiki/Demilitarized_zone" title="Demilitarized zone">DMZ</a> to <a href="/wiki/North_Korea" title="North Korea">North Korea</a> in 1965, pleads guilty to <a href="/wiki/Desertion" title="Desertion">desertion</a> and aiding the enemy at his court martial in Japan. He is sentenced to 30 days in prison and given a dishonorable discharge. <a class="external text" href="http://news.bbc.co.uk/2/hi/asia-pacific/3975055.stm" rel="nofollow">(BBC)</a></li>
<li>The <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Republic_of_China" title="Republic of China">Republic of China</a> (Taiwan) establishes diplomatic relations with <a href="/wiki/Vanuatu" title="Vanuatu">Vanuatu</a>, bringing <a href="/wiki/Foreign_relations_of_Taiwan" title="Foreign relations of Taiwan">its international recognition</a> to 27 countries. <a class="external text" href="http://edition.cnn.com/2004/WORLD/asiapcf/11/02/taiwan.vanuatu.ap/index.html" rel="nofollow">(CNN)</a></li>
<li><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Puerto_Rico_General_Elections_of_2004" title="Puerto Rico General Elections of 2004">Puerto Rico General Elections</a>:
<ul>
<li>The <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/State_Commission_of_Elections_of_Puerto_Rico" title="State Commission of Elections of Puerto Rico">State Commission of Elections of Puerto Rico</a> preliminarily certifies <a href="/wiki/An%C3%ADbal_Acevedo_Vil%C3%A1" title="Aníbal Acevedo Vilá">Aníbal Acevedo Vilá</a> as the winning candidate for <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/List_of_Governors_of_Puerto_Rico" title="List of Governors of Puerto Rico">Governor of Puerto Rico</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Luis_Fortu%C3%B1o" title="Luis Fortuño">Luis Fortuño</a> as <a href="/wiki/Resident_Commissioner_of_Puerto_Rico" title="Resident Commissioner of Puerto Rico">Resident Commissioner</a> after computing 98.3% of the total votes. A full recount will begin on November 9 to announce the official winner. <a class="external text" href="http://www.endi.com/elecciones2004/noticia.asp?newsid=3DC2C262-908F-45EF-A14A-6B0BAC2ABB57" rel="nofollow">(El Nuevo Día)</a> <a class="external text" href="http://www.ceepur.org/" rel="nofollow">(CEE-PUR)</a></li>
<li>The <a href="/wiki/Senate_of_Puerto_Rico" title="Senate of Puerto Rico">Senate of Puerto Rico</a> and the <a href="/wiki/House_of_Representatives_of_Puerto_Rico" title="House of Representatives of Puerto Rico">House of Representatives</a> will be dominated by the <a href="/wiki/New_Progressive_Party_of_Puerto_Rico" title="New Progressive Party of Puerto Rico">New Progressive Party</a> for the new term. Future senators from the party have already decided certain positions for once they are in office, and how do they plan to work with a governor of the opposing party. <a class="external text" href="http://www.endi.com/elecciones2004/noticia.asp?newsid=3DC2C262-908F-45EF-A14A-6B0BAC2ABB57" rel="nofollow">(El Nuevo Día)</a></li>
</ul>
</li>
</ul>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="November_4.2C_2004_.28Thursday.29">November 4, 2004 (Thursday)</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Portal:Current_events/November_2004&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: November 4, 2004 (Thursday)">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<ul>
<li>The shutdown of the Number 2 <a href="/wiki/Balakovo" title="Balakovo">Balakovo</a> <a href="/wiki/Nuclear_reactor" title="Nuclear reactor">nuclear reactor</a> in the <a href="/wiki/Saratov" title="Saratov">Saratov</a> region of southern Russia due to a <a href="/wiki/Turbine" title="Turbine">turbine</a> malfunction causes widespread local panic. Local <a href="/wiki/Pharmacy" title="Pharmacy">pharmacies'</a> supplies of <a href="/wiki/Iodine" title="Iodine">iodine</a> sell out; residents flee, urging each other to drink <a href="/wiki/Vodka" title="Vodka">vodka</a> and avoid public water. <a href="/wiki/Engineer" title="Engineer">Engineers</a> at the plant find no leak of <a href="/wiki/Radiation" title="Radiation">radiation</a>. A number of people are hospitalized for iodine overdose; the government and media are criticized for poor coordination. <a class="external text" href="http://www.bellona.no/en/international/russia/envirorights/info_access/35971.html" rel="nofollow">(Bellona)</a></li>
<li>The Number 4 <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Rivno" title="Rivno">Rivno</a> <a href="/wiki/Nuclear_reactor" title="Nuclear reactor">nuclear reactor</a> of the <a href="/wiki/Ukraine" title="Ukraine">Ukraine</a> is shut down after 19 days of operation due to an oil leak. No leak of <a href="/wiki/Radiation" title="Radiation">radiation</a> is found.</li>
<li><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Spam_(electronic)" title="Spam (electronic)">Spammer</a> <a href="/wiki/Jeremy_Jaynes" title="Jeremy Jaynes">Jeremy Jaynes</a>, rated the world's eighth most-prolific spammer, is convicted of three felony charges of sending thousands of junk e-mails through servers located in <a href="/wiki/Virginia" title="Virginia">Virginia</a>, and is recommended to be sentenced to nine years' imprisonment. His sister is fined <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/USD" title="USD">$</a>7500 for related offences. <a class="external text" href="http://www.computerworld.com/governmenttopics/government/legalissues/story/0,10801,97229,00.html" rel="nofollow">(Computerworld)</a> <a class="external text" href="http://www.cbc.ca/world/story/2004/11/04/spam041104.html" rel="nofollow">(CBC)</a></li>
<li>President designate of the <a href="/wiki/European_Commission" title="European Commission">European Commission</a> <a href="/wiki/Jos%C3%A9_Manuel_Barroso" title="José Manuel Barroso">José Manuel Barroso</a> announces that <a href="/wiki/Franco_Frattini" title="Franco Frattini">Franco Frattini</a> from Italy and <a href="/wiki/Andris_Piebalgs" title="Andris Piebalgs">Andris Piebalgs</a> from <a href="/wiki/Latvia" title="Latvia">Latvia</a> will complete his commission.</li>
<li>Russian President <a href="/wiki/Vladimir_Putin" title="Vladimir Putin">Vladimir Putin</a> signs a bill approving parliament's ratification of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Kyoto_protocol" title="Kyoto protocol">Kyoto protocol</a> bringing the number of countries bound by the treaty to 126. <a class="external text" href="http://www.reuters.co.uk/newsPackageArticle.jhtml?type=worldNews&amp;storyID=615771&amp;section=news" rel="nofollow">(Reuters)</a></li>
<li>The <a href="/wiki/Israel" title="Israel">Israeli</a> senior commander in the <a href="/wiki/Gaza_Strip" title="Gaza Strip">Gaza Strip</a>, Brig. Gen. <a href="/wiki/Shmuel_Zakai" title="Shmuel Zakai">Shmuel Zakai</a>, resigns amid allegations of telling the press Prime Minister <a href="/wiki/Ariel_Sharon" title="Ariel Sharon">Ariel Sharon</a> ordered to increase <a href="/wiki/Operation_Days_of_Penitence" title="Operation Days of Penitence">Operation Days of Penitence</a> on Day 14 while the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Israeli_Defence_Force" title="Israeli Defence Force">army</a> considered the operation extracted itself. <a class="external text" href="http://news.bbc.co.uk/1/hi/world/middle_east/3982895.stm" rel="nofollow">(BBC)</a></li>
<li><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Conflict_in_Iraq" title="Conflict in Iraq">Conflict in Iraq</a>:
<ul>
<li>The <a href="/wiki/Non-governmental_organization" title="Non-governmental organization">NGO</a> aid agency <a href="/wiki/M%C3%A9decins_Sans_Fronti%C3%A8res" title="Médecins Sans Frontières">Médecins Sans Frontières</a> ends work in <a href="/wiki/Iraq" title="Iraq">Iraq</a> due to the "escalating violence" and "the warring parties have repeatedly shown their disrespect for independent humanitarian assistance." <a class="external text" href="http://news.bbc.co.uk/1/hi/world/middle_east/3982689.stm" rel="nofollow">(BBC)</a></li>
<li>A suicide <a href="/wiki/Car_bomb" title="Car bomb">car bomb</a> and <a href="/wiki/Mortar_(weapon)" title="Mortar (weapon)">mortar</a> fire kills three <a href="/wiki/Black_Watch" title="Black Watch">Black Watch</a>(<a href="/wiki/Scotland" title="Scotland">Scottish</a>) soldiers and an Iraqi translator south of <a href="/wiki/Baghdad" title="Baghdad">Baghdad</a> at <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Camp_Dogwood&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Camp Dogwood (page does not exist)">Camp Dogwood</a>. <a class="external text" href="http://news.bbc.co.uk/1/hi/uk/3983443.stm" rel="nofollow">(BBC)</a></li>
</ul>
</li>
<li>The United States recognizes the <a href="/wiki/Republic_of_Macedonia" title="Republic of Macedonia">Republic of Macedonia</a> under its constitutional name rather than the name "former Yugoslav Republic of Macedonia" used by the United Nations, the first major foreign policy move by the re-elected <a href="/wiki/George_W._Bush" title="George W. Bush">Bush administration</a>. The move outrages Greece, who had the <a href="/wiki/European_Union" title="European Union">European Union</a>'s support in lobbying against recognition since Macedonia's independence in 1991. <a class="external text" href="http://www.reuters.com/newsArticle.jhtml?type=worldNews&amp;storyID=6717491" rel="nofollow">(Reuters)</a> <a class="external text" href="http://news.bbc.co.uk/1/hi/world/europe/3981499.stm" rel="nofollow">(BBC)</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Elizabeth_Edwards" title="Elizabeth Edwards">Elizabeth Edwards</a>, wife of former <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/United_States_Democratic_Party" title="United States Democratic Party">Democratic</a> <a href="/wiki/Vice_President_of_the_United_States" title="Vice President of the United States">vice presidential</a> candidate <a href="/wiki/John_Edwards" title="John Edwards">John Edwards</a>, announces that she has <a href="/wiki/Breast_cancer" title="Breast cancer">breast cancer</a>.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Yasser_Arafat" title="Yasser Arafat">Yasser Arafat</a>, who is on a <a href="/wiki/Life_support" title="Life support">life-support</a> machine, has been officially declared <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Brain-dead" title="Brain-dead">brain-dead</a> while in intensive care at a hospital in Paris, according to medical sources inside the hospital. <a class="external text" href="http://seattletimes.nwsource.com/html/nationworld/2002081775_arafat04.html" rel="nofollow">(Seattle Times)</a> <a class="external text" href="http://news.bbc.co.uk/2/hi/middle_east/3980903.stm" rel="nofollow">(BBC)</a></li>
<li>The High Court in the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Republic_of_China" title="Republic of China">Republic of China</a> rejects a petition by the <a href="/wiki/Kuomintang" title="Kuomintang">Kuomintang</a> to nullify the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/ROC_presidential_election,_2004" title="ROC presidential election, 2004">March 2004 presidential election result</a> that saw <a href="/wiki/Chen_Shui-bian" title="Chen Shui-bian">Chen Shui-bian</a> re-elected <a href="/wiki/President_of_the_Republic_of_China" title="President of the Republic of China">president</a> by a margin of 0.2% over <a href="/wiki/Lien_Chan" title="Lien Chan">Lien Chan</a>. The KMT plans to appeal to the Supreme Court. <a class="external text" href="http://news.bbc.co.uk/2/hi/asia-pacific/3981259.stm" rel="nofollow">(BBC)</a></li>
<li>Researchers of <a href="/wiki/Diabetes_mellitus_type_2" title="Diabetes mellitus type 2">Type 2 diabetes</a> at a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Winnipeg,_Manitoba" title="Winnipeg, Manitoba">Winnipeg</a> laboratory announce that they have isolated a previously hypothetical second substance, called <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Hepatic_insulin_sensitizing_substance&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Hepatic insulin sensitizing substance (page does not exist)">hepatic insulin sensitizing substance</a> or HISS, that participates in sugar storage along with <a href="/wiki/Insulin" title="Insulin">insulin</a>. <a class="external text" href="http://www.theglobeandmail.com/servlet/story/RTGAM.20041103.wdiab1103/BNStory/specialScienceandHealth/" rel="nofollow">(Globe and Mail)</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Same-sex_marriage_in_Canada" title="Same-sex marriage in Canada">Same-sex marriage in Canada</a>: Two lesbian couples denied marriage licences file a lawsuit against the governments of Canada and of <a href="/wiki/Newfoundland_and_Labrador" title="Newfoundland and Labrador">Newfoundland and Labrador</a>, asking for the legalization of <a href="/wiki/Same-sex_marriage_in_Newfoundland_and_Labrador" title="Same-sex marriage in Newfoundland and Labrador">same-sex marriage in that province</a>. <a class="external text" href="http://www.365gay.com/newscon04/11/110404canMarr.htm" rel="nofollow">(365Gay)</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Olympic_Games" title="Olympic Games">Olympic</a> gold medalist <a href="/wiki/Michael_Phelps" title="Michael Phelps">Michael Phelps</a> arrested and charged with driving under the influence. <a href="/wiki/Maryland" title="Maryland">Maryland</a> State Police say Phelps was stopped around 11:30 Thursday night, near the intersection of Route 13 and Bateman Street in <a href="/wiki/Salisbury,_Maryland" title="Salisbury, Maryland">Salisbury</a>, after a trooper spotted an <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/SUV" title="SUV">SUV</a> that failed to stop at a stop sign. Beside the charge of driving under the influence, Phelps was also charged with driving while impaired by alcohol, violation of a license restriction, and failure to obey a traffic control device. <a class="external text" href="http://wbal.com/stories/templates/news.asp?articleid=24737" rel="nofollow">(WBAL Radio)</a></li>
</ul>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="November_5.2C_2004_.28Friday.29">November 5, 2004 (Friday)</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Portal:Current_events/November_2004&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: November 5, 2004 (Friday)">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<ul>
<li><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Israeli-Palestinian_Conflict" title="Israeli-Palestinian Conflict">Israeli-Palestinian Conflict</a>: Two <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Palestinian_people" title="Palestinian people">Palestinian</a> children are killed by an explosion in the <a href="/wiki/Refugee_camp" title="Refugee camp">refugee camp</a> of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Khan_Yonis" title="Khan Yonis">Khan Yonis</a> in the <a href="/wiki/Gaza_Strip" title="Gaza Strip">Gaza Strip</a>. Hospital officials say it was from a tank shell that hit a house. <a href="/wiki/Israel" title="Israel">Israeli</a> spokesmen said there had been no army fire in the area. They believe it was either caused when a Palestinian <a href="/wiki/Mortar_(weapon)" title="Mortar (weapon)">mortar</a> misfired or by the detonation of a roadside bomb. <a class="external text" href="http://reuters.com/newsArticle.jhtml?type=worldNews&amp;storyID=6725339&amp;section=news" rel="nofollow">(Reuters)</a></li>
<li><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Conflict_in_Iraq" title="Conflict in Iraq">Conflict in Iraq</a>:
<ul>
<li><a href="/wiki/United_Nations" title="United Nations">United Nations</a> Secretary General <a href="/wiki/Kofi_Annan" title="Kofi Annan">Kofi Annan</a> warns that an assault on <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Falluja" title="Falluja">Falluja</a> may result in a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Sunni" title="Sunni">Sunni</a> Muslim boycott of January elections. British ambassador to <a href="/wiki/Iraq" title="Iraq">Iraq</a> Jones Parry states: "You can't have an area the size of Falluja operating as a base for <a href="/wiki/Terrorism" title="Terrorism">terrorism</a>." Iraqi Interim Prime Minister Iyad Allawi describes Annan's letter as confused and unclear. <a class="external text" href="http://reuters.com/newsArticle.jhtml?type=worldNews&amp;storyID=6731678&amp;section=news" rel="nofollow">(Reuters)</a></li>
<li>Two U.S. soldiers are killed and five wounded when fighting breaks out near a base on the outskirts of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Falluja" title="Falluja">Falluja</a>. After weeks of intensive <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Airstrikes" title="Airstrikes">airstrikes</a>, U.S. and <a href="/wiki/Iraq" title="Iraq">Iraqi</a> troops seal off all roads to the city. They drop leaflets and play loudspeaker messages encouraging all civilians to leave, but say they would arrest any men under 45. Near <a href="/wiki/Baghdad" title="Baghdad">Baghdad</a>, two children are killed when a <a href="/wiki/Mortar_(weapon)" title="Mortar (weapon)">mortar</a> shell lands near a police station. <a class="external text" href="http://reuters.com/newsArticle.jhtml?type=topNews&amp;storyID=6731581&amp;section=news" rel="nofollow">(Reuters)</a><a class="external text" href="http://news.bbc.co.uk/1/hi/world/middle_east/3985493.stm" rel="nofollow">(BBC)</a></li>
</ul>
</li>
<li>Dutch–Moroccan Muslim <a href="/wiki/Mohammed_Bouyeri" title="Mohammed Bouyeri">Mohammed Bouyeri</a>, identified by the Dutch media as "Mohammed B.", is to be charged for murdering filmmaker <a href="/wiki/Theo_van_Gogh_(film_director)" title="Theo van Gogh (film director)">Theo van Gogh</a> and for being a member of a group with "<a href="/wiki/Terrorism" title="Terrorism">terrorist</a> intentions". <a class="external text" href="http://www.reuters.com/newsArticle.jhtml;jsessionid=G5EKT0PFITMBICRBAEKSFFA?type=worldNews&amp;storyID=6731257&amp;section=news" rel="nofollow">(Reuters)</a></li>
<li><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Illness_of_Yasser_Arafat" title="Illness of Yasser Arafat">Illness of Yasser Arafat</a>: <a href="/wiki/Israel" title="Israel">Israel</a> refuses to allow <a href="/wiki/Yasser_Arafat" title="Yasser Arafat">Yasser Arafat</a> to be buried in <a href="/wiki/Jerusalem" title="Jerusalem">Jerusalem</a>. The ailing leader of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Palestinian_Authority" title="Palestinian Authority">Palestinian Authority</a> is still in a <a href="/wiki/Coma" title="Coma">coma</a>, which might be reversible; an aide rejects reports that Arafat is "<a href="/wiki/Brain_death" title="Brain death">brain dead</a>". <a href="/wiki/Palestinians" title="Palestinians">Palestinians</a> claim they will only trust a successor who is "determined and steadfast on the fundamental Palestinian rights", some say who is less willing to <a href="/wiki/Compromise" title="Compromise">compromise</a>. <a class="external text" href="http://www.reuters.com/newsArticle.jhtml;jsessionid=G5EKT0PFITMBICRBAEKSFFA?type=worldNews&amp;storyID=6730716&amp;section=news" rel="nofollow">(Reuters)</a></li>
<li>Voters in the <a href="/wiki/North_East_England" title="North East England">north east</a> of England decisively reject plans for a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Regional_Assemblies_in_England" title="Regional Assemblies in England">devolved assembly for the region</a>. With a turnout of 47.8% 197,310 vote for and 696,519 vote against the plans. It is a serious setback for the British <a href="/wiki/Deputy_Prime_Minister_of_the_United_Kingdom" title="Deputy Prime Minister of the United Kingdom">Deputy Prime Minister</a>, <a href="/wiki/John_Prescott" title="John Prescott">John Prescott</a>, who had championed the plans. <a class="external text" href="http://news.bbc.co.uk/1/hi/uk_politics/3984387.stm" rel="nofollow">(BBC)</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Same-sex_marriage_in_Canada" title="Same-sex marriage in Canada">Same-sex marriage in Canada</a>: A judge in <a href="/wiki/Saskatchewan" title="Saskatchewan">Saskatchewan</a> rules that same-sex couples must enjoy the right to <a href="/wiki/Same-sex_marriage_in_Saskatchewan" title="Same-sex marriage in Saskatchewan">equal marriage in that province</a>. <a class="external text" href="http://www.cbc.ca/canada/story/2004/11/05/same-sex_marriage_041105.html" rel="nofollow">(CBC)</a></li>
<li><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Episcopal_Church_in_the_United_States_of_America" title="Episcopal Church in the United States of America">Episcopal Church</a>: The Annual Convention of the Episcopal <a href="/wiki/Diocese" title="Diocese">Diocese</a> of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Pittsburgh,_Pennsylvania" title="Pittsburgh, Pennsylvania">Pittsburgh</a> approves an amendment to its Constitution which allows it to differ with the opinion of the national church on issues which the diocese believes to be "contrary to the historic faith and order" of the church. <a class="external text" href="http://www.pgh.anglican.org/templates/cla15bl/details.asp?id=25239&amp;PID=196046&amp;mast=" rel="nofollow">(Diocese of Pittsburgh)</a></li>
</ul>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="November_6.2C_2004_.28Saturday.29">November 6, 2004 (Saturday)</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Portal:Current_events/November_2004&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: November 6, 2004 (Saturday)">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<ul>
<li>Talks between <a href="/wiki/Iran" title="Iran">Iran</a> and three <a href="/wiki/European_Union" title="European Union">European Union</a> members, France, Germany, and the United Kingdom, on the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Iran%27s_nuclear_program" title="Iran's nuclear program">Iranian nuclear program</a> end without an agreement and no further meetings planned. Iran has offered a six-month suspension of its <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Uranium_enrichment" title="Uranium enrichment">uranium enrichment</a> program. The European Union seeks an indefinite halt to the program. The issue is expected to be referred to the <a href="/wiki/United_Nations_Security_Council" title="United Nations Security Council">United Nations Security Council</a> at the November 25 meeting of the <a href="/wiki/International_Atomic_Energy_Agency" title="International Atomic Energy Agency">International Atomic Energy Agency</a>. <a class="external text" href="http://www.reuters.com/newsArticle.jhtml?type=worldNews&amp;storyID=6735025&amp;section=news" rel="nofollow">(Reuters)</a> Others report, however, that a preliminary agreement has been reached. <a class="external text" href="http://hosted.ap.org/dynamic/stories/I/IRAN_NUCLEAR?SITE=UTSGS&amp;SECTION=HOME&amp;TEMPLATE=DEFAULT" rel="nofollow">(AP)</a> <a class="external text" href="http://news.bbc.co.uk/1/hi/world/middle_east/3989407.stm" rel="nofollow">(BBC)</a></li>
<li>An <a href="/wiki/Ufton_Nervet_rail_crash" title="Ufton Nervet rail crash">express train has collided</a> with a stationary car near the village of <a href="/wiki/Ufton_Nervet" title="Ufton Nervet">Ufton Nervet</a>, England. It is thought that nine carriages of the 17:35 <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/First_Great_Western" title="First Great Western">First Great Western</a> service between <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Paddington_Station" title="Paddington Station">London Paddington</a> and <a href="/wiki/Plymouth" title="Plymouth">Plymouth</a> have been derailed. Six people have reportedly been killed, with around 150 more injured. <a class="external text" href="http://news.bbc.co.uk/1/hi/uk/3989277.stm" rel="nofollow">(BBC)</a></li>
<li>An Indian spokesman says the <a href="/wiki/Indian_Army" title="Indian Army">Indian Army</a> has been conducting <a href="/wiki/Counter-insurgency" title="Counter-insurgency">counter-insurgency</a> operations on the border of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Burma" title="Burma">Burma</a>. Two Indian soldiers and 13 rebels have been killed so far. <a class="external text" href="http://news.bbc.co.uk/1/hi/world/south_asia/3987897.stm" rel="nofollow">(BBC)</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Chile" title="Chile">Chilean</a> army commander General <a href="/wiki/Juan_Emilio_Cheyre" title="Juan Emilio Cheyre">Juan Emilio Cheyre</a> releases a statement saying abuses under <a href="/wiki/Augusto_Pinochet" title="Augusto Pinochet">Augusto Pinochet</a> were "punishable and morally unacceptable acts of the past", reversing its previous stance that they were excesses carried out by individual officers. <a class="external text" href="http://news.bbc.co.uk/1/hi/world/americas/3987341.stm" rel="nofollow">(BBC)</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/African_Union" title="African Union">African Union</a> mediators adjourn negotiations with <a href="/wiki/Sudan" title="Sudan">Sudan</a> on the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Darfur_conflict" title="Darfur conflict">Darfur conflict</a> after numerous security issues are not agreed upon, mainly a <a href="/wiki/No-fly_zone" title="No-fly zone">no-fly zone</a> in <a href="/wiki/Darfur" title="Darfur">Darfur</a>. <a class="external text" href="http://www.reuters.com/newsArticle.jhtml?type=topNews&amp;storyID=6734420&amp;pageNumber=0" rel="nofollow">(Reuters)</a><a class="external text" href="http://news.bbc.co.uk/1/hi/world/africa/3988709.stm" rel="nofollow">(BBC)</a></li>
<li><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Conflict_in_Iraq" title="Conflict in Iraq">Conflict in Iraq</a>: Three suicide <a href="/wiki/Car_bomb" title="Car bomb">car bombs</a> in <a href="/wiki/Samarra" title="Samarra">Samarra</a> kill 19 <a href="/wiki/Iraq" title="Iraq">Iraqi</a> police, two <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Iraqi_National_Guard" title="Iraqi National Guard">Iraqi National Guardsmen</a>, two <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Iraqi_Rapid_Reaction_Force&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Iraqi Rapid Reaction Force (page does not exist)">Iraqi Rapid Reaction Forces</a>, and 11 civilians, with 48 wounded. In <a href="/wiki/Ramadi" title="Ramadi">Ramadi</a>, an Iraqi is killed and 20 <a href="/wiki/United_States_Marine_Corps" title="United States Marine Corps">U.S. Marines</a> are wounded after a shoot-out between the Marines and rebels. A physician at <a href="/wiki/Fallujah" title="Fallujah">Fallujah</a> General Hospital reports two dead and maintains no foreign fighters have been admitted to his hospital. <a class="external text" href="http://www.reuters.com/newsArticle.jhtml?type=worldNews&amp;storyID=6734598" rel="nofollow">(Reuters)</a><a class="external text" href="http://news.bbc.co.uk/1/hi/world/middle_east/3987927.stm" rel="nofollow">(BBC)</a></li>
<li>Nine French <a href="/wiki/Peacekeeping" title="Peacekeeping">peacekeepers</a> and a U.S. citizen are killed in the rebel-held town of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Bouake" title="Bouake">Bouake</a> in <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/C%C3%B4te_d%27Ivoire" title="Côte d'Ivoire">Côte d'Ivoire</a> after government warplanes bomb the town to root out insurgents. In response, the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Military_of_France" title="Military of France">French military</a> launches attacks which destroy two warplanes at <a href="/wiki/Yamoussoukro" title="Yamoussoukro">Yamoussoukro</a> airport. <a class="external text" href="http://www.cnn.com/2004/WORLD/africa/11/06/ivorycoast.reut/index.html" rel="nofollow">(CNN)</a> <a class="external text" href="http://news.bbc.co.uk/1/hi/world/africa/3989127.stm" rel="nofollow">(BBC)</a></li>
<li>At an anti-nuclear waste shipment protest rally near the French town of Avricourt a protester, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Death_of_Sebastien_Briat" title="Death of Sebastien Briat">Sébastien Briat</a>, is killed after a train severs his leg. The 23-year-old French man was protesting against the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/CASTOR_(nuclear_waste)" title="CASTOR (nuclear waste)">CASTOR</a> transport. <a class="external text" href="http://news.bbc.co.uk/2/hi/europe/3990641.stm" rel="nofollow">(BBC)</a></li>
<li><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Arab-Israeli_Conflict" title="Arab-Israeli Conflict">Arab-Israeli Conflict</a>: The <a href="/wiki/Lebanon" title="Lebanon">Lebanese</a> Militant group, <a href="/wiki/Hezbollah" title="Hezbollah">Hezbollah</a>, has flown a <a href="/wiki/Reconnaissance" title="Reconnaissance">reconnaissance</a> <a href="/wiki/Unmanned_aerial_vehicle" title="Unmanned aerial vehicle">drone</a> over <a href="/wiki/Israel" title="Israel">Israeli</a> territory for the first time. <a class="external text" href="http://news.bbc.co.uk/1/hi/world/middle_east/3990773.stm" rel="nofollow">(BBC)</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Burt_Rutan" title="Burt Rutan">Burt Rutan</a> of <a href="/wiki/Scaled_Composites" title="Scaled Composites">Scaled Composites</a> is officially awarded the <a href="/wiki/Ansari_X_Prize" title="Ansari X Prize">Ansari X Prize</a> for the first privately funded space flight. <a class="external text" href="http://hosted.ap.org/dynamic/stories/P/PRIVATE_SPACESHIP?SITE=UTSGS&amp;SECTION=HOME&amp;TEMPLATE=DEFAULT" rel="nofollow">(AP)</a></li>
<li>The <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Iraq_interim_government" title="Iraq interim government">Iraq interim government</a> declares a <a href="/wiki/State_of_emergency" title="State of emergency">state of emergency</a> ahead of an expected assault on the rebel stronghold of <a href="/wiki/Fallujah" title="Fallujah">Fallujah</a>.</li>
<li><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Illness_of_Yasser_Arafat" title="Illness of Yasser Arafat">Illness of Yasser Arafat</a>: A spokesman for <a href="/wiki/Yasser_Arafat" title="Yasser Arafat">Yasser Arafat</a> claims that all the Palestinian president's vital functions are fine although it remains unclear why Arafat has not regained <a href="/wiki/Consciousness" title="Consciousness">consciousness</a> and if or when he will. <a class="external text" href="http://story.news.yahoo.com/news?tmpl=story&amp;u=/ap/20041107/ap_on_re_mi_ea/arafat&amp;cid=540&amp;ncid=716" rel="nofollow">(AP)</a> <a class="external text" href="http://www.theage.com.au/news/World/Arafat-stable-not-in-a-coma/2004/11/07/1099781228880.html?oneclick=true" rel="nofollow">(The Age)</a></li>
<li>The <a href="/wiki/Ralph_Nader" title="Ralph Nader">Ralph Nader</a>/<a href="/wiki/Peter_Camejo" title="Peter Camejo">Peter Camejo</a> campaign has filed a challenge to the voting results in <a href="/wiki/New_Hampshire" title="New Hampshire">New Hampshire</a> after receiving numerous complaints from voting rights activists. This effort is widely encouraged by Democrats and Independents due to suspected flaws related to <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Diebold_Election_Systems" title="Diebold Election Systems">Diebold Election Systems</a> voting machines. <a class="external text" href="http://portland.indymedia.org/en/2004/11/302395.shtml" rel="nofollow">(Portland Independent Media Center)</a> <a class="external text" href="http://www.nashuatelegraph.com/apps/pbcs.dll/article?AID=/20041106/NEWS02/111060040/-1/news" rel="nofollow">(Nashua Telegraph)</a></li>
</ul>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="November_8.2C_2004_.28Monday.29">November 8, 2004 (Monday)</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Portal:Current_events/November_2004&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: November 8, 2004 (Monday)">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<ul>
<li>In <a href="/wiki/Broward_County,_Florida" title="Broward County, Florida">Broward County</a>, officials find the software used in Broward can handle only 32,000 votes per precinct. After that, the system starts counting backward. The problem affected running tallies and not the final vote totals. All absentee ballots had been placed in a single precinct to be counted and only the votes for constitutional amendments reached the threshold and encountered the problem. <a class="external text" href="http://www.palmbeachpost.com/politics/content/news/epaper/2004/11/05/a29a_BROWVOTE_1105.html" rel="nofollow">(The Palm Beach Post)</a></li>
<li>In <a href="/wiki/Palm_Beach_County,_Florida" title="Palm Beach County, Florida">Palm Beach County</a>, about 88,000 more votes are recorded than voters recorded as having turned out for the election. <a class="external text" href="http://www.washingtondispatch.com/spectrum/archives/000715.html" rel="nofollow">(The Washington Dispatch)</a></li>
<li>U.S. Federal District Judge <a href="/wiki/James_Robertson_(judge)" title="James Robertson (judge)">James Robertson</a> rules that the system of tribunals set up by the United States military to try and sentence prisoners being held at <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Guantanamo_Bay_detainment_camp" title="Guantanamo Bay detainment camp">Guantanamo Bay</a> is illegal. <a class="external text" href="http://www.washingtonpost.com/wp-dyn/articles/A34519-2004Nov8.html" rel="nofollow">(Washington Post)</a> <a class="external text" href="http://www.aclu.org/SafeandFree/SafeandFree.cfm?ID=16966&amp;c=206" rel="nofollow">(ACLU)</a> <a class="external text" href="http://www.guardian.co.uk/worldlatest/story/0,1280,-4603846,00.html" rel="nofollow">(The Guardian)</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Microsoft" title="Microsoft">Microsoft</a> announces it will pay <a href="/wiki/Novell" title="Novell">Novell</a> <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/USD" title="USD">USD</a> <span class="nowrap">$536 million</span> to settle its ten-year-long <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Antitrust" title="Antitrust">antitrust</a> suit and will pay legal costs incurred by the Computer and Communications Industry Association (<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/CCIA" title="CCIA">CCIA</a>). In return, CCIA will not pursue its arguments in favor of the <a href="/wiki/European_Union" title="European Union">European Union</a>'s antitrust suit. <a class="external text" href="http://reuters.com/newsArticle.jhtml?type=businessNews&amp;storyID=6750002" rel="nofollow">(Reuters)</a></li>
<li>The <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Pitcairn_Island" title="Pitcairn Island">Pitcairn Island</a> governing council selects the first female mayor in its 214-year history after the former mayor, <a href="/wiki/Steve_Christian" title="Steve Christian">Steve Christian</a>, was <a href="/wiki/Pitcairn_sexual_assault_trial_of_2004" title="Pitcairn sexual assault trial of 2004">convicted of rape</a>. <a class="external text" href="http://news.bbc.co.uk/2/hi/asia-pacific/3991523.stm" rel="nofollow">(BBC)</a></li>
<li>The <a href="/wiki/United_States_dollar" title="United States dollar">United States dollar</a> falls to a record low of $1.2985 against the <a href="/wiki/Euro" title="Euro">euro</a>. <a class="external text" href="http://news.bbc.co.uk/2/hi/business/3991341.stm" rel="nofollow">(BBC)</a></li>
<li>China confirms that two <a href="/wiki/Hong_Kong" title="Hong Kong">Hong Kong</a> officials have been convicted and jailed for <a href="/wiki/Espionage" title="Espionage">spying</a> for the United Kingdom. <a class="external text" href="http://news.bbc.co.uk/2/hi/asia-pacific/3991845.stm" rel="nofollow">(BBC)</a></li>
<li>Intelligence services intercept <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Revolutionary_Armed_Forces_of_Colombia" title="Revolutionary Armed Forces of Colombia">FARC</a> <a href="/wiki/Guerrilla_warfare" title="Guerrilla warfare">guerrilla</a> communications calling all units to focus on assassinating Colombian President <a href="/wiki/%C3%81lvaro_Uribe" title="Álvaro Uribe">Álvaro Uribe</a>. <a class="external text" href="http://news.bbc.co.uk/2/hi/americas/3991945.stm" rel="nofollow">(BBC)</a></li>
<li>Russian troops storm a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Chechen_people" title="Chechen people">Chechen</a> rebel base and kill 22 <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Insurgent" title="Insurgent">militants</a>. <a class="external text" href="http://www.reuters.com/newsArticle.jhtml?type=worldNews&amp;storyID=6744109" rel="nofollow">(Reuters)</a></li>
<li><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Conflict_in_Iraq" title="Conflict in Iraq">Conflict in Iraq</a>:
<ul>
<li>Iraqi Prime Minister <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Iyad_Allawi" title="Iyad Allawi">Iyad Allawi</a> publicly authorizes an offensive in <a href="/wiki/Fallujah" title="Fallujah">Fallujah</a> and <a href="/wiki/Ramadi" title="Ramadi">Ramadi</a> to "liberate the people" and "clean Falluja of <a href="/wiki/Terrorism" title="Terrorism">terrorists</a>". U.S. and Iraqi forces advance. A hospital doctor in Falluja reports 15 people killed and 20 wounded. <a class="external text" href="http://www.reuters.com/newsArticle.jhtml?type=worldNews&amp;storyID=6750224" rel="nofollow">(Reuters)</a><a class="external text" href="http://news.bbc.co.uk/1/hi/world/middle_east/3992263.stm" rel="nofollow">(BBC)</a></li>
<li>In <a href="/wiki/Baghdad" title="Baghdad">Baghdad</a>, three Iraqis are killed when a suicide <a href="/wiki/Car_bomb" title="Car bomb">car bomb</a> explodes near a U.S. convoy. A U.K. soldier is killed by a roadside bomb near <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Camp_Dogwood&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Camp Dogwood (page does not exist)">Camp Dogwood</a>. A U.S. soldier is killed when gunmen open fire on a military patrol. At least three people are killed and 40 others injured in explosions at two Christian churches. <a class="external text" href="http://www.reuters.com/newsArticle.jhtml?type=worldNews&amp;storyID=6750224&amp;pageNumber=2" rel="nofollow">(Reuters)</a><a class="external text" href="http://news.bbc.co.uk/1/hi/world/middle_east/3992263.stm" rel="nofollow">(BBC)</a></li>
</ul>
</li>
<li><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Illness_of_Yasser_Arafat" title="Illness of Yasser Arafat">Illness of Yasser Arafat</a>: Officials of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Palestinian_Authority" title="Palestinian Authority">Palestinian Authority</a> travel to France to see <a href="/wiki/Yasser_Arafat" title="Yasser Arafat">Yasser Arafat</a>. <a href="/wiki/Suha_Arafat" title="Suha Arafat">Suha Arafat</a>, wife of Yasser Arafat, says, "They are trying to bury Abu Ammar (Arafat) alive". <a href="/wiki/Israel" title="Israel">Israeli</a> security officials believe Arafat is brain-dead or comatose, and is on <a href="/wiki/Life_support" title="Life support">life support</a> equipment and will be disconnected on Tuesday, the Muslim holiday of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Lailat-ul-Qadr" title="Lailat-ul-Qadr">Lailat-ul-Qadr</a> so that he will be declared dead on that day. <a class="external text" href="http://www.reuters.com/newsArticle.jhtml?type=worldNews&amp;storyID=6744501&amp;pageNumber=1" rel="nofollow">(Reuters)</a></li>
<li>A 5.8 <a href="/wiki/Richter_magnitude_scale" title="Richter magnitude scale">magnitude</a> <a href="/wiki/Earthquake" title="Earthquake">earthquake</a> rocks northern Japan. It was centered close to the Earth's surface in the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Chuetsu" title="Chuetsu">Chuetsu</a> area of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Niigata_prefecture" title="Niigata prefecture">Niigata prefecture</a>. <a class="external text" href="http://edition.cnn.com/2004/WORLD/asiapcf/11/07/new.japan.quake.ap/" rel="nofollow">(CNN)</a></li>
<li>A Muslim school in <a href="/wiki/Eindhoven" title="Eindhoven">Eindhoven</a> in the Netherlands suffers a <a href="/wiki/Improvised_explosive_device" title="Improvised explosive device">bomb</a> attack. It is believed to be a revenge attack in retaliation for the murder of <a href="/wiki/Theo_van_Gogh_(film_director)" title="Theo van Gogh (film director)">Theo van Gogh</a>, following a weekend in which several <a href="/wiki/Mosque" title="Mosque">mosques</a> were attacked throughout the Netherlands. <a class="external text" href="http://news.bbc.co.uk/1/hi/world/europe/3991547.stm" rel="nofollow">(BBC)</a></li>
<li>The current wave of violence in <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/C%C3%B4te_d%27Ivoire" title="Côte d'Ivoire">Côte d'Ivoire</a> causes London markets to fear a lack of <a href="/wiki/Cocoa_bean" title="Cocoa bean">cocoa</a> exports, sending cocoa to a five-year high. French forces, including tanks, deploy throughout the Ivorian capital, <a href="/wiki/Abidjan" title="Abidjan">Abidjan</a>, to restore order. <a class="external text" href="http://news.bbc.co.uk/1/hi/world/africa/3991241.stm" rel="nofollow">(BBC)</a></li>
<li>An <a href="/wiki/Electronic_voting" title="Electronic voting">electronic voting</a> machine in 1B in <a href="/wiki/Franklin_County,_Ohio" title="Franklin County, Ohio">Franklin County, Ohio</a>, recorded 260 votes for <a href="/wiki/John_Kerry" title="John Kerry">John Kerry</a> and 4258 votes for <a href="/wiki/George_W._Bush" title="George W. Bush">George W. Bush</a> though only 638 people voted there, one of several alleged problems. <a class="external text" href="http://www.idg.se/ArticlePages/200411/06/20041106110334_IDG.se/20041106110334_IDG.se.dbp.asp" rel="nofollow">(IDG)</a> <a class="external text" href="http://asia.cnet.com/news/security/0,39037064,39200322,00.htm" rel="nofollow">(c|net)</a> <a class="external text" href="http://www.dissidentvoice.org/Nov2004/Fitrakis1108.htm" rel="nofollow">(Dissident Voice)</a></li>
<li><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Supercomputers" title="Supercomputers">Supercomputers</a>: The <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Top_500_Supercomputers" title="Top 500 Supercomputers">Top 500 Supercomputers</a> list, which officially charts the records for the 500 fastest computers in the world, announces <a href="/wiki/IBM" title="IBM">IBM</a>'s <a href="/wiki/Blue_Gene" title="Blue Gene">Blue Gene/L</a> prototype as the world's fastest supercomputer. Using the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Linpack" title="Linpack">Linpack</a> benchmark, it achieved a record computational speed of 70.72 <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/TeraFlops" title="TeraFlops">TFlops</a>, taking the title away from Japan's <a href="/wiki/Earth_Simulator" title="Earth Simulator">Earth Simulator</a> (35.86 TFlops) which held the title since June 2002. <a href="/wiki/NASA" title="NASA">NASA</a>'s <a href="/wiki/Columbia_(supercomputer)" title="Columbia (supercomputer)">Columbia</a> takes second place with 51.87 TFlops. <a class="external text" href="http://news.bbc.co.uk/1/hi/technology/3993409.stm" rel="nofollow">(BBC)</a></li>
</ul>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="November_9.2C_2004_.28Tuesday.29">November 9, 2004 (Tuesday)</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Portal:Current_events/November_2004&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: November 9, 2004 (Tuesday)">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<ul>
<li><i><a href="/wiki/Halo_2" title="Halo 2">Halo 2</a></i>, a game for the <a href="/wiki/Xbox" title="Xbox">Xbox system</a>, exceeds more than <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/United_States_dollars" title="United States dollars">US$</a> <span class="nowrap">125 million</span> in sales on its first day of release. This makes it the biggest opening day in the <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=History_of_entertainment&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="History of entertainment (page does not exist)">history of entertainment</a>, surpassing any other games or movies. <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Microsoft_Game_Studios" title="Microsoft Game Studios">Microsoft</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Video_game_publisher" title="Video game publisher">publisher of the game</a>, estimates more than <span class="nowrap">2.4 million</span> units sold. <a class="external text" href="http://www17.tomshardware.com/game/200411131/index.html" rel="nofollow">(Tom's Hardware)</a></li>
<li><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Darfur_conflict" title="Darfur conflict">Darfur conflict</a>: The <a href="/wiki/Sudan" title="Sudan">Sudanese</a> government and <a href="/wiki/Rebellion" title="Rebellion">rebel</a> leaders sign two accords that include a <a href="/wiki/No-fly_zone" title="No-fly zone">no-fly zone</a> over <a href="/wiki/Darfur" title="Darfur">Darfur</a>, disarming <a href="/wiki/Janjaweed" title="Janjaweed">Janjaweed</a> militia and informing the location of forces to cease-fire monitors. <a href="/wiki/United_Nations" title="United Nations">United Nations</a> officials arrive to investigate claims of <a href="/wiki/Genocide" title="Genocide">genocide</a>. <a class="external text" href="http://reuters.com/newsArticle.jhtml?type=worldNews&amp;storyID=6761796" rel="nofollow">(Reuters)</a><a class="external text" href="http://news.bbc.co.uk/2/hi/africa/3996859.stm" rel="nofollow">(BBC)</a></li>
<li>United States <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Attorney_General" title="Attorney General">Attorney General</a> <a href="/wiki/John_Ashcroft" title="John Ashcroft">John Ashcroft</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Secretary_of_Commerce" title="Secretary of Commerce">Secretary of Commerce</a> <a href="/wiki/Donald_Evans" title="Donald Evans">Donald Evans</a> resign. <a class="external text" href="http://reuters.com/newsArticle.jhtml?type=topNews&amp;storyID=6763917" rel="nofollow">(Reuters)</a></li>
<li><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Conflict_in_Iraq" title="Conflict in Iraq">Conflict in Iraq</a>: U.S. troops reach the center of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Falluja" title="Falluja">Falluja</a> with heavy fighting reported throughout the city. <a href="/wiki/The_Pentagon" title="The Pentagon">The Pentagon</a> announces 10 U.S. and two Iraqi soldiers killed in the assault. One third of prisoners captured in Falluja by Iraqi forces have been foreigners from Egypt and Syria. Residents say a U.S. <a href="/wiki/Airstrike" title="Airstrike">airstrike</a> hit a clinic killing medical staff and patients. A nine-year-old boy dies because of lack of medical assistance after he was hit by shrapnel in what parents say was a separate airstrike. The mainly <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Sunni" title="Sunni">Sunni</a> <a href="/wiki/Iraqi_Islamic_Party" title="Iraqi Islamic Party">Iraqi Islamic Party</a> withdraws from the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Iraq_Interim_Governing_Council" title="Iraq Interim Governing Council">Iraq Interim Governing Council</a>. Iraqi and U.S. forces capture a mosque in northwest Falluja that was being used as an arms depot and insurgent meeting place and the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Muslim_Clerics_Association" title="Muslim Clerics Association">Muslim Clerics Association</a> called for a <a href="/wiki/Boycott" title="Boycott">boycott</a> of the election in protest of the assault. In <a href="/wiki/Mosul" title="Mosul">Mosul</a>, two U.S. soldiers are killed when <a href="/wiki/Mortar_(weapon)" title="Mortar (weapon)">mortars</a> land in a military base. Three police stations are attacked in <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Baquba" title="Baquba">Baquba</a> with casualty reports ranging from 25 to 45 people killed. A <a href="/wiki/Car_bomb" title="Car bomb">car bomb</a> outside an <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Iraqi_National_Guard" title="Iraqi National Guard">Iraqi National Guard</a> base near <a href="/wiki/Kirkuk" title="Kirkuk">Kirkuk</a> kills three people and wounds two. In <a href="/wiki/Samarra" title="Samarra">Samarra</a>, a senior local government official is assassinated. <a class="external text" href="http://reuters.com/newsArticle.jhtml?type=topNews&amp;storyID=6764423" rel="nofollow">(Reuters)</a><a class="external text" href="http://news.bbc.co.uk/2/hi/middle_east/3994605.stm" rel="nofollow">(BBC)</a></li>
<li>The <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Belgian_Supreme_Court" title="Belgian Supreme Court">Supreme Court</a> of Belgium upholds a decision of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Court_of_Appeal" title="Court of Appeal">Court of Appeal</a> of <a href="/wiki/Ghent" title="Ghent">Ghent</a> condemning the <a href="/wiki/Vlaams_Blok" title="Vlaams Blok">Vlaams Blok</a> <a href="/wiki/Political_party" title="Political party">political party</a> for permanent incitation to <a href="/wiki/Racism" title="Racism">racism</a> and <a href="/wiki/Discrimination" title="Discrimination">discrimination</a>. The decision amounts to banning the party, one of the most popular in <a href="/wiki/Flanders" title="Flanders">Flanders</a>. <a class="external text" href="http://uk.biz.yahoo.com/041109/323/f6a5u.html" rel="nofollow">(AFP)</a><a class="external text" href="http://news.bbc.co.uk/1/hi/world/europe/3994867.stm" rel="nofollow">(BBC)</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Michael_Scheuer" title="Michael Scheuer">Michael Scheuer</a>, a senior intelligence official in the U.S. <a href="/wiki/Central_Intelligence_Agency" title="Central Intelligence Agency">CIA</a>, claims that the number of "experienced" officers assigned to the agency's <a href="/wiki/Osama_bin_Laden" title="Osama bin Laden">Osama bin Laden</a> unit is fewer than before the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/September_11,_2001_attacks" title="September 11, 2001 attacks">9/11 Attacks</a>. Scheuer claims that the most experienced have been reassigned elsewhere in the <a href="/wiki/Homeland_security" title="Homeland security">homeland security</a> apparatus or are in <a href="/wiki/Iraq" title="Iraq">Iraq</a>. <a class="external text" href="http://www.washingtonpost.com/ac2/wp-dyn/A35237-2004Nov8?language=printer" rel="nofollow">(Washington Post)</a></li>
<li><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Illness_of_Yasser_Arafat" title="Illness of Yasser Arafat">Illness of Yasser Arafat</a>:
<ul>
<li>Three unnamed senior Palestinian sources state he has died. <a href="/wiki/Nabil_Shaath" title="Nabil Shaath">Nabil Shaath</a> and <a href="/wiki/Saeb_Erekat" title="Saeb Erekat">Saeb Erekat</a> state that he is still alive. <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Tayeb_Abdel_Rahim&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Tayeb Abdel Rahim (page does not exist)">Tayeb Abdel Rahim</a> explains that Arafat has suffered a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Brain_hemorrhage" title="Brain hemorrhage">brain hemorrhage</a>. <a class="external text" href="http://www.reuters.com/newsArticle.jhtml?type=worldNews&amp;storyID=6759641&amp;section=news" rel="nofollow">(Reuters)</a><a class="external text" href="http://story.news.yahoo.com/news?tmpl=story2&amp;u=/ap/20041109/ap_on_re_mi_ea/arafat" rel="nofollow">(AP)</a></li>
<li><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Palestinian_people" title="Palestinian people">Palestinian</a> Prime Minister <a href="/wiki/Ahmed_Qurei" title="Ahmed Qurei">Ahmed Qurei</a> and Former Prime Minister <a href="/wiki/Mahmoud_Abbas" title="Mahmoud Abbas">Mahmoud Abbas</a> have visited Arafat at his bedside, and Mr. Abbas has described his condition as "very serious" <a class="external text" href="http://news.bbc.co.uk/2/hi/middle_east/3994667.stm" rel="nofollow">(BBC)</a></li>
</ul>
</li>
<li><a class="external text" href="http://www.house.gov/judiciary_democrats" rel="nofollow">House Judiciary Committee Democrats</a> request a <a href="/wiki/Government_Accountability_Office" title="Government Accountability Office">GAO</a> investigation into voting irregularities in the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/U.S._presidential_election,_2004" title="U.S. presidential election, 2004">2004 U.S. Presidential election</a>. <a class="external text" href="http://www.house.gov/judiciary_democrats/gaoinvestvote2004ltr11504.pdf" rel="nofollow">(first letter)</a> <a class="external text" href="http://www.house.gov/judiciary_democrats/gaoinvestvote2004ltr11804.pdf" rel="nofollow">(follow-up letter)</a></li>
<li><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Same-sex_marriage_in_Ireland" title="Same-sex marriage in Ireland">Same-sex marriage in Ireland</a>: An <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Irish_High_Court" title="Irish High Court">Irish High Court</a> judge rules that a lesbian couple who <a href="/wiki/Same-sex_marriage_in_Canada" title="Same-sex marriage in Canada">married in Canada</a> may proceed with their case seeking to have their marriage recognized in Ireland. <a class="external text" href="http://www.cbc.ca/world/story/2004/11/09/gaywed041109.html" rel="nofollow">(CBC)</a> <a class="external text" href="http://www.rte.ie/news/2004/1109/gay.html" rel="nofollow">(RTÉ)</a></li>
<li>The <a href="/wiki/Mozilla_Foundation" title="Mozilla Foundation">Mozilla Foundation</a> releases the first official version of its <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Open_source" title="Open source">open source</a> <a href="/wiki/Web_browser" title="Web browser">web browser</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Mozilla_Firefox" title="Mozilla Firefox">Firefox</a>. <a class="external text" href="http://www.reuters.com/newsArticle.jhtml?type=internetNews&amp;storyID=6755158" rel="nofollow">(Reuters)</a></li>
<li>Violence in <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/C%C3%B4te_d%27Ivoire" title="Côte d'Ivoire">Côte d'Ivoire</a> has left 20 dead and 600 injured and stopped <a href="/wiki/Cocoa_bean" title="Cocoa bean">cocoa</a> exports. South African President <a href="/wiki/Thabo_Mbeki" title="Thabo Mbeki">Thabo Mbeki</a> has flown to the country to help find a settlement. <a class="external text" href="http://story.news.yahoo.com/news?tmpl=story2&amp;u=/ap/20041109/ap_on_re_af/ivory_coast" rel="nofollow">(CNN)</a></li>
</ul>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="November_10.2C_2004_.28Wednesday.29">November 10, 2004 (Wednesday)</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Portal:Current_events/November_2004&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: November 10, 2004 (Wednesday)">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<ul>
<li><a href="/wiki/President_of_the_Republic_of_China" title="President of the Republic of China">President of the Republic of China</a> <a href="/wiki/Chen_Shui-bian" title="Chen Shui-bian">Chen Shui-bian</a> calls for a ban on the use of <a href="/wiki/Taiwan_and_weapons_of_mass_destruction" title="Taiwan and weapons of mass destruction">weapons of mass destruction</a> across the <a href="/wiki/Taiwan_Strait" title="Taiwan Strait">Taiwan Strait</a> and asked the People's Republic of China to do the same. <a class="external text" href="http://www.voanews.com/english/2004-11-10-voa21.cfm" rel="nofollow">(VOA)</a></li>
<li>The <a href="/wiki/Supreme_Court_of_Pakistan" title="Supreme Court of Pakistan">Supreme Court of Pakistan</a> dismisses a petition seeking the release from house arrest of nuclear scientist <a href="/wiki/Abdul_Qadeer_Khan" title="Abdul Qadeer Khan">Abdul Qadeer Khan</a> for health reasons. <a class="external text" href="http://www.voanews.com/english/2004-11-10-voa68.cfm" rel="nofollow">(VOA)</a></li>
<li><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Darfur_conflict" title="Darfur conflict">Darfur conflict</a>: <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Sudanese" title="Sudanese">Sudanese</a> Police beat people and <a href="/wiki/Tear_gas" title="Tear gas">tear gas</a> women and children at a <a href="/wiki/Refugee_camp" title="Refugee camp">refugee camp</a> <a class="external text" href="http://news.bbc.co.uk/1/hi/world/africa/3998243.stm" rel="nofollow">(BBC)</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/White_House_Counsel" title="White House Counsel">White House Counsel</a> <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Alberto_R._Gonzales" title="Alberto R. Gonzales">Alberto R. Gonzales</a> has been announced by President <a href="/wiki/George_W._Bush" title="George W. Bush">George W. Bush</a> as his nominee for <a href="/wiki/United_States_Attorney_General" title="United States Attorney General">United States Attorney General</a>, succeeding <a href="/wiki/John_Ashcroft" title="John Ashcroft">John Ashcroft</a>. <a class="external text" href="http://www.cnn.com/2004/ALLPOLITICS/11/10/bush.cabinet/index.html" rel="nofollow">(CNN)</a></li>
<li><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Conflict_in_Iraq" title="Conflict in Iraq">Conflict in Iraq</a>:
<ul>
<li>Three relatives of <a href="/wiki/Iraq" title="Iraq">Iraqi</a> <a href="/wiki/List_of_Prime_Ministers_of_Iraq" title="List of Prime Ministers of Iraq">Prime Minister</a> <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Iyad_Allawi" title="Iyad Allawi">Iyad Allawi</a> have been kidnapped. The kidnappers have demanded that the siege on <a href="/wiki/Fallujah" title="Fallujah">Fallujah</a> be lifted, or the <a href="/wiki/Hostage" title="Hostage">hostages</a> will be killed. <a class="external text" href="http://news.bbc.co.uk/2/hi/middle_east/3998681.stm" rel="nofollow">(BBC)</a></li>
