<li>The <a href="/wiki/Iraq" title="Iraq">Iraqi</a> City of <a href="/wiki/Mosul" title="Mosul">Mosul</a> has gone under curfew following a rebel strike which left four Iraqi National Guards and a Foreign contractor dead. <a class="external text" href="http://www.kasa.com/Global/story.asp?S=2546517" rel="nofollow">(Fox)</a></li>
</ul>
</li>
<li>The <a href="/wiki/First_Minister_of_Scotland" title="First Minister of Scotland">First Minister of Scotland</a>, <a href="/wiki/Jack_McConnell" title="Jack McConnell">Jack McConnell</a>, announces to the <a href="/wiki/Scottish_Parliament" title="Scottish Parliament">Scottish Parliament</a> that the Executive intends to introduce a <a href="/wiki/Smoking_ban" title="Smoking ban">law to prohibit smoking</a> in all public enclosed spaces in <a href="/wiki/Scotland" title="Scotland">Scotland</a>. Both of the ruling coalition parties, as well as the main opposition party, the <a href="/wiki/Scottish_National_Party" title="Scottish National Party">SNP</a>, are in favour and the move is likely to come into effect in spring 2006. <a class="external text" href="http://news.bbc.co.uk/1/hi/scotland/3996587.stm" rel="nofollow">(BBC)</a></li>
<li>The <a href="/wiki/Euro" title="Euro">euro</a> reaches a new record high against the <a href="/wiki/United_States_dollar" title="United States dollar">United States dollar</a>, valued at more than $1.30. Concerns over the U.S. <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Trade_deficit" title="Trade deficit">trade deficit</a>, the <span class="nowrap">$427 billion</span> <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Budget_deficit" title="Budget deficit">budget deficit</a> and <span class="nowrap">$166 billion</span> current account deficit are thought to be behind the dollar's recent losses. <a class="external text" href="http://news.bbc.co.uk/2/hi/business/3999825.stm" rel="nofollow">(BBC)</a> <a class="external text" href="http://news.bbc.co.uk/2/hi/business/3991341.stm" rel="nofollow">(BBC)</a></li>
<li>The <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Association_of_International_Educators" title="Association of International Educators">Association of International Educators</a> reports that the number of foreign graduate students in the U.S. has fallen. <a class="external text" href="http://www.expressindia.com/fullstory.php?newsid=38262" rel="nofollow">(Express India)</a> <a class="external text" href="http://www.nytimes.com/2004/11/10/education/10college.html" rel="nofollow">(New York Times)</a> <a class="external text" href="http://olympics.reuters.com/newsArticle.jhtml?type=domesticNews&amp;storyID=6766422" rel="nofollow">(Reuters)</a></li>
<li>The trial of the suspected French <a href="/wiki/Serial_killer" title="Serial killer">serial killer</a> <a href="/wiki/%C3%89mile_Louis" title="Émile Louis">Émile Louis</a> proceeds, as the <a href="/wiki/Yonne" title="Yonne">Yonne</a> <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Assize_court" title="Assize court">assize court</a> transports itself to the location where the bodies of two victims were found under Louis' indications.</li>
<li><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Illness_of_Yasser_Arafat" title="Illness of Yasser Arafat">Illness of Yasser Arafat</a>
<ul>
<li>Muslim cleric <a href="/wiki/Mufti" title="Mufti">Mufti</a> <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Taissir_Dayut_Tamimi&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Taissir Dayut Tamimi (page does not exist)">Taissir Dayut Tamimi</a>, a close personal friend of Arafat, flies to Paris to attend to Arafat's spiritual needs. Aides deny reports that Arafat will be taken off life support. <a class="external text" href="http://www.canada.com/news/world/story.html?id=b7c01530-8ac3-4e99-82ac-51bdc16ea63c" rel="nofollow">(National Post {Canada})</a> <a class="external text" href="http://news.bbc.co.uk/1/hi/world/middle_east/3998091.stm" rel="nofollow">(BBC)</a></li>
<li>The <a href="/wiki/Israel" title="Israel">Israeli</a> government agrees to allow Arafat to be buried at his compound in <a href="/wiki/Ramallah" title="Ramallah">Ramallah</a>, <a href="/wiki/West_Bank" title="West Bank">West Bank</a>. State funeral services are being planned for <a href="/wiki/Cairo" title="Cairo">Cairo</a>, Egypt followed by burial in Ramallah, if Arafat dies. <a class="external text" href="http://fr.jpost.com/servlet/Satellite?pagename=JPost/JPArticle/ShowFull&amp;cid=1099973628375" rel="nofollow">(Jerusalem Post)</a> <a class="external text" href="http://www.cnn.com/2004/WORLD/meast/11/10/arafat/index.html" rel="nofollow">(CNN)</a> <a class="external text" href="http://www.haaretz.com/hasen/spages/499854.html" rel="nofollow">(Haaretz)</a></li>
</ul>
</li>
<li>A <a href="/wiki/Netherlands" title="Netherlands">Dutch</a> police squad comes under a <a href="/wiki/Grenade" title="Grenade">grenade</a> attack, injuring three policemen, following an antiterrorist raid on a house in <a href="/wiki/The_Hague" title="The Hague">The Hague</a>. The area's airspace is closed as a precaution. Two arrests have been made.<a class="external text" href="http://news.bbc.co.uk/1/hi/world/europe/3998347.stm" rel="nofollow">(BBC)</a> <a class="external text" href="http://www.reuters.com/newsArticle.jhtml?type=worldNews&amp;storyID=6770892&amp;section=news" rel="nofollow">(Reuters)</a></li>
<li>A Muslim school in <a href="/wiki/Uden" title="Uden">Uden</a> was set on fire in another of a series of sectarian attacks on Islamic schools in the Netherlands. <a class="external text" href="http://news.bbc.co.uk/1/hi/world/europe/3998347.stm" rel="nofollow">(BBC)</a></li>
<li><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/C%C3%B4te_d%27Ivoire" title="Côte d'Ivoire">Conflict in Côte d'Ivoire</a>: Canada has decided to <a href="/wiki/Airlift" title="Airlift">airlift</a> its citizens out of the troubled <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/C%C3%B4te_d%27Ivoire" title="Côte d'Ivoire">Côte d'Ivoire</a> following a similar course of action by France and the <a href="/wiki/United_Nations" title="United Nations">United Nations</a>. Other countries such as Spain, Italy, Germany, and the United Kingdom will do so. <a class="external text" href="http://www.thestar.com/NASApp/cs/ContentServer?pagename=thestar/Layout/Article_Type1&amp;c=Article&amp;cid=1100041812966&amp;call_pageid=968332188854&amp;col=968350060724" rel="nofollow">(Toronto Star)</a> <a class="external text" href="http://news.scotsman.com/latest.cfm?id=3739674" rel="nofollow">(The Scotsman)</a></li>
<li>Reports of <b><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/2004_U.S._Election_controversies_and_irregularities" title="2004 U.S. Election controversies and irregularities">irregularities</a></b> in the votes for the <b><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/U.S._presidential_election,_2004" title="U.S. presidential election, 2004">2004 Presidential election</a></b> emerge. Reports of voting machine error and <a href="/wiki/Electoral_fraud" title="Electoral fraud">electoral fraud</a> center on <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/2004_U.S._Election_voting_controversies,_Ohio" title="2004 U.S. Election voting controversies, Ohio">Ohio</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/2004_U.S._Election_voting_controversies,_Florida" title="2004 U.S. Election voting controversies, Florida">Florida</a>.</li>
</ul>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="November_11.2C_2004_.28Thursday.29">November 11, 2004 (Thursday)</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Portal:Current_events/November_2004&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: November 11, 2004 (Thursday)">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<ul>
<li><a href="/wiki/Iris_Chang" title="Iris Chang">Iris Chang</a>, acclaimed author of <i><a href="/wiki/The_Rape_of_Nanking_(book)" title="The Rape of Nanking (book)">The Rape of Nanking</a></i>, is found dead near a freeway in <a href="/wiki/Los_Gatos,_California" title="Los Gatos, California">Los Gatos, California</a>. Authorities believe her cause of death to be a self-inflicted gunshot wound. <a class="external text" href="http://news.bbc.co.uk/2/hi/entertainment/4002289.stm" rel="nofollow">(BBC)</a> <a class="external text" href="http://www.cnn.com/2004/SHOWBIZ/books/11/11/obit.chang.ap/index.html" rel="nofollow">(CNN)</a> <a class="external text" href="http://story.news.yahoo.com/news?tmpl=story&amp;u=/ap/20041111/ap_on_re_us/obit_chang_2" rel="nofollow">(AP)</a></li>
<li><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Death_of_Yasser_Arafat" title="Death of Yasser Arafat">Death of Yasser Arafat</a>
<ul>
<li><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Saeb_Erakat" title="Saeb Erakat">Saeb Erakat</a> announces that <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Palestinian_Authority" title="Palestinian Authority">Palestinian Authority</a> leader <a href="/wiki/Yasser_Arafat" title="Yasser Arafat">Yasser Arafat</a> has died at the age of 75 at a Paris hospital. <a href="/wiki/Rawhi_Fattouh" title="Rawhi Fattouh">Rawhi Fattouh</a> becomes interim President of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Palestinian_Authority" title="Palestinian Authority">Palestinian Authority</a>. <a href="/wiki/Mahmoud_Abbas" title="Mahmoud Abbas">Mahmoud Abbas</a> leads the <a href="/wiki/Palestine_Liberation_Organization" title="Palestine Liberation Organization">Palestine Liberation Organization</a>. <a href="/wiki/Farouk_Kaddoumi" title="Farouk Kaddoumi">Farouk Kaddoumi</a>, foreign minister of the PLO, leads <a href="/wiki/Fatah" title="Fatah">Fatah</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Ahmed_Qureia" title="Ahmed Qureia">Ahmed Qureia</a> receives the security portfolio of the Palestinian Authority. <a class="external text" href="http://www.cnn.com/2004/WORLD/meast/11/10/arafat.obit/index.html" rel="nofollow">(CNN)</a> <a class="external text" href="http://story.news.yahoo.com/news?tmpl=story&amp;cid=578&amp;e=1&amp;u=/nm/20041111/ts_nm/mideast_arafat_dc" rel="nofollow">(Reuters)</a><a class="external text" href="http://news.bbc.co.uk/2/hi/middle_east/3984841.stm" rel="nofollow">(BBC)</a></li>
<li>Tributes and condolences pour in from around the world for the former <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Palestinian_people" title="Palestinian people">Palestinian</a> leader, from leaders as diverse <a href="/wiki/Jacques_Chirac" title="Jacques Chirac">Jacques Chirac</a> (France), <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Zine_al-Abidine_Ben_Ali" title="Zine al-Abidine Ben Ali">Zine al-Abidine Ben Ali</a> (Tunisia), <a href="/wiki/Pope_John_Paul_II" title="Pope John Paul II">Pope John Paul II</a> (<a href="/wiki/Vatican_City" title="Vatican City">Vatican City</a>), <a href="/wiki/Pervez_Musharraf" title="Pervez Musharraf">Pervez Musharraf</a> (Pakistan), <a href="/wiki/Bertie_Ahern" title="Bertie Ahern">Bertie Ahern</a> (Ireland), <a href="/wiki/Abdullah_Ahmad_Badawi" title="Abdullah Ahmad Badawi">Abdullah Ahmad Badawi</a> (Malaysia), <a href="/wiki/Abdullah_of_Saudi_Arabia" title="Abdullah of Saudi Arabia">Crown Prince Abdullah</a> (Saudi Arabia), and <a href="/wiki/Hosni_Mubarak" title="Hosni Mubarak">Hosni Mubarak</a> (Egypt). <a class="external text" href="http://news.bbc.co.uk/1/hi/world/middle_east/4001697.stm" rel="nofollow">(BBC)</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/George_W._Bush" title="George W. Bush">President Bush</a> says, "For the Palestinian people, we hope that the future will bring peace and the fulfillment of their aspirations for an independent, democratic Palestine that is at peace with its neighbors." <a class="external text" href="http://www.washtimes.com/world/20041111-023027-4665r.htm" rel="nofollow">(Washington Times)</a></li>
<li>Israeli Justice minister <a href="/wiki/Tommy_Lapid" title="Tommy Lapid">Tommy Lapid</a> says it is "good that the world is rid of him ... The sun is shining in the Middle East". <a class="external text" href="http://news.bbc.co.uk/1/hi/world/middle_east/4001697.stm" rel="nofollow">(BBC)</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Tunisia" title="Tunisia">Tunisia</a>, <a href="/wiki/Lebanon" title="Lebanon">Lebanon</a>, <a href="/wiki/Libya" title="Libya">Libya</a>, <a href="/wiki/Morocco" title="Morocco">Morocco</a>, <a href="/wiki/Yemen" title="Yemen">Yemen</a> and <a href="/wiki/Jordan" title="Jordan">Jordan</a> have announced three days of national mourning along with <a href="/wiki/Egypt" title="Egypt">Egypt</a>. <a class="external text" href="http://news.bbc.co.uk/1/hi/world/middle_east/4002665.stm" rel="nofollow">(BBC)</a></li>
</ul>
</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Lithuania" title="Lithuania">Lithuania</a> became the first country to approve the new <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/EU_constitution" title="EU constitution">EU constitution</a>. <a class="external text" href="http://news.bbc.co.uk/1/hi/world/europe/4002555.stm" rel="nofollow">(BBC)</a></li>
<li><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Conflict_in_Iraq" title="Conflict in Iraq">Conflict in Iraq</a>: Heavy fighting continues in <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Falluja" title="Falluja">Falluja</a>, where U.S. military officials say over 500 <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Iraqi_insurgency_(Iraq_War)" title="Iraqi insurgency (Iraq War)">insurgents</a>, 18 U.S. and five Iraqi troops had been killed. In <a href="/wiki/Baghdad" title="Baghdad">Baghdad</a>, 17 people are killed when a <a href="/wiki/Car_bomb" title="Car bomb">car bomb</a> explodes near a shopping center. <a class="external text" href="http://news.bbc.co.uk/2/hi/middle_east/4003549.stm" rel="nofollow">(BBC)</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Israel_Defense_Forces" title="Israel Defense Forces">Israel Defense Forces</a> repel an <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Al-Aqsa_Martyrs_Brigades" title="Al-Aqsa Martyrs Brigades">al-Aqsa Martyrs Brigades</a> attack on <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Netzarim_(settlement)" title="Netzarim (settlement)">Netzarim</a> in the <a href="/wiki/Gaza_Strip" title="Gaza Strip">Gaza Strip</a> killing three <a href="/wiki/Palestinians" title="Palestinians">Palestinians</a>. In <a href="/wiki/Hebron" title="Hebron">Hebron</a>, one Palestinian, among a group of 400 throwing cement bricks at Jewish cars, is killed when Israeli soldiers open fire.<a class="external text" href="http://www.reuters.com/newsArticle.jhtml;jsessionid=B2QIMXIA0YRY4CRBAEKSFFA?type=worldNews&amp;storyID=6787281&amp;section=news" rel="nofollow">(Reuters)</a></li>
<li>Israeli nuclear technician <a href="/wiki/Mordechai_Vanunu" title="Mordechai Vanunu">Mordechai Vanunu</a> is arrested, again, on suspicion of leaking classified information. <a class="external text" href="http://news.bbc.co.uk/1/hi/world/4002227.stm" rel="nofollow">(BBC)</a></li>
<li>British forces launch <a href="/wiki/Operation_Phillis" title="Operation Phillis">Operation Phillis</a>, the service-assisted evacuation of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/C%C3%B4te_d%27Ivoire" title="Côte d'Ivoire">Côte d'Ivoire</a>, in response to riots in the country. <a class="external text" href="http://www.operations.mod.uk/phillis/index.htm" rel="nofollow">(MoD)</a></li>
<li>Spain has announced that <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Photovoltaic_module" title="Photovoltaic module">solar panels</a> will be mandatory on new and renovated buildings. <a class="external text" href="http://www.timesonline.co.uk/article/0,,3-1350946,00.html" rel="nofollow">(Times)</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Global_warming" title="Global warming">Global warming</a> is accelerating rapidly in the <a href="/wiki/Arctic" title="Arctic">Arctic</a>, according to <a class="external text" href="http://www.acia.uaf.edu/" rel="nofollow">Arctic Climate Impact Assessment</a> scientists. Probable outcomes include a <span class="nowrap">1 m</span> rise in worldwide oceans by year 2100, elimination of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Habitat_(ecology)" title="Habitat (ecology)">habitat</a> for the <a href="/wiki/Polar_bear" title="Polar bear">polar bear</a>, reduction of tundra and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Migratory_bird" title="Migratory bird">migratory bird</a> habitat. <a class="external text" href="http://story.news.yahoo.com/news?tmpl=story&amp;cid=624&amp;ncid=624&amp;e=1&amp;u=/ap/20041108/ap_on_sc/arctic_warming_1" rel="nofollow">(AP)</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Alice_Munro" title="Alice Munro">Alice Munro</a> has won the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Giller_Prize" title="Giller Prize">Giller Prize</a> for her short story collection <i>Runaway</i>. It is her second Giller. <a class="external text" href="http://www.cbc.ca/arts/story/2004/11/11/gillerwin041111.html" rel="nofollow">(CBC)</a></li>
</ul>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="November_12.2C_2004_.28Friday.29">November 12, 2004 (Friday)</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Portal:Current_events/November_2004&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: November 12, 2004 (Friday)">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<ul>
<li>The <a href="/wiki/Comparative_Toxicogenomics_Database" title="Comparative Toxicogenomics Database">Comparative Toxicogenomics Database</a> is launched on the web and revolutionizes chemical-gene-disease information for research scientists.</li>
<li>Deputy director of central intelligence <a href="/wiki/John_E._McLaughlin" title="John E. McLaughlin">John E. McLaughlin</a> and some other senior officials in the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/CIA" title="CIA">CIA</a> resign amid conflict with new director <a href="/wiki/Porter_Goss" title="Porter Goss">Porter Goss</a>'s chief of staff, Patrick Murray. <a class="external text" href="http://www.washingtonpost.com/ac2/wp-dyn/A46580-2004Nov12?language=printer" rel="nofollow">(Washington Post)</a> <a class="external text" href="http://www.khaleejtimes.com/DisplayArticle.asp?xfile=data/theworld/2004/November/theworld_November311.xml&amp;section=theworld" rel="nofollow">(AFP)</a></li>
<li><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Scott_Peterson_(murderer)" title="Scott Peterson (murderer)">Scott Peterson</a> is found guilty of murder in the first degree of his wife, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Laci_Peterson" title="Laci Peterson">Laci Peterson</a>, and in the second degree of his unborn son, Connor. The penalty phase of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Trial_(law)" title="Trial (law)">trial</a> was scheduled for November 22, 2004. <a class="external text" href="http://www.cnn.com/2004/LAW/11/12/peterson.verdict/index.html" rel="nofollow">(CNN)</a></li>
<li><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Conflict_in_Iraq" title="Conflict in Iraq">Conflict in Iraq</a>: The <a href="/wiki/United_States_Armed_Forces" title="United States Armed Forces">United States Armed Forces</a> report that <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Iraqi_insurgency_(Iraq_War)" title="Iraqi insurgency (Iraq War)">insurgents</a> in <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Falluja" title="Falluja">Falluja</a>, <a href="/wiki/Iraq" title="Iraq">Iraq</a>, are trapped. Hundreds of insurgents, 18 U.S. soldiers and five members of the Iraqi security forces have been killed in four days of fighting. <a class="external text" href="http://www.reuters.com/newsArticle.jhtml?type=worldNews&amp;storyID=6796559&amp;section=news" rel="nofollow">(Reuters)</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/President_of_the_United_States" title="President of the United States">President of the United States</a> <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/George_W_Bush" title="George W Bush">George W Bush</a> states that it is possible for a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Proposals_for_a_Palestinian_state" title="Proposals for a Palestinian state">Palestinian state</a> to arise in the next four years but that it would depend greatly upon who they elect to replace <a href="/wiki/Yasser_Arafat" title="Yasser Arafat">Yasser Arafat</a>. <a class="external text" href="http://www.reuters.com/newsArticle.jhtml?type=topNews&amp;storyID=6801950" rel="nofollow">(Reuters)</a></li>
<li>Ilda Boccassini, an Italian prosecutor in the <a href="/wiki/Milan" title="Milan">Milan</a> corruption trial, asks the court to sentence <a href="/wiki/Prime_Minister_of_Italy" title="Prime Minister of Italy">Italian Prime Minister</a> <a href="/wiki/Silvio_Berlusconi" title="Silvio Berlusconi">Silvio Berlusconi</a> to eight years' imprisonment for bribing judges. <a class="external text" href="http://www.reuters.com/newsArticle.jhtml?type=worldNews&amp;storyID=6801872" rel="nofollow">(Reuters)</a></li>
<li><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Iran%27s_nuclear_program" title="Iran's nuclear program">Iran's nuclear program</a>: The <a href="/wiki/International_Atomic_Energy_Agency" title="International Atomic Energy Agency">International Atomic Energy Agency</a> delays issuing its report on Iran's nuclear activities as <a href="/wiki/Iran" title="Iran">Iran</a>, France, Germany and Britain remain deadlocked in talks aimed at freezing Iran's <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Uranium_enrichment" title="Uranium enrichment">uranium enrichment</a> program. <a class="external text" href="http://www.reuters.com/newsArticle.jhtml?type=worldNews&amp;storyID=6799535&amp;section=news" rel="nofollow">(Reuters)</a></li>
<li><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Death_of_Yasser_Arafat" title="Death of Yasser Arafat">Death of Yasser Arafat</a>
<ul>
<li><a href="/wiki/Yasser_Arafat" title="Yasser Arafat">Yasser Arafat</a>'s funeral procession is held in <a href="/wiki/Cairo" title="Cairo">Cairo</a>, Egypt. Arafat is given full military honours and his coffin is led by a horse-drawn carriage. Leaders of Muslim and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Arab" title="Arab">Arab</a> countries as well as other dignitaries attend, including <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Khaled_Meshaal" title="Khaled Meshaal">Khaled Meshaal</a>, head of <a href="/wiki/Hamas" title="Hamas">Hamas</a>, who is currently sought by <a href="/wiki/Israel" title="Israel">Israel</a>. <a class="external text" href="http://www.reuters.com/newsArticle.jhtml?type=worldNews&amp;storyID=6798182&amp;section=news" rel="nofollow">(Reuters)</a><a class="external text" href="http://news.bbc.co.uk/1/hi/world/middle_east/4005027.stm" rel="nofollow">(BBC)</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Israel" title="Israel">Israel</a> has barred the entire population of the <a href="/wiki/Gaza_Strip" title="Gaza Strip">Gaza Strip</a> from attending Yassir Arafat's funeral in <a href="/wiki/Ramallah" title="Ramallah">Ramallah</a>, and has sealed off many <a href="/wiki/West_Bank" title="West Bank">West Bank</a> towns. <a class="external text" href="http://news.bbc.co.uk/1/hi/world/middle_east/4005751.stm" rel="nofollow">(BBC)</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Ramallah" title="Ramallah">Ramallah</a> is described as in a state of "<a class="extiw" href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/chaos" title="wikt:chaos">chaos</a>" as tens of thousands of people pack the area in and around the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Muqata" title="Muqata">Muqata</a>, prior to <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Yassir_Arafat" title="Yassir Arafat">Arafat</a>'s burial. Gunmen in the crowd shot repeatedly into the air, but there is no serious violence; and plans for Arafat to <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Lying-in-state" title="Lying-in-state">lie in state</a> appear to have been dropped due to the huge crowd. He was buried in soil from <a href="/wiki/Jerusalem" title="Jerusalem">Al Quds</a>.<a class="external text" href="http://news.bbc.co.uk/1/hi/world/middle_east/4005605.stm" rel="nofollow">(BBC)</a></li>
</ul>
</li>
</ul>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="November_13.2C_2004_.28Saturday.29">November 13, 2004 (Saturday)</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Portal:Current_events/November_2004&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: November 13, 2004 (Saturday)">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<ul>
<li>US Troops are preventing a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Red_Crescent" title="Red Crescent">Red Crescent</a> aid convoy from entering the city of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Falluja" title="Falluja">Falluja</a>, reportedly for safety reasons <a class="external text" href="http://www.reuters.co.uk/newsPackageArticle.jhtml?type=worldNews&amp;storyID=620613&amp;section=news" rel="nofollow">(Reuters)</a></li>
<li><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Conflict_in_Iraq" title="Conflict in Iraq">Conflict in Iraq</a>: Hundreds of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/US_Troops" title="US Troops">US Troops</a> are diverted from <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Falluja" title="Falluja">Falluja</a> as insurgents appear to take control of the northeastern city of <a href="/wiki/Mosul" title="Mosul">Mosul</a>. <a class="external text" href="http://news.bbc.co.uk/1/hi/world/middle_east/4010549.stm" rel="nofollow">(BBC)</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Iran" title="Iran">Iran</a> is reportedly concluding a deal with the <a href="/wiki/European_Union" title="European Union">European Union</a> which would spare it from possible <a href="/wiki/United_Nations" title="United Nations">United Nations</a> sanctions over its <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Iran%27s_nuclear_program" title="Iran's nuclear program">nuclear arms programme</a>. <a class="external text" href="http://www.reuters.co.uk/newsPackageArticle.jhtml?type=worldNews&amp;storyID=620552&amp;section=news" rel="nofollow">(Reuters)</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/United_States_Secretary_of_Education" title="United States Secretary of Education">United States Secretary of Education</a> <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Rodney_Paige" title="Rodney Paige">Rod Paige</a> announces his intent to resign from his post, making him the third member of President <a href="/wiki/George_W._Bush" title="George W. Bush">George W. Bush</a>'s Cabinet to resign since his re-election. No time-table has been set for his actually leaving the post. <a href="/wiki/White_House" title="White House">White House</a> domestic policy adviser <a href="/wiki/Margaret_Spellings" title="Margaret Spellings">Margaret Spellings</a> has been suggested as his successor. <a class="external text" href="http://www.washingtonpost.com/wp-dyn/articles/A46017-2004Nov12.html" rel="nofollow">(Washington Post)</a> <a class="external text" href="http://www.reuters.com/newsArticle.jhtml?type=topNews&amp;storyID=6803222" rel="nofollow">(Reuters)</a></li>
<li>Former <a href="/wiki/Afghanistan" title="Afghanistan">Afghan</a> leader <a href="/wiki/Mohammed_Omar" title="Mohammed Omar">Mullah Mohammed Omar</a> has made a rallying call to his <a href="/wiki/Taliban" title="Taliban">Taliban</a> forces. He sent a two-page message to the <a href="/wiki/Afghan_Islamic_Press" title="Afghan Islamic Press">Afghan Islamic Press</a> agency to mark the Muslim <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Eid_ul_Fitr" title="Eid ul Fitr">Eid ul Fitr</a> festival. <a class="external text" href="http://news.bbc.co.uk/2/hi/south_asia/4007015.stm" rel="nofollow">(BBC)</a></li>
<li>A fire has badly damaged a <a href="/wiki/Mosque" title="Mosque">mosque</a> in the south-eastern village of <a href="/wiki/Helden" title="Helden">Helden</a>, Netherlands, in the latest of a series of attacks on Dutch Muslim sites. <a class="external text" href="http://news.bbc.co.uk/1/hi/world/europe/4008781.stm" rel="nofollow">(BBC)</a></li>
</ul>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="November_14.2C_2004_.28Sunday.29">November 14, 2004 (Sunday)</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Portal:Current_events/November_2004&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: November 14, 2004 (Sunday)">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<ul>
<li><a href="/wiki/Iran" title="Iran">Iran</a> has agreed to curb most of its <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Uranium_enrichment" title="Uranium enrichment">uranium enrichment</a> with three <a href="/wiki/European_Union" title="European Union">EU</a> countries, France, Germany and the UK. <a class="external text" href="http://news.bbc.co.uk/1/hi/world/middle_east/4011535.stm" rel="nofollow">(BBC)</a> <a class="external text" href="http://www.euobserver.com/?sid=9&amp;aid=17749" rel="nofollow">(EUObserver.com)</a></li>
<li>The Belgian <a href="/wiki/Political_party" title="Political party">political party</a> <a href="/wiki/Vlaams_Blok" title="Vlaams Blok">Vlaams Blok</a> changes its name to <a href="/wiki/Vlaams_Belang" title="Vlaams Belang">Vlaams Belang</a> (<i>Flemish Interest</i>) after being banned for being racist. <a class="external text" href="http://www.turkishpress.com/news.asp?ID=33683" rel="nofollow">(AFP)</a></li>
<li>The <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Basque_people" title="Basque people">Basque</a> separatist party <a href="/wiki/Batasuna" title="Batasuna">Batasuna</a> calls for talks with a view to ending armed conflict in Spain. <a class="external text" href="http://news.bbc.co.uk/2/hi/europe/4010625.stm" rel="nofollow">(BBC)</a></li>
<li>Fierce storms cause three <a href="/wiki/Shipwreck" title="Shipwreck">shipwrecks</a> off <a href="/wiki/Algiers" title="Algiers">Algiers</a>. At least one sailor has been killed and 18 are missing. <a class="external text" href="http://news.bbc.co.uk/2/hi/africa/4011255.stm" rel="nofollow">(BBC)</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Uganda" title="Uganda">Ugandan</a> President <a href="/wiki/Yoweri_Museveni" title="Yoweri Museveni">Yoweri Museveni</a> declares a week-long truce with the <a href="/wiki/Lord%27s_Resistance_Army" title="Lord's Resistance Army">Lord's Resistance Army</a> starting Monday. <a class="external text" href="http://news.bbc.co.uk/2/hi/africa/4011669.stm" rel="nofollow">(BBC)</a></li>
<li>The <a href="/wiki/BBC" title="BBC">BBC</a> based on a water test of one well claims thousands in India still face a risk of <a href="/wiki/Poison" title="Poison">poisoning</a> after the <a href="/wiki/Union_Carbide" title="Union Carbide">Union Carbide</a> <a href="/wiki/Bhopal_disaster" title="Bhopal disaster">Bhopal disaster</a> 20 years ago that killed at least 4000 people. <a class="external text" href="http://news.bbc.co.uk/2/hi/south_asia/4010511.stm" rel="nofollow">(BBC)</a></li>
<li>Kidnappers release two female relatives of Iraqi interim Prime Minister <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Iyad_Allawi" title="Iyad Allawi">Iyad Allawi</a>. <a class="external text" href="http://www.reuters.com/newsArticle.jhtml?type=worldNews&amp;storyID=6806370" rel="nofollow">(Reuters)</a></li>
<li>UK shadow arts minister <a href="/wiki/Boris_Johnson" title="Boris Johnson">Boris Johnson</a> is sacked by <a href="/wiki/Michael_Howard" title="Michael Howard">Michael Howard</a> following allegations about his private life. <a class="external text" href="http://news.bbc.co.uk/1/hi/uk_politics/4011027.stm" rel="nofollow">(BBC)</a></li>
<li>Two bodyguards of former <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Palestinian_people" title="Palestinian people">Palestinian</a> prime minister <a href="/wiki/Mahmoud_Abbas" title="Mahmoud Abbas">Mahmoud Abbas</a> (Abu Mazen) are killed as they exchange fire with masked Gunmen as Abbas pays a visit to a mourning tent for <a href="/wiki/Yasser_Arafat" title="Yasser Arafat">Yasser Arafat</a> in <a href="/wiki/Gaza_City" title="Gaza City">Gaza City</a>. <a class="external text" href="http://www.haaretz.com/hasen/spages/501473.html" rel="nofollow">(Haaretz)</a><a class="external text" href="http://news.bbc.co.uk/1/hi/world/middle_east/4011667.stm" rel="nofollow">(BBC)</a></li>
<li>Japan's trade minister <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Shoichi_Nakagawa" title="Shoichi Nakagawa">Shoichi Nakagawa</a> says he believes that a Chinese submarine, which Tokyo says intruded into Japanese waters last week, is linked to gas exploration by China in a <a href="/wiki/Senkaku_Islands" title="Senkaku Islands">remote island area</a> claimed by both countries. <a class="external text" href="http://www.voanews.com/english/2004-11-14-voa11.cfm" rel="nofollow">(VOA)</a></li>
<li><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Elections" title="Elections">Elections</a> to choose the successor to <a href="/wiki/Yasser_Arafat" title="Yasser Arafat">Yasser Arafat</a> are to be held on 9 January 2005, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Palestine_Authority" title="Palestine Authority">Palestine Authority</a> interim President <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Rawhi_Fattuh" title="Rawhi Fattuh">Rawhi Fattuh</a> announced today. <a class="external text" href="http://news.bbc.co.uk/1/hi/world/middle_east/4011065.stm" rel="nofollow">(BBC)</a></li>
<li>Groundbreaking animated/live action dramedy <a href="/wiki/Tom_Goes_to_the_Mayor" title="Tom Goes to the Mayor">Tom Goes to the Mayor</a> airs for the first time on <a href="/wiki/Adult_Swim" title="Adult Swim">Adult Swim</a> in America.</li>
<li>Researchers claim to have found the lost city of <a href="/wiki/Atlantis" title="Atlantis">Atlantis</a> on the bottom of the east Mediterranean, 80 kilometers southeast of <a href="/wiki/Cyprus" title="Cyprus">Cyprus</a>. The Cypriot government disputes the claim, saying more evidence is needed. <a class="external text" href="http://www.cnn.com/2004/WORLD/europe/11/14/cyprus.atlantis.ap/index.html" rel="nofollow">(CNN)</a></li>
</ul>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="November_15.2C_2004_.28Monday.29">November 15, 2004 (Monday)</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Portal:Current_events/November_2004&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: November 15, 2004 (Monday)">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<ul>
<li><a href="/wiki/China_and_the_United_Nations" title="China and the United Nations">China and the United Nations</a>: The <a href="/wiki/President_of_the_Republic_of_China" title="President of the Republic of China">President of the Republic of China</a> <a href="/wiki/Chen_Shui-bian" title="Chen Shui-bian">Chen Shui-bian</a> declares he will push to get the ROC included in the <a href="/wiki/United_Nations" title="United Nations">United Nations</a> under the name <i>Taiwan</i>. The People's Republic of China condemns the move as a political trick to create an <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Taiwan_independence" title="Taiwan independence">independent Taiwan</a>. <a class="external text" href="http://asia.news.yahoo.com/041115/afp/041115070644asiapacificnews.html" rel="nofollow">(Yahoo)</a> <a class="external text" href="http://abcnews.go.com/International/wireStory?id=252792" rel="nofollow">(ABC US)</a> <a class="external text" href="http://www.reuters.com/newsArticle.jhtml?type=worldNews&amp;storyID=6811416" rel="nofollow">(Reuters)</a></li>
<li>The <a href="/wiki/European_Space_Agency" title="European Space Agency">European Space Agency</a>'s <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Ion_propulsion" title="Ion propulsion">ion propulsion</a> spacecraft <a href="/wiki/SMART-1" title="SMART-1">SMART-1</a> enters into lunar orbit, 14 months after its launch. <a class="external text" href="http://www.space.com/missionlaunches/smart1_lunarorbit_041112.html" rel="nofollow">(Space.com)</a><a class="external text" href="http://www.spacedaily.com/2004/041114031722.iu2d7dbs.html" rel="nofollow">(SpaceDaily.com)</a></li>
<li>Media magnate <a href="/wiki/Conrad_Black" title="Conrad Black">Conrad Black</a> has been sued for <a href="/wiki/Fraud" title="Fraud">fraud</a> by the <a href="/wiki/U.S._Securities_and_Exchange_Commission" title="U.S. Securities and Exchange Commission">U.S. Securities and Exchange Commission</a>. <a class="external text" href="http://news.bbc.co.uk/2/hi/business/4014083.stm" rel="nofollow">(BBC)</a> <a class="external text" href="http://quote.bloomberg.com/apps/news?pid=10000006&amp;sid=ajGXWQzlt_Zs" rel="nofollow">(Bloomberg)</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Vanuatu" title="Vanuatu">Vanuatu</a>'s Council of Ministers drops its opposition to a surprise decision by Prime Minister <a href="/wiki/Serge_Vohor" title="Serge Vohor">Serge Vohor</a> to establish <a href="/wiki/Foreign_relations_of_Vanuatu" title="Foreign relations of Vanuatu">diplomatic relations</a> with the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Republic_of_China" title="Republic of China">Republic of China</a> (Taiwan). <a class="external text" href="http://www.alertnet.org/thenews/newsdesk/SYD74561.htm" rel="nofollow">(Reuters)</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/President_of_the_United_States" title="President of the United States">U.S. President</a> <a href="/wiki/George_W._Bush" title="George W. Bush">George W. Bush</a> accepts the resignation of <a href="/wiki/United_States_Secretary_of_State" title="United States Secretary of State">Secretary of State</a> <a href="/wiki/Colin_Powell" title="Colin Powell">Colin Powell</a>. He is the sixth <a href="/wiki/Cabinet_of_the_United_States" title="Cabinet of the United States">Cabinet</a> member to resign since the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/U.S._presidential_election,_2004" title="U.S. presidential election, 2004">re-election of President Bush</a>. <a class="external text" href="http://www.cnn.com/2004/ALLPOLITICS/11/15/powell/index.html" rel="nofollow">(CNN)</a> <a class="external text" href="http://news.bbc.co.uk/2/hi/americas/4013621.stm" rel="nofollow">(BBC)</a>. Other resignations today include <a href="/wiki/United_States_Secretary_of_Agriculture" title="United States Secretary of Agriculture">Agriculture Secretary</a> <a href="/wiki/Ann_Veneman" title="Ann Veneman">Ann Veneman</a> <a class="external text" href="http://www.reuters.com/newsArticle.jhtml?type=politicsNews&amp;storyID=6816327" rel="nofollow">(Reuters)</a>, <a href="/wiki/United_States_Secretary_of_Energy" title="United States Secretary of Energy">Energy Secretary</a> <a href="/wiki/Spencer_Abraham" title="Spencer Abraham">Spencer Abraham</a> <a class="external text" href="http://www.reuters.com/newsArticle.jhtml?type=politicsNews&amp;storyID=6815887" rel="nofollow">(Reuters)</a> and <a href="/wiki/United_States_Secretary_of_Education" title="United States Secretary of Education">Education Secretary</a> <a href="/wiki/Rod_Paige" title="Rod Paige">Rod Paige</a>.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Bhutan" title="Bhutan">Bhutan</a> announces a nationwide ban on <a href="/wiki/Tobacco_smoking" title="Tobacco smoking">tobacco</a> sales. <a class="external text" href="http://news.bbc.co.uk/2/hi/south_asia/4012639.stm" rel="nofollow">(BBC)</a></li>
<li>Candidate cities for the <a href="/wiki/2012_Summer_Olympics" title="2012 Summer Olympics">2012 Summer Olympics</a> (Paris, London, <a href="/wiki/Madrid" title="Madrid">Madrid</a>, Moscow, and New York City) submit 120 copies of their candidate files to the <a href="/wiki/International_Olympic_Committee" title="International Olympic Committee">International Olympic Committee</a>. The IOC will announce the winning candidate in <a href="/wiki/Singapore" title="Singapore">Singapore</a> in July 2005. <a class="external text" href="http://www.olympic.org/uk/news/olympic_news/full_story_uk.asp?id=857" rel="nofollow">(IOC)</a> <a class="external text" href="http://multimedia.olympic.org/pdf/en_report_810.pdf" rel="nofollow">(IOC – candidacy procedures (PDF))</a> <a class="external text" href="http://www.guardian.co.uk/olympics2012/story/0,14174,1351713,00.html" rel="nofollow">(Guardian)</a></li>

<ul>

<li>The <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/US_military" title="US military">US military</a> says they believe civilian casualties are low in <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Falluja" title="Falluja">Falluja</a> because so many people fled the city before the assault began, but this is disputed by some eyewitnesses. The military is still refusing to allow aid workers in and casualty figures cannot yet be confirmed. <a class="external text" href="http://news.bbc.co.uk/1/hi/world/middle_east/4012005.stm" rel="nofollow">(BBC)</a><a class="external text" href="http://www.gulf-daily-news.com/Story.asp?Article=96571&amp;Sn=WORL&amp;IssueID=27240" rel="nofollow">(Gulf Daily News)</a><a class="external text" href="http://news.yahoo.com/news?tmpl=story&amp;u=/ap/20041114/ap_on_re_mi_ea/iraq_escaping_fallujah_1" rel="nofollow">(AP)</a></li>

<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="November_16.2C_2004_.28Tuesday.29">November 16, 2004 (Tuesday)</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Portal:Current_events/November_2004&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: November 16, 2004 (Tuesday)">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<ul>
<li><a href="/wiki/The_Pentagon" title="The Pentagon">The Pentagon</a> announces that <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Secretary_of_the_Air_Force" title="Secretary of the Air Force">Secretary of the Air Force</a>, Dr. <a href="/wiki/James_G._Roche" title="James G. Roche">James G. Roche</a>, has submitted his resignation. <a class="external text" href="http://www.alertnet.org/thenews/newsdesk/WAT002189.htm" rel="nofollow">(Reuters)</a></li>
<li>French scientists at the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Institut_Pasteur" title="Institut Pasteur">Institut Pasteur</a> announce they have successfully stimulated <a href="/wiki/Antibody" title="Antibody">antibodies</a> to block <a href="/wiki/HIV" title="HIV">HIV</a> from infecting human cells <i><a href="/wiki/In_vitro" title="In vitro">in vitro</a></i>. The achievement is a significant breakthrough towards the goal of an <a href="/wiki/HIV_vaccine" title="HIV vaccine">HIV vaccine</a>. <a class="external text" href="http://www.365gay.com/newscon04/11/111604AIDS.htm" rel="nofollow">(365gay.com)</a></li>
<li>Indian military officials announce that a withdrawal of troops will begin from the Indian-administered part of <a href="/wiki/Kashmir" title="Kashmir">Kashmir</a> during <a href="/wiki/Prime_Minister_of_India" title="Prime Minister of India">Prime Minister</a> <a href="/wiki/Manmohan_Singh" title="Manmohan Singh">Manmohan Singh</a>'s first visit to the disputed, Muslim-majority region which sparked two of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Indo-Pakistani_Wars" title="Indo-Pakistani Wars">Indo-Pakistani Wars</a> and a 15-year <a href="/wiki/Separatism" title="Separatism">separatist</a> movement. <a class="external text" href="http://reuters.com/newsArticle.jhtml?type=worldNews&amp;storyID=6829475" rel="nofollow">(Reuters)</a> <a class="external text" href="http://news.bbc.co.uk/2/hi/south_asia/4015203.stm" rel="nofollow">(BBC)</a></li>
<li><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Madrid_Train_Bombing" title="Madrid Train Bombing">Madrid Train Bombing</a>: A 16-year-old <a href="/wiki/Spain" title="Spain">Spaniard</a> has been jailed for six years for his part in the bombing which killed 191. <a class="external text" href="http://news.bbc.co.uk/1/hi/world/europe/4015127.stm" rel="nofollow">(BBC)</a></li>
<li><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Conflict_in_Iraq" title="Conflict in Iraq">Conflict in Iraq</a>:
<ul>
<li>A possible <a href="/wiki/War_crime" title="War crime">war crime</a> by a <a href="/wiki/United_States_Marine_Corps" title="United States Marine Corps">U.S. Marine</a> in <a href="/wiki/Fallujah" title="Fallujah">Fallujah</a>, <a href="/wiki/Iraq" title="Iraq">Iraq</a>, is caught on film by an <a href="/wiki/NBC" title="NBC">NBC</a> camera crew. The marine shot and killed an apparently unarmed Iraqi while in a <a href="/wiki/Mosque" title="Mosque">mosque</a>. <a class="external text" href="http://www.nytimes.com/2004/11/16/international/middleeast/16marine.html" rel="nofollow">(NYT)</a> <a class="external text" href="http://abcnews.go.com/International/wireStory?id=255312" rel="nofollow">(ABC US)</a> <a class="external text" href="http://news.independent.co.uk/world/middle_east/story.jsp?story=583322" rel="nofollow">(The Independent)</a></li>
<li><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/US_troops" title="US troops">US troops</a> have launched a major assault of the northern <a href="/wiki/Iraq" title="Iraq">Iraqi</a> city of <a href="/wiki/Mosul" title="Mosul">Mosul</a> following insurgents gaining control of key sites. <a class="external text" href="http://news.bbc.co.uk/1/hi/world/middle_east/4015431.stm" rel="nofollow">(BBC)</a></li>
<li>1,052 prisoners have been captured in the US assault on <a href="/wiki/Fallujah" title="Fallujah">Fallujah</a>, approximately two dozen of whom are non-<a href="/wiki/Iraq" title="Iraq">Iraqi</a>. <a class="external text" href="http://news.independent.co.uk/world/middle_east/story.jsp?story=583322" rel="nofollow">(The Independent)</a> <a class="external text" href="http://www.news.com.au/common/story_page/0,4057,11401358%5E1702,00.html" rel="nofollow">(The Nation)</a></li>

A tape apparently showing her being shot has surfaced. <a class="external text" href="http://news.bbc.co.uk/1/hi/world/middle_east/4017515.stm" rel="nofollow">(BBC)</a></li>
</ul>

<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="November_17.2C_2004_.28Wednesday.29">November 17, 2004 (Wednesday)</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Portal:Current_events/November_2004&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: November 17, 2004 (Wednesday)">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<ul>
<li><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Conflict_in_Iraq" title="Conflict in Iraq">Conflict in Iraq</a>: U.S. officers in <a href="/wiki/Fallujah" title="Fallujah">Fallujah</a> say <a href="/wiki/United_States_Marine_Corps" title="United States Marine Corps">marines</a> are "cleaning up" remaining <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Iraqi_insurgency_(Iraq_War)" title="Iraqi insurgency (Iraq War)">insurgents</a>, as artillery and airstrikes continue. In <a href="/wiki/Baiji,_Iraq" title="Baiji, Iraq">Baiji</a>, A suicide <a href="/wiki/Car_bomb" title="Car bomb">car bomb</a> kills 15 <a href="/wiki/Iraq" title="Iraq">Iraqis</a> and wounds 22. Three <a href="/wiki/Turkic_peoples" title="Turkic peoples">Turkish</a> truck drivers are ambushed and killed in <a href="/wiki/Mosul" title="Mosul">Mosul</a>. In <a href="/wiki/Ramadi" title="Ramadi">Ramadi</a>, nine Iraqis are killed and 15 wounded when U.S. forces confront insurgents. <a class="external text" href="http://news.bbc.co.uk/2/hi/middle_east/4020921.stm" rel="nofollow">(BBC)</a> <a class="external text" href="http://reuters.com/newsArticle.jhtml?type=worldNews&amp;storyID=6843284&amp;section=news" rel="nofollow">(Reuters)</a></li>
<li>Three apparently home-made explosive devices are detonated in three <a href="/wiki/Buenos_Aires" title="Buenos Aires">Buenos Aires</a> banks in <a href="/wiki/Argentina" title="Argentina">Argentina</a>, killing a security guard and wounding a police officer. <a class="external text" href="http://news.bbc.co.uk/2/hi/americas/4019947.stm" rel="nofollow">(BBC)</a> <a class="external text" href="http://reuters.com/newsArticle.jhtml?type=worldNews&amp;storyID=6845666" rel="nofollow">(Reuters)</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Kmart" title="Kmart">Kmart</a> purchases <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Sears,_Roebuck_and_Company" title="Sears, Roebuck and Company">Sears</a> in a deal worth <span class="nowrap">$11.5 billion</span>. The <a href="/wiki/Sears_Holdings" title="Sears Holdings">combined resources of the companies</a> results in a <span class="nowrap">$55 billion</span>/year company and encompasses close to 3,500 stores. <a class="external text" href="http://www.reuters.com/financeNewsArticle.jhtml?type=bondsNews&amp;storyID=6844476" rel="nofollow">(Reuters)</a></li>
<li>The British <a href="/wiki/House_of_Lords" title="House of Lords">House of Lords</a> passes a bill to allow <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Homosexual" title="Homosexual">same-sex couples</a> to obtain <a href="/wiki/Civil_union" title="Civil union">civil partnerships</a>. This is the final legislative hurdle for the bill, which is expected to receive <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Royal_Assent" title="Royal Assent">Royal Assent</a> later in the week.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-3"><a href="#cite_note-3">[3]</a></sup></li>
<li><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Iran%27s_nuclear_program" title="Iran's nuclear program">Iran's nuclear program</a>: A spokesman for the controversial <a href="/wiki/National_Council_of_Resistance_of_Iran" title="National Council of Resistance of Iran">National Council of Resistance of Iran</a> (NCRI) states that Pakistani nuclear scientist "<a href="/wiki/Abdul_Qadeer_Khan" title="Abdul Qadeer Khan">Abdul Qadeer Khan</a> gave Iran a quantity of HEU (highly <a href="/wiki/Enriched_uranium" title="Enriched uranium">enriched uranium</a>) in 2001" and a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Nuclear_bomb" title="Nuclear bomb">nuclear bomb</a> design and that Iran "continues to enrich uranium as we speak". <a class="external text" href="http://www.reuters.com/newsArticle.jhtml?type=worldNews&amp;storyID=6844621&amp;section=news" rel="nofollow">(Reuters)</a></li>
<li><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Death_of_Yasser_Arafat" title="Death of Yasser Arafat">Death of Yasser Arafat</a>: <a href="/wiki/Le_Monde" title="Le Monde">Le Monde</a> reports that former <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Palestinian_people" title="Palestinian people">Palestinian</a> leader <a href="/wiki/Yasser_Arafat" title="Yasser Arafat">Yasser Arafat</a> suffered from <a href="/wiki/Cirrhosis" title="Cirrhosis">cirrhosis</a> before <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Death_of_Yasser_Arafat" title="Death of Yasser Arafat">dying</a>. <a class="external text" href="http://212.2.162.45/news/story.asp?j=124432500&amp;p=yz4433zx6&amp;n=124433260" rel="nofollow">(IOL, Ireland)</a></li>
<li>The U.S. <a href="/wiki/National_Institutes_of_Health" title="National Institutes of Health">National Institute of Child Health and Human Development</a> has launched the <a href="/wiki/National_Children%27s_Study" title="National Children's Study">National Children's Study</a> to follow 100,000 humans from birth to age 21 in what will be the largest-ever comprehensive study of children. <a class="external text" href="http://www.reuters.com/newsArticle.jhtml;jsessionid=LVXJEWWL0XAWICRBAE0CFFA?type=healthNews&amp;storyID=6835079" rel="nofollow">(Reuters)</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Dino_Rossi" title="Dino Rossi">Dino Rossi</a> defeats <a href="/wiki/Christine_Gregoire" title="Christine Gregoire">Christine Gregoire</a> by 261 votes in the <a href="/wiki/Washington_(state)" title="Washington (state)">Washington</a> <a href="/wiki/Washington_gubernatorial_election,_2004" title="Washington gubernatorial election, 2004">governor's race</a>, pending a state-mandated recount. It is the final undecided race of the 2004 United States election season. (Note: After the recount, <a href="/wiki/Christine_Gregoire" title="Christine Gregoire">Gregoire</a> is shown to have, in fact, won the highly contested race.)</li>
</ul>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="November_18.2C_2004_.28Thursday.29">November 18, 2004 (Thursday)</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Portal:Current_events/November_2004&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: November 18, 2004 (Thursday)">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<ul>
<li><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/2004_U.S._presidential_election_controversy" title="2004 U.S. presidential election controversy">2004 U.S. presidential election controversy</a>: According to a report called <i>The Effect of Electronic Voting Machines on Change in Support for Bush in the 2004 Florida Elections</i><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-4"><a href="#cite_note-4">[4]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/George_W._Bush" title="George W. Bush">George W. Bush</a> received between 130,000 and 260,000 faulty votes in Florida. <a class="external text" href="http://www.idg.se/ArticlePages/200411/19/20041119151145_CS/20041119151145_CS.dbp.asp" rel="nofollow">(IDG)</a> <a class="external text" href="http://www.itweek.co.uk/news/1159546" rel="nofollow">(IT Week)</a> <a class="external text" href="http://www.scoop.co.nz/mason/stories/WO0411/S00229.htm" rel="nofollow">(Scoop)</a> <a class="external text" href="http://www.vnunet.com/news/1159546" rel="nofollow">(Vunet)</a></li>
<li>In <a href="/wiki/North_Korea" title="North Korea">North Korea</a>, portraits of <a href="/wiki/Kim_Jong-il" title="Kim Jong-il">Kim Jong-il</a> vanish and the official media stops referring to him as the "Dear Leader" leading to speculation his <a href="/wiki/Cult_of_personality" title="Cult of personality">cult of personality</a> is undergoing revision or weakening. <a class="external text" href="http://www.voanews.com/english/2004-11-18-voa15.cfm" rel="nofollow">(VOA)</a> <a class="external text" href="http://www.atimes.com/atimes/Korea/FK20Dg01.html" rel="nofollow">(Asia Times)</a></li>
<li>Former Canadian <a href="/wiki/Cabinet_(government)" title="Cabinet (government)">cabinet</a> minister <a href="/wiki/Alfonso_Gagliano" title="Alfonso Gagliano">Alfonso Gagliano</a> vehemently denies he has any links with <a href="/wiki/New_York" title="New York">New York</a>'s <a href="/wiki/Bonanno_crime_family" title="Bonanno crime family">Bonanno crime family</a>, as was reported on November 17 in the <i><a href="/wiki/New_York_Daily_News" title="New York Daily News">New York Daily News</a></i>. The issue is raised by <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Leader_of_the_Opposition_(Canada)" title="Leader of the Opposition (Canada)">Opposition Leader</a> <a href="/wiki/Stephen_Harper" title="Stephen Harper">Stephen Harper</a> in the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Canadian_House_of_Commons" title="Canadian House of Commons">House of Commons</a>, where <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Canadian_Prime_Minister" title="Canadian Prime Minister">Canadian Prime Minister</a> <a href="/wiki/Paul_Martin" title="Paul Martin">Paul Martin</a> also denies knowing of any links between the <a href="/wiki/Sicily" title="Sicily">Sicilian</a>-born Gagliano and <a href="/wiki/Organized_crime" title="Organized crime">organized crime</a>. <a class="external text" href="http://story.news.yahoo.com/news?tmpl=story&amp;cid=1845&amp;ncid=1845&amp;e=5&amp;u=/cpress/20041119/ca_pr_on_na/gagliano_mob" rel="nofollow">(CP)</a></li>
<li>The UK <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/British_House_of_Commons" title="British House of Commons">House of Commons</a> invokes the <a href="/wiki/Parliament_Acts_1911_and_1949" title="Parliament Acts 1911 and 1949">Parliament Acts 1911 and 1949</a> for only the seventh time (since 1911). The Act was used to push through a bill which bans <a class="external text" href="http://news.bbc.co.uk/1/hi/uk_politics/4021627.stm" rel="nofollow">Hunting with dogs</a>. <a class="external text" href="http://news.bbc.co.uk/1/hi/uk_politics/4024171.stm" rel="nofollow">(BBC)</a></li>
<li>Former U.S. President <a href="/wiki/Bill_Clinton" title="Bill Clinton">Bill Clinton</a> opens his <a href="/wiki/Presidential_library" title="Presidential library">presidential library</a>, the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/William_J._Clinton_Presidential_Center_and_Park" title="William J. Clinton Presidential Center and Park">William J. Clinton Presidential Center and Park</a>, in <a href="/wiki/Little_Rock,_Arkansas" title="Little Rock, Arkansas">Little Rock, Arkansas</a>. Speakers include former presidents <a href="/wiki/Jimmy_Carter" title="Jimmy Carter">Jimmy Carter</a> and <a href="/wiki/George_H._W._Bush" title="George H. W. Bush">George H. W. Bush</a>, and current president <a href="/wiki/George_W._Bush" title="George W. Bush">George W. Bush</a>. <a class="external text" href="http://news.bbc.co.uk/2/hi/americas/4021201.stm" rel="nofollow">(BBC)</a></li>
<li>The <a href="/wiki/Canadian_Radio-television_and_Telecommunications_Commission" title="Canadian Radio-television and Telecommunications Commission">Canadian Radio-television and Telecommunications Commission</a> (CRTC) approves an application by the American <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/News_channel" title="News channel">news channel</a> <a href="/wiki/Fox_News" title="Fox News">Fox News</a> for a <a href="/wiki/Digital_television" title="Digital television">digital</a> <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Licence" title="Licence">licence</a>. Fox's previous exclusion from the Canadian airwaves had been criticized by some Canadians as being motivated by the network's perceived <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Conservative_bias" title="Conservative bias">conservative bias</a>. <a class="external text" href="http://www.cbc.ca/canada/story/2004/11/18/fox_crtc041118.html" rel="nofollow">(CBC)</a></li>
<li>The <a href="/wiki/European_Parliament" title="European Parliament">European Parliament</a> approves the new make-up of the <a href="/wiki/European_Commission" title="European Commission">European Commission</a>, headed by <a href="/wiki/Jos%C3%A9_Manuel_Barroso" title="José Manuel Barroso">José Manuel Barroso</a>. <a class="external text" href="http://news.xinhuanet.com/english/2004-11/18/content_2234653.htm" rel="nofollow">(Xinhua)</a> <a class="external text" href="http://www.bloomberg.com/apps/news?pid=10000085&amp;sid=ajQSXUBXhJnM&amp;refer=europe" rel="nofollow">(Bloomberg)</a></li>
<li>In <a href="/wiki/Israel" title="Israel">Israel</a>, the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Israeli_Defence_Force" title="Israeli Defence Force">Israeli Defence Force</a> (IDF), investigating alleged crimes by an Israeli <a href="/wiki/Officer_(armed_forces)" title="Officer (armed forces)">officer</a>, is seeking to exhume the body of 13-year-old <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Iman_al-Hams" title="Iman al-Hams">Iman al-Hams</a>. The schoolgirl was shot at least 15 times by the IDF. <a class="external text" href="http://news.bbc.co.uk/1/hi/world/middle_east/4022109.stm" rel="nofollow">(BBC)</a></li>
<li>The <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/U.S._Department_of_Agriculture" title="U.S. Department of Agriculture">U.S. Department of Agriculture</a> announces that a cow has tested positive for <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Mad_cow_disease" title="Mad cow disease">mad cow disease</a>. Officials caution that the test is inconclusive until confirmed at a lab in <a href="/wiki/Ames,_Iowa" title="Ames, Iowa">Ames, Iowa</a>, but if confirmed, it will be the second case in the U.S. The agency says the disease has not entered the <a href="/wiki/Food_chain" title="Food chain">food chain</a>. <a class="external text" href="http://www.technewsworld.com/story/Second-Case-of-Mad-Cow-Disease-in-US-38269.html" rel="nofollow">Tech News World</a>, <a class="external text" href="http://www.nytimes.com/2004/11/19/health/19cow.html" rel="nofollow">(NY Times)</a></li>
<li>Three <a href="/wiki/Palestinians" title="Palestinians">Palestinians</a> are buried while digging a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Smuggling_tunnels" title="Smuggling tunnels">smuggling tunnel</a> in <a href="/wiki/Rafah" title="Rafah">Rafah</a>. The tunnel collapsed due to heavy rain. The <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Israeli_Defence_Force" title="Israeli Defence Force">Israeli Defence Force</a> permitted Palestinian rescue forces to try to rescue them, and later sent its own <a href="/wiki/Bulldozer" title="Bulldozer">bulldozers</a> to help. The rescue efforts succeeded and three Palestinian were recovered from the ruins alive. They were treated by IDF medical staff and later taken to investigation. <a class="external text" href="http://www.washtimes.com/upi-breaking/20041118-112424-7560r.htm" rel="nofollow">(Washington Times)</a>, <a class="external text" href="http://www.maarivintl.com/index.cfm?fuseaction=article&amp;articleID=11723" rel="nofollow">(Maariv)</a>, <a class="external text" href="http://www.haaretz.com/hasen/spages/503376.html" rel="nofollow">(Haaretz)</a></li>
<li>Three Egyptian paramilitary security officers stationed at the <a href="/wiki/Sinai_Peninsula" title="Sinai Peninsula">Sinai</a>–<a href="/wiki/Gaza_Strip" title="Gaza Strip">Gaza</a> border are killed by <a href="/wiki/Israel" title="Israel">Israeli</a> tank fire, after <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Israeli_Defence_Force" title="Israeli Defence Force">IDF</a> troops allegedly mistook them for <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Palestinian_people" title="Palestinian people">Palestinian</a> <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Palestinian_terrorism" title="Palestinian terrorism">terrorists</a> or militants. The Egyptian government accepts an apology from Israeli Prime Minister <a href="/wiki/Ariel_Sharon" title="Ariel Sharon">Ariel Sharon</a> and demands an investigation on the incident. <a class="external text" href="http://www.haaretz.com/hasen/spages/503304.html" rel="nofollow">(Haaretz)</a> <a class="external text" href="http://story.news.yahoo.com/news?tmpl=story&amp;cid=578&amp;e=3&amp;u=/nm/20041118/ts_nm/mideast_israel_egypt_dc" rel="nofollow">(Reuters)</a> <a class="external text" href="http://news.bbc.co.uk/1/hi/world/middle_east/4021461.stm" rel="nofollow">(BBC)</a></li>
<li>The <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Parliament_of_New_Zealand" title="Parliament of New Zealand">Parliament of New Zealand</a> finally passes a controversial bill on the <a href="/wiki/New_Zealand_foreshore_and_seabed_controversy" title="New Zealand foreshore and seabed controversy">foreshore and seabed ownership dispute</a>, which has caused considerable tension between <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Maori_people" title="Maori people">Maori</a> and non-Maori. <a class="external text" href="http://tvnz.co.nz/view/news_politics_story_skin/459602?format=html" rel="nofollow">(TVNZ)</a></li>
<li>The <a href="/wiki/Great_American_Smokeout" title="Great American Smokeout">Great American Smokeout</a>, sponsored by the <a href="/wiki/American_Cancer_Society" title="American Cancer Society">American Cancer Society</a> is held for the 28th time. <a class="external text" href="http://www.newsday.com/news/health/wire/sns-ap-smokeout,0,6504425.story?coll=sns-ap-health-headlines" rel="nofollow">(Newsday)</a></li>
</ul>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="November_19.2C_2004_.28Friday.29">November 19, 2004 (Friday)</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Portal:Current_events/November_2004&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: November 19, 2004 (Friday)">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<ul>
<li>Research by the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Medical_Research_Council_(UK)" title="Medical Research Council (UK)">Medical Research Council</a> shows that the antibiotic <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Co-trimoxazole" title="Co-trimoxazole">co-trimoxazole</a> can halve the death rate in <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/HIV-positive" title="HIV-positive">HIV-positive</a> children in <a href="/wiki/Zambia" title="Zambia">Zambia</a>. <a class="external text" href="http://news.bbc.co.uk/1/hi/health/4021887.stm" rel="nofollow">(BBC)</a></li>
<li>Attempts by the United States to draft a <a href="/wiki/United_Nations" title="United Nations">U.N.</a> treaty banning <a href="/wiki/Human_cloning" title="Human cloning">human cloning</a> have been abandoned. <a class="external text" href="http://edition.cnn.com/2004/TECH/science/11/19/un.humancloning.ap/index.html" rel="nofollow">(CNN)</a></li>
<li>U.S. President <a href="/wiki/George_W._Bush" title="George W. Bush">George W. Bush</a> arrives at the <a href="/wiki/Asia-Pacific_Economic_Cooperation" title="Asia-Pacific Economic Cooperation">Asia-Pacific Economic Cooperation</a> summit in <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Santiago_de_Chile" title="Santiago de Chile">Santiago de Chile</a> for talks with China and other nations. The summit's agenda includes <a href="/wiki/Nuclear_proliferation" title="Nuclear proliferation">nuclear proliferation</a> and new <a href="/wiki/Free_trade" title="Free trade">free trade</a> agreements, particularly on agriculture. Bush hopes to revive <a href="/wiki/Six-party_talks" title="Six-party talks">six-party talks</a> on <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/North_Korea%27s_nuclear_program" title="North Korea's nuclear program">North Korea's nuclear program</a> and promote the "<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/War_on_Terrorism" title="War on Terrorism">War on Terrorism</a>". The Chinese delegation ask Bush to take "all measures necessary" to halt the slide in value of the <a href="/wiki/United_States_dollar" title="United States dollar">U.S. dollar</a>. About 40,000 people protest against the summit, Bush, the <a href="/wiki/2003_invasion_of_Iraq" title="2003 invasion of Iraq">war in Iraq</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Globalization" title="Globalization">globalization</a>; they are blocked by Chilean police with <a href="/wiki/Tear_gas" title="Tear gas">tear gas</a> and <a href="/wiki/Water_cannon" title="Water cannon">water cannon</a>. <a class="external text" href="http://www.msnbc.msn.com/id/6533636/" rel="nofollow">(MSNBC)</a> <a class="external text" href="http://www.cbc.ca/world/story/2004/11/19/apec-bush041119.html" rel="nofollow">(CBC)</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Second_Sudanese_Civil_War" title="Second Sudanese Civil War">Sudanese Civil War</a>: At a special session of the <a href="/wiki/United_Nations" title="United Nations">United Nations</a> <a href="/wiki/United_Nations_Security_Council" title="United Nations Security Council">Security Council</a> in <a href="/wiki/Nairobi" title="Nairobi">Nairobi</a>, <a href="/wiki/Kenya" title="Kenya">Kenya</a>, the government of <a href="/wiki/Sudan" title="Sudan">Sudan</a> and southern rebels sign an agreement which states that both sides will commit themselves to ending the 21-year conflict by December 31. The Council then unanimously passes a resolution which promises substantial aid to the country after the wars in the south and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Darfur_conflict" title="Darfur conflict">in the region of Darfur</a> come to an end. <a class="external text" href="http://olympics.reuters.com/newsArticle.jhtml?type=worldNews&amp;storyID=6870630" rel="nofollow">(Reuters)</a></li>
<li><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Sino-Japanese_relations" title="Sino-Japanese relations">Sino-Japanese relations</a>: <a href="/wiki/President_of_the_Republic_of_China" title="President of the Republic of China">Taiwan President</a> <a href="/wiki/Chen_Shui-bian" title="Chen Shui-bian">Chen Shui-bian</a> says information provided by his government helped Japan locate a Chinese nuclear submarine in Japanese waters a week ago. The PRC expressed "regret" after the incident. <a class="external text" href="http://www.voanews.com/english/Taiwan-Provided-Chinese-Sub-Intel-to-Japan.cfm" rel="nofollow">(VOA)</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Netherlands" title="Netherlands">Dutch</a> lawmaker <a href="/wiki/Geert_Wilders" title="Geert Wilders">Geert Wilders</a>, one of the most controversial Dutch politicians, advocates a five-year halt to non-Western <a href="/wiki/Immigration" title="Immigration">immigration</a> in the wake of the murder of <a href="/wiki/Theo_van_Gogh_(film_director)" title="Theo van Gogh (film director)">Theo van Gogh</a> stating: "The Netherlands has been too tolerant to intolerant people for too long, we should not import a retarded political Islamic society to our country". <a class="external text" href="http://www.nytimes.com/aponline/international/AP-Netherlands-Opposing-Immigration.html" rel="nofollow">(NYT)</a></li>
<li><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/2004_U.S._presidential_election_controversy" title="2004 U.S. presidential election controversy">2004 U.S. presidential election controversy</a>: A recount has begun in <a href="/wiki/New_Hampshire" title="New Hampshire">New Hampshire</a>, testing anomalous statistical discrepancies related to <a href="/wiki/Electronic_voting" title="Electronic voting">voting machine technologies</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-5"><a href="#cite_note-5">[5]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-6"><a href="#cite_note-6">[6]</a></sup></li>
<li><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Israeli-Palestinian_conflict" title="Israeli-Palestinian conflict">Israeli-Palestinian conflict</a>: The commander of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Israeli_Defense_Force" title="Israeli Defense Force">Israeli Defense Force</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Moshe_Yaalon" title="Moshe Yaalon">Moshe Yaalon</a>, orders an investigation "to reach the truth" of claims by the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Yediot_Ahronot" title="Yediot Ahronot">Yediot Ahronot</a> newspaper that IDF troops abused <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Palestinian_people" title="Palestinian people">Palestinian</a> corpses. <a class="external text" href="http://news.bbc.co.uk/2/hi/middle_east/4026859.stm" rel="nofollow">(BBC)</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/United_States_Congress" title="United States Congress">United States Congress</a>: The U.S. Congress has passed a bill reinstating and extending a ban on taxation of internet access for another three years. <a class="external text" href="http://www.reuters.com/newsArticle.jhtml;jsessionid=G0CVLL2TJ5AXUCRBAEZSFFA?type=domesticNews&amp;storyID=6871862" rel="nofollow">(Reuters)</a></li>
<li>Russia announces it will sell off the main production unit of <a href="/wiki/Yukos" title="Yukos">Yukos</a>, the energy company seized last year for supposedly failing to pay taxes. <a class="external text" href="http://news.bbc.co.uk/2/hi/business/4024607.stm" rel="nofollow">(BBC)</a></li>
<li>The U.S. <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Congress_of_the_United_States" title="Congress of the United States">U.S. Congress</a> raises the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/National_debt" title="National debt">national debt</a> ceiling by <a href="/wiki/United_States_dollar" title="United States dollar">USD</a> <span class="nowrap">800 billion</span> to a total of USD <span class="nowrap">8.18 trillion</span>. This makes the new borrowing cap 30% higher than the debt Bush inherited, and 70% of the size of the U.S. economy. <a class="external text" href="http://www.cnn.com/2004/ALLPOLITICS/11/19/congress.spending.debt.ap/index.html" rel="nofollow">(CNN)</a> <a class="external text" href="http://www.brillig.com/debt_clock/" rel="nofollow">(Debt Clock)</a></li>
<li>In <a href="/wiki/Auburn_Hills,_Michigan" title="Auburn Hills, Michigan">Auburn Hills, Michigan</a>, members of the <a href="/wiki/National_Basketball_Association" title="National Basketball Association">NBA</a> <a href="/wiki/Indiana_Pacers" title="Indiana Pacers">Indiana Pacers</a> and <a href="/wiki/Detroit_Pistons" title="Detroit Pistons">Detroit Pistons</a> engage in a brawl involving players and spectators. <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Ron_Artest" title="Ron Artest">Ron Artest</a> of the Pacers initiated the conflict with fans when he entered the crowd at <a href="/wiki/The_Palace_of_Auburn_Hills" title="The Palace of Auburn Hills">The Palace of Auburn Hills</a> after a fan threw a cup of beer at him. The game was postponed with 45 seconds remaining. Artest was suspended for the rest of the season, while several members of both teams were suspended by the league for their involvement.
<div class="hatnote" role="note">See also: <a href="/wiki/Pacers%E2%80%93Pistons_brawl" title="Pacers–Pistons brawl">Pacers–Pistons brawl</a></div>
</li>
<li><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Conflict_in_Iraq" title="Conflict in Iraq">Conflict in Iraq</a>:
<ul>
<li><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/U.S._Military" title="U.S. Military">U.S. Military</a> officials report that 102 soldiers, 85% of which are serving in <a href="/wiki/Iraq" title="Iraq">Iraq</a>, <a href="/wiki/Kuwait" title="Kuwait">Kuwait</a> and <a href="/wiki/Afghanistan" title="Afghanistan">Afghanistan</a>, have contracted a rather rare blood infection by <a href="/wiki/Acinetobacter_baumannii" title="Acinetobacter baumannii">Acinetobacter baumannii</a>. Military investigators say there is no evidence of biochemical agents in the infection which surfaces occasionally in unsanitary hospitals, but that some soldiers were arriving with infections. <a class="external text" href="http://www.cnn.com/2004/HEALTH/conditions/11/19/soldiers.blood.reut/index.html" rel="nofollow">(CNN)</a></li>
<li><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/World_Vision" title="World Vision">World Vision</a>, one of the last aid agencies left in <a href="/wiki/Iraq" title="Iraq">Iraq</a>, announces it will pull its staff out of the country following the murder of its senior manager. <a class="external text" href="http://news.bbc.co.uk/1/hi/world/middle_east/4025171.stm" rel="nofollow">(BBC)</a></li>
<li>In <a href="/wiki/Baghdad" title="Baghdad">Baghdad</a>, two people are killed when clashes break out as <a href="/wiki/Iraq" title="Iraq">Iraqi</a> forces backed by U.S. troops enter a popular <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Sunni" title="Sunni">Sunni</a> <a href="/wiki/Mosque" title="Mosque">mosque</a> to arrest dozens of members reportedly including the <a href="/wiki/Imam" title="Imam">imam</a>. <a class="external text" href="http://news.bbc.co.uk/2/hi/middle_east/4026505.stm" rel="nofollow">(BBC)</a></li>
</ul>
</li>
<li><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/The_Spongebob_Squarepants_Movie" title="The Spongebob Squarepants Movie">The Spongebob Squarepants Movie</a> debuts in movie theaters across the United States, grossing $32,018,216 during its opening weekend.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Hi_Hi_Puffy_AmiYumi" title="Hi Hi Puffy AmiYumi">Hi Hi Puffy AmiYumi</a> premieres on <a href="/wiki/Cartoon_Network" title="Cartoon Network">Cartoon Network</a> and scores the highest-ever Kids 2-11 rating and delivery and the second highest Kids 6-11 rating (4.4) and delivery (1,068,000) ever for an original series premiere.</li>
</ul>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="November_20.2C_2004_.28Saturday.29">November 20, 2004 (Saturday)</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Portal:Current_events/November_2004&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: November 20, 2004 (Saturday)">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<ul>
<li><a href="/wiki/Mar%C3%ADa_Isabel" title="María Isabel">María Isabel</a> from Spain wins the <a href="/wiki/Junior_Eurovision_Song_Contest_2004" title="Junior Eurovision Song Contest 2004">Junior Eurovision Song Contest 2004</a>. (<a class="external text" href="http://www.junioreurovision.tv" rel="nofollow">JESC</a>)</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/NASA" title="NASA">NASA</a> launches a <a href="/wiki/Satellite" title="Satellite">satellite</a>, named <a href="/wiki/Swift_Gamma-Ray_Burst_Mission" title="Swift Gamma-Ray Burst Mission"><i>Swift</i></a>, to investigate <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Gamma_ray_burst" title="Gamma ray burst">gamma ray bursts</a>. <a class="external text" href="http://news.bbc.co.uk/2/hi/science/nature/4022683.stm" rel="nofollow">(BBC)</a></li>
<li>The 25th annual <a href="/wiki/BBC" title="BBC">BBC</a> <a href="/wiki/Children_in_Need" title="Children in Need">Children in Need</a> <a href="/wiki/Telethon" title="Telethon">telethon</a> has raised over <a href="/wiki/Pound_sterling" title="Pound sterling">£</a>17 million (<span class="nowrap">£1.5 million</span> more than in 2003). <a class="external text" href="http://news.bbc.co.uk/1/hi/uk/4024795.stm" rel="nofollow">(BBC)</a></li>
<li>The <a href="/wiki/Conseil_Repr%C3%A9sentatif_des_Institutions_juives_de_France" title="Conseil Représentatif des Institutions juives de France">Conseil Représentatif des Institutions juives de France</a> (CRIF), an umbrella group of French Jewish organisations, accused the French government of failing to protect citizens from broadcasts by <a href="/wiki/Hezbollah" title="Hezbollah">Hezbollah</a>'s al-Manar TV, which includes films that CRIF claims are <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Anti-Semitic" title="Anti-Semitic">anti-Semitic</a> and incite Muslims to attack Jews. <a class="external text" href="http://www.haaretz.com/hasen/spages/503916.html" rel="nofollow">(Reuters-Haaretz)</a></li>
<li>A small <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/China_Eastern" title="China Eastern">China Eastern</a> airlines jet, a <a href="/wiki/Bombardier_Aerospace" title="Bombardier Aerospace">Bombardier</a> <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=CRJ2000&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="CRJ2000 (page does not exist)">CRJ2000</a>, crashes in <a href="/wiki/Mongolia" title="Mongolia">Mongolia</a>, causing the deaths of 53 persons. <a class="external text" href="http://edition.cnn.com/2004/WORLD/asiapcf/11/20/china.planecrash.ap/index.html" rel="nofollow">(CNN)</a></li>
<li>Indian policemen and soldiers of the <a href="/wiki/Indian_Army" title="Indian Army">Indian Army</a> recover 300 kg of <a href="/wiki/RDX" title="RDX">RDX</a> from a grocery store near the southern <a href="/wiki/Kashmir" title="Kashmir">Kashmir</a> town of <a href="/wiki/Anantnag" title="Anantnag">Anantnag</a>, 55 km from <a href="/wiki/Srinagar" title="Srinagar">Srinagar</a>. This is the biggest ever explosive haul in the state of <a href="/wiki/Jammu_and_Kashmir" title="Jammu and Kashmir">Jammu and Kashmir</a>. <a class="external text" href="http://www.hinduonnet.com/thehindu/holnus/001200411201223.htm" rel="nofollow">(The Hindu)</a> <a class="external text" href="http://www.expressindia.com/fullstory.php?newsid=38247" rel="nofollow">(Indian Express)</a></li>
<li>The <a href="/wiki/Madras_High_Court" title="Madras High Court">Madras High Court</a> in India dismisses the bail petition of <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Kanchi_Shankaracharya&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Kanchi Shankaracharya (page does not exist)">Kanchi Shankaracharya</a> <a href="/wiki/Jayendra_Saraswathi" title="Jayendra Saraswathi">Jayendra Saraswathi</a>, the prime accused in the murder of temple manager Sankararaman. <a class="external text" href="http://timesofindia.indiatimes.com/articleshow/929572.cms" rel="nofollow">(Times of India)</a></li>
</ul>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="November_21.2C_2004_.28Sunday.29">November 21, 2004 (Sunday)</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Portal:Current_events/November_2004&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: November 21, 2004 (Sunday)">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<ul>
<li><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Conflict_in_Iraq" title="Conflict in Iraq">Conflict in Iraq</a>: The nineteen member <a href="/wiki/Paris_Club" title="Paris Club">Paris Club</a> agrees to forgive 80% of nearly <span class="nowrap">$40 billion</span> in Iraqi debt, in three stages: 20% now, 30% in 2005 and 20% in 2008 in tandem with Iraq's implementation of an International Monetary Fund economic programme. <span class="nowrap">$80 billion</span> in debt to <a href="/wiki/Saudi_Arabia" title="Saudi Arabia">Saudi Arabia</a> and <a href="/wiki/Kuwait" title="Kuwait">Kuwait</a>, among others, will remain. <a class="external text" href="http://news.bbc.co.uk/1/hi/business/4029905.stm" rel="nofollow">(BBC)</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Hifikepunye_Pohamba" title="Hifikepunye Pohamba">Hifikepunye Pohamba</a>, the candidate of the ruling <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/South-West_Africa_People%27s_Organisation" title="South-West Africa People's Organisation">South-West Africa People's Organisation</a> party, is declared the winner of the <a href="/wiki/Namibia" title="Namibia">Namibian</a> <a href="/wiki/President_of_Namibia" title="President of Namibia">presidential</a> election with 76% of the vote.
