He succeeds <a href="/wiki/Sam_Nujoma" title="Sam Nujoma">Sam Nujoma</a>, who is retiring after serving as president for 15 years. <a class="external text" href="http://news.bbc.co.uk/1/hi/world/africa/4030163.stm" rel="nofollow">(BBC)</a></li>
<li><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Israeli-Palestinian_conflict" title="Israeli-Palestinian conflict">Israeli-Palestinian conflict</a>:
<ul>
<li>U.S. <a href="/wiki/United_States_Secretary_of_State" title="United States Secretary of State">Secretary of State</a> <a href="/wiki/Colin_Powell" title="Colin Powell">Colin Powell</a> arrives in <a href="/wiki/Israel" title="Israel">Israel</a> for talks with leaders of both sides of the conflict with an aim to restarting the stalled peace process. <a class="external text" href="http://news.bbc.co.uk/1/hi/world/middle_east/4030823.stm" rel="nofollow">(BBC)</a></li>
<li>Three <a href="/wiki/Fatah" title="Fatah">Fatah</a> militants are killed in a gunfight with <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/YAMAM" title="YAMAM">YAMAM</a>, an <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Israeli_Police" title="Israeli Police">Israeli Police</a> <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Counterterrorist" title="Counterterrorist">counterterrorist</a> unit. Among those killed is <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Mohammed_Rassan_Sheikh&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Mohammed Rassan Sheikh (page does not exist)">Mohammed Rassan Sheikh</a>, who hid in <a href="/wiki/Mukataa" title="Mukataa">Arafat's compound</a>. One Israeli police officer sustained light injuries.<a class="external text" href="http://www.haaretz.com/hasen/spages/504306.html" rel="nofollow">(Haaretz)</a></li>
<li>In the <a href="/wiki/Gaza_Strip" title="Gaza Strip">Gaza Strip</a>, the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Israeli_Defence_Forces" title="Israeli Defence Forces">IDF</a> foils an attack on Kissufim road to <a href="/wiki/Gush_Katif" title="Gush Katif">Gush Katif</a>, killing two militants. <a class="external text" href="http://www.haaretz.com/hasen/spages/504306.html" rel="nofollow">(Haaretz)</a></li>
</ul>
</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Ukraine" title="Ukraine">Ukraine</a> holds the second vote in a <a href="/wiki/Two-round_system" title="Two-round system">run-off</a> <a href="/wiki/Ukrainian_presidential_election,_2004" title="Ukrainian presidential election, 2004">presidential election</a> today. Voters will decide between Moscow-oriented Prime Minister <a href="/wiki/Viktor_Yanukovych" title="Viktor Yanukovych">Viktor Yanukovych</a> and western-leaning reformer <a href="/wiki/Viktor_Yushchenko" title="Viktor Yushchenko">Viktor Yushchenko</a>. Observers have expressed concern over possible Russian interference, election abuses, and <a href="/wiki/Bias" title="Bias">bias</a> in reporting by the state <a href="/wiki/News_media" title="News media">media</a>. With 74% of vote counted, Yanukovych leads Yushchenko 49–48%. Yushchenko has alleged that massive election fraud has taken place. <a class="external text" href="http://news.bbc.co.uk/1/hi/world/europe/4029635.stm" rel="nofollow">(BBC)</a> <a class="external text" href="http://news.bbc.co.uk/2/hi/europe/4031127.stm" rel="nofollow">(BBC)</a></li>
<li>The Electoral Commission of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Iraq_interim_government" title="Iraq interim government">Iraq interim government</a> schedules <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Iraqi_transitional_parliamentary_election" title="Iraqi transitional parliamentary election">parliamentary elections</a> for January 30, 2005. <a class="external text" href="http://www.reuters.co.uk/newsPackageArticle.jhtml?type=topNews&amp;storyID=624862&amp;section=news" rel="nofollow">Reuters</a></li>
<li>The <a href="/wiki/Grand_Canyon" title="Grand Canyon">Grand Canyon</a> is artificially flooded to bring natural <a href="/wiki/Sediment" title="Sediment">sediment</a> to the ecosystem. <a class="external text" href="http://www.cnn.com/2004/TECH/science/11/21/grand.canyon.ap/index.html" rel="nofollow">(CNN)</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Kurt_Busch" title="Kurt Busch">Kurt Busch</a> clinches the first <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/NASCAR_Nextel_Cup" title="NASCAR Nextel Cup">NASCAR Nextel Cup</a> championship trophy.</li>
<li>The <a href="/wiki/Nintendo_DS" title="Nintendo DS">Nintendo DS</a> was released in North America.</li>
</ul>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="November_22.2C_2004_.28Monday.29">November 22, 2004 (Monday)</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Portal:Current_events/November_2004&amp;action=edit&amp;section=22" title="Edit section: November 22, 2004 (Monday)">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<ul>
<li><a href="/wiki/Ukrainian_presidential_election,_2004" title="Ukrainian presidential election, 2004">2004 Ukrainian presidential election</a>: <a href="/wiki/Ukraine" title="Ukraine">Ukraine</a>'s electoral commission declares <a href="/wiki/Prime_Minister_of_Ukraine" title="Prime Minister of Ukraine">Prime Minister</a> <a href="/wiki/Viktor_Yanukovych" title="Viktor Yanukovych">Viktor Yanukovych</a> the winner. Opposition leader <a href="/wiki/Viktor_Yushchenko" title="Viktor Yushchenko">Viktor Yushchenko</a> calls for supporters to protest "the total falsification of the vote". Observers from the <a href="/wiki/Organization_for_Security_and_Co-operation_in_Europe" title="Organization for Security and Co-operation in Europe">Organization for Security and Co-operation in Europe</a> (OSCE) say the run-off vote "did not meet international standards", and the senior U.S. election observer, <a href="/wiki/United_States_Senate" title="United States Senate">Senator</a> <a href="/wiki/Richard_Lugar" title="Richard Lugar">Richard Lugar</a>, notes a "concerted and forceful program of election day fraud". <a class="external text" href="http://reuters.com/newsArticle.jhtml?type=worldNews&amp;storyID=6889036" rel="nofollow">(Reuters)</a> <a class="external text" href="http://news.bbc.co.uk/2/hi/europe/4031981.stm" rel="nofollow">(BBC)</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/European_Parliament" title="European Parliament">European Parliament</a> lawmakers urge <a href="/wiki/European_Commission" title="European Commission">European Commission</a> <a href="/wiki/President_of_the_European_Commission" title="President of the European Commission">president</a> <a href="/wiki/Jos%C3%A9_Manuel_Barroso" title="José Manuel Barroso">José Manuel Barroso</a> to suspend Transport Commissioner <a href="/wiki/Jacques_Barrot" title="Jacques Barrot">Jacques Barrot</a>, after it was revealed that Barrot was involved in a party funding scandal in 2000. <a class="external text" href="http://edition.cnn.com/2004/WORLD/europe/11/22/eu.commission.ap/index.html" rel="nofollow">(CNN)</a></li>
<li><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Iran%27s_nuclear_program" title="Iran's nuclear program">Iran's nuclear program</a>: <a href="/wiki/Iran" title="Iran">Iran</a> declares that it will suspend its <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Uranium_enrichment" title="Uranium enrichment">uranium enrichment</a> programme to comply with a <a href="/wiki/European_Union" title="European Union">European Union</a>-brokered deadline. Iran will review its decision in three months. The EU seeks to have the suspension made permanent and is willing to provide economic and political incentives. <a class="external text" href="http://www.reuters.com/newsArticle.jhtml?type=worldNews&amp;storyID=6889248&amp;section=news" rel="nofollow">(Reuters)</a><a class="external text" href="http://news.bbc.co.uk/1/hi/world/middle_east/4031055.stm" rel="nofollow">(BBC)</a></li>
<li>A mechanical failure has been blamed for an <a href="/wiki/Oil_spill" title="Oil spill">oil spill</a> on the eastern coast of Canada. Experts estimate 170,000 litres of oil have been spilled into the Atlantic Ocean off the coast of <a href="/wiki/Newfoundland_(island)" title="Newfoundland (island)">Newfoundland</a>, covering an area 9 km long by 1 km wide. <a class="external text" href="http://www.cbc.ca/canada/story/2004/11/22/newfoundland-oilspill041122.html" rel="nofollow">(CBC)</a></li>
<li>A <a href="/wiki/Gulfstream_Aerospace" title="Gulfstream Aerospace">Gulfstream II</a> airplane heading to pick up former <a href="/wiki/President_of_the_United_States" title="President of the United States">United States President</a> <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/George_H.W._Bush" title="George H.W. Bush">George H.W. Bush</a> crashes before landing, killing all three people on board, in <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Houston,_Texas" title="Houston, Texas">Houston, Texas</a>. <a class="external text" href="http://www.cnn.com/2004/US/11/22/texas.crash/index.html" rel="nofollow">(CNN)</a></li>
<li>The <a href="/wiki/American_Journal_of_Psychiatry" title="American Journal of Psychiatry">American Journal of Psychiatry</a> reports researchers from the <a href="/wiki/University_of_Southern_California" title="University of Southern California">University of Southern California</a> conclude in a study of 1,000 <a href="/wiki/Mauritius" title="Mauritius">Mauritian</a> children that <a href="/wiki/Malnutrition" title="Malnutrition">malnutrition</a> and a poor diet are strongly <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Correlation" title="Correlation">correlated</a> to a low <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/IQ" title="IQ">IQ</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Anti-social_behavior" title="Anti-social behavior">anti-social behavior</a>. <a class="external text" href="http://news.bbc.co.uk/2/hi/health/4032449.stm" rel="nofollow">(BBC)</a> <a class="external text" href="http://ajp.psychiatryonline.org/cgi/content/abstract/161/11/2005" rel="nofollow">(AJP)</a></li>
<li>The <a href="/wiki/United_Nations" title="United Nations">United Nations</a> is investigating 150 <a href="/wiki/Sexual_abuse" title="Sexual abuse">sexual abuse</a> allegations involving civilian staff and soldiers on the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Peace-keeping" title="Peace-keeping">peace-keeping</a> mission in the <a href="/wiki/Democratic_Republic_of_the_Congo" title="Democratic Republic of the Congo">Congo</a>, some reportedly caught on video. <a class="external text" href="http://reuters.com/newsArticle.jhtml?type=worldNews&amp;storyID=6889808&amp;section=news" rel="nofollow">(Reuters)</a></li>
<li>An <a href="/wiki/Israel" title="Israel">Israeli</a> military court indicts an unidentified outpost commander in charge of soldiers who killed a 13-year-old <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Palestinian_people" title="Palestinian people">Palestinian</a> girl in the <a href="/wiki/Gaza_Strip" title="Gaza Strip">Gaza Strip</a> on October 5. <a class="external text" href="http://www.haaretz.com/hasen/spages/504926.html" rel="nofollow">(Haaretz)</a></li>
<li>In the Canadian province of <a href="/wiki/Alberta" title="Alberta">Alberta</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Progressive_Conservative_Association_of_Alberta" title="Progressive Conservative Association of Alberta">Progressive Conservative</a> party under Premier <a href="/wiki/Ralph_Klein" title="Ralph Klein">Ralph Klein</a> is <a href="/wiki/Alberta_general_election,_2004" title="Alberta general election, 2004">re-elected</a> to a 10th consecutive term, and the fourth for Klein. The PCs drop to from 74 to 60 seats in the 83-seat legislature.<a class="external text" href="http://www.canada.com/edmonton/edmontonjournal/news/albertavotes/story.html?id=2d2409f2-d950-4ab9-b305-af2a0f8c80c4" rel="nofollow">(Edmonton Journal)</a> <a class="external text" href="http://www.cbc.ca/canada/story/2004/11/23/alberta-election-041123.html" rel="nofollow">(CBC)</a></li>
</ul>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="November_23.2C_2004_.28Tuesday.29">November 23, 2004 (Tuesday)</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Portal:Current_events/November_2004&amp;action=edit&amp;section=23" title="Edit section: November 23, 2004 (Tuesday)">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<ul>
<li><a href="/wiki/CBS_News" title="CBS News">CBS News</a> anchor <a href="/wiki/Dan_Rather" title="Dan Rather">Dan Rather</a> resigns from <a href="/wiki/CBS_Evening_News" title="CBS Evening News">CBS Evening News</a> effective in March 2005. He will remain a correspondent for <a href="/wiki/60_Minutes" title="60 Minutes">60 Minutes</a> news magazine and other assignments. <a class="external text" href="http://olympics.reuters.com/newsArticle.jhtml?type=entertainmentNews&amp;storyID=6899357" rel="nofollow">(Reuters)</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Ukrainian_presidential_election,_2004" title="Ukrainian presidential election, 2004">2004 Ukrainian presidential election</a>: Opposition leader <a href="/wiki/Viktor_Yushchenko" title="Viktor Yushchenko">Viktor Yushchenko</a> declares himself winner and takes a symbolic oath of office at a parliament special session, boycotted by pro-government <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Member_of_Parliament" title="Member of Parliament">MPs</a>. Crowds of around 200,000 Yushchenko supporters rally outside the parliament building in <a href="/wiki/Kiev" title="Kiev">Kiev</a>. <a href="/wiki/Freedom_House" title="Freedom House">Freedom House</a> releases a statement saying that the runoff election was "tainted by massive voter fraud." Russian Foreign Ministry expresses "extreme concern" about the disobedience actions by the Ukrainian opposition. <a class="external text" href="http://news.bbc.co.uk/2/hi/europe/4036867.stm" rel="nofollow">(BBC)</a> <a class="external text" href="http://reuters.com/newsArticle.jhtml?type=worldNews&amp;storyID=6898993" rel="nofollow">(Reuters)</a> <a class="external text" href="http://freedomhouse.org/media/pressrel/112204.htm" rel="nofollow">(FH)</a>
<ul>
<li>The city governments of <a href="/wiki/Lviv" title="Lviv">Lviv</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ternopil" title="Ternopil">Ternopil</a>, <a href="/wiki/Vinnytsia" title="Vinnytsia">Vinnytsia</a> and <a href="/wiki/Ivano-Frankivsk" title="Ivano-Frankivsk">Ivano-Frankivsk</a> announce their support for Yushchenko. A crowd estimated at 200,000 surrounds the Parliament building in <a href="/wiki/Kiev" title="Kiev">Kiev</a>, calling for Yanukovych to step down. <a class="external text" href="http://www.guardian.co.uk/worldlatest/story/0,1280,-4632943,00.html" rel="nofollow">(The Guardian)</a></li>
</ul>
</li>
<li><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Conflict_in_Iraq" title="Conflict in Iraq">Conflict in Iraq</a>
<ul>
<li>Officials from the <a href="/wiki/Arab_League" title="Arab League">Arab League</a>, <a href="/wiki/Organisation_of_Islamic_Cooperation" title="Organisation of Islamic Cooperation">Organisation of the Islamic Conference</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/G8" title="G8">G8</a> nations, People's Republic of China and <a href="/wiki/United_Nations" title="United Nations">UN</a> <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Secretary_General" title="Secretary General">Secretary General</a> <a href="/wiki/Kofi_Annan" title="Kofi Annan">Kofi Annan</a> convene at <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Sharm_el-Sheikh" title="Sharm el-Sheikh">Sharm el-Sheikh</a>, <a href="/wiki/Egypt" title="Egypt">Egypt</a> to discuss and issue declarations on <a href="/wiki/Iraq" title="Iraq">Iraq</a>. <a class="external text" href="http://news.bbc.co.uk/2/hi/middle_east/4035625.stm" rel="nofollow">(BBC)</a> <a class="external text" href="http://reuters.com/newsArticle.jhtml?type=worldNews&amp;storyID=6896464" rel="nofollow">(Reuters)</a></li>
<li>A second <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Cleric" title="Cleric">cleric</a> of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Sunni" title="Sunni">Sunni</a> <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Muslim_Clerics_Association" title="Muslim Clerics Association">Muslim Clerics Association</a> in two days is gunned down in <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Miqdadiya" title="Miqdadiya">Miqdadiya</a> near <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Baquba" title="Baquba">Baquba</a> on his way to a mosque. <a class="external text" href="http://reuters.com/newsArticle.jhtml?type=worldNews&amp;storyID=6892146&amp;section=news" rel="nofollow">(Reuters)</a></li>
</ul>
</li>
<li>The popular <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/MMORPG" title="MMORPG">MMORPG</a> <a href="/wiki/World_of_Warcraft" title="World of Warcraft">World of Warcraft</a> was released on this day, on the 10th anniversary of the <a href="/wiki/Warcraft" title="Warcraft">Warcraft franchise</a>.</li>
</ul>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="November_24.2C_2004_.28Wednesday.29">November 24, 2004 (Wednesday)</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Portal:Current_events/November_2004&amp;action=edit&amp;section=24" title="Edit section: November 24, 2004 (Wednesday)">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<ul>
<li><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/2004_U.S._presidential_election_controversy" title="2004 U.S. presidential election controversy">2004 U.S. presidential election controversy</a>: The U.S. <a href="/wiki/Government_Accountability_Office" title="Government Accountability Office">Government Accountability Office</a> plans to investigate complaints of several systemic problems with this month's elections. <a class="external text" href="http://www.cnn.com/2004/ALLPOLITICS/11/23/election.investigation/" rel="nofollow">(CNN)</a>
<ul>
<li><a href="/wiki/Ohio" title="Ohio">Ohio</a> law requires state officials to perform a recount when called for by candidates on the ballot, but a federal judge today declared that the results can be declared final before the recount occurs. <a class="external text" href="http://www.cnn.com/2004/ALLPOLITICS/11/24/ohio.vote.ap/" rel="nofollow">(CNN)</a></li>
<li><a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Justice_Through_Music&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Justice Through Music (page does not exist)">Justice Through Music</a> has posted a minimum $200,000 reward for specific evidence of vote fraud in the recent election in light of the many instances of reported voter irregularities. <a class="external text" href="http://www.emediawire.com/releases/2004/11/emw180023.htm" rel="nofollow">(eMediaWire)</a></li>
</ul>
</li>
<li><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Israeli-Palestinian_conflict" title="Israeli-Palestinian conflict">Israeli-Palestinian conflict</a>:
<ul>
<li><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Israeli_Defence_Force" title="Israeli Defence Force">Israeli Defence Force</a> officer claims, he was right to repeatedly shoot an unarmed 13-year-old <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Palestinian_people" title="Palestinian people">Palestinian</a> girl in Gaza, saying he would have killed her even if she was three years old.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-7"><a href="#cite_note-7">[7]</a></sup></li>
</ul>
</li>
<li><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Iran%27s_nuclear_program" title="Iran's nuclear program">Iran's nuclear program</a>: The <a href="/wiki/European_Union" title="European Union">European Union</a> rejects a request by <a href="/wiki/Iran" title="Iran">Iran</a> to be allowed <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Iran%27s_nuclear_program" title="Iran's nuclear program">to continue using</a> <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Uranium_enrichment" title="Uranium enrichment">uranium enrichment</a> <a href="/wiki/Centrifuge" title="Centrifuge">centrifuges</a>. <a class="external text" href="http://www.reuters.com/newsArticle.jhtml?type=worldNews&amp;storyID=6910662&amp;section=news" rel="nofollow">(Reuters)</a></li>
<li><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/U.S._Department_of_Agriculture" title="U.S. Department of Agriculture">U.S. Department of Agriculture</a> officials have announced that the possible U.S. case of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Mad_cow" title="Mad cow">mad cow</a> disease from the previous week has tested negative twice in tests run by the <a href="/wiki/National_Veterinary_Services_Laboratory" title="National Veterinary Services Laboratory">National Veterinary Services Laboratory</a>. <a class="external text" href="http://www.sacbee.com/content/business/story/11551940p-12450633c.html" rel="nofollow">(Sac. Bee)</a> <a class="external text" href="http://www.wisconsinagconnection.com/story-national.cfm?Id=1228&amp;yr=2004" rel="nofollow">(Wisc. Ag.)</a></li>
<li>Despite earlier reports that <a href="/wiki/Ukraine" title="Ukraine">Ukraine</a>'s Prime Minister <a href="/wiki/Viktor_Yanukovych" title="Viktor Yanukovych">Viktor Yanukovych</a> and opposition leader <a href="/wiki/Viktor_Yushchenko" title="Viktor Yushchenko">Viktor Yushchenko</a> had agreed to hold talks over the country's <a href="/wiki/Ukrainian_presidential_election,_2004" title="Ukrainian presidential election, 2004">heavily disputed elections</a>, this now seems unlikely. Protests continue, with an official election result due to be announced at around 1400 UTC. <a class="external text" href="http://news.bbc.co.uk/1/hi/world/europe/4037419.stm" rel="nofollow">(BBC)</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Indonesia" title="Indonesia">Indonesian</a> police officials announce the arrest of four suspects wanted concerning the <a href="/wiki/2004_Australian_Embassy_bombing_in_Jakarta" title="2004 Australian Embassy bombing in Jakarta">2004 Australian Embassy bombing in Jakarta</a>. <a class="external text" href="http://news.bbc.co.uk/2/hi/asia-pacific/4037403.stm" rel="nofollow">(BBC)</a> <a class="external text" href="http://edition.cnn.com/2004/WORLD/asiapcf/11/24/jakarta.arrests/index.html" rel="nofollow">(CNN)</a></li>
</ul>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="November_25.2C_2004_.28Thursday.29">November 25, 2004 (Thursday)</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Portal:Current_events/November_2004&amp;action=edit&amp;section=25" title="Edit section: November 25, 2004 (Thursday)">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<ul>
<li>India proposes to Pakistan that India grant <a href="/wiki/Kashmir" title="Kashmir">Kashmir</a> a large amount of <a class="extiw" href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/autonomy" title="wiktionary:autonomy">autonomy</a>, in order to end the <a href="/wiki/War" title="War">state of war</a> between the two countries, but that the current <a href="/wiki/Border" title="Border">border</a> can not be modified. Pakistan recently proposed that Kashmir be <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Demilitarization" title="Demilitarization">demilitarized</a>, split along <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Ethnic" title="Ethnic">ethnic</a>/<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Religious" title="Religious">religious</a> lines and granted <a href="/wiki/Independence" title="Independence">independence</a> or transferred to <a href="/wiki/United_Nations" title="United Nations">United Nations</a> control. <a class="external text" href="http://en.wikipedia.org/w/wiki.phtml?title=Current_events&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9">(Reuters)</a></li>
<li>The <a href="/wiki/Ukraine" title="Ukraine">Ukrainian</a> Supreme Court bars publication of the presidential election results, delaying inauguration, and decides to examine a complaint alleging fraud on November 28. <a class="external text" href="http://www.reuters.com/newsArticle.jhtml?type=worldNews&amp;storyID=6920567&amp;section=news" rel="nofollow">(Reuters)</a></li>
<li><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Iran%27s_nuclear_program" title="Iran's nuclear program">Iran's nuclear program</a>: Just three days after an agreement with the <a href="/wiki/European_Union" title="European Union">European Union</a> took effect, <a href="/wiki/Iran" title="Iran">Iran</a> prevents the <a href="/wiki/International_Atomic_Energy_Agency" title="International Atomic Energy Agency">International Atomic Energy Agency</a> (IAEA) from sealing <a href="/wiki/Centrifuge" title="Centrifuge">centrifuges</a> at the <a href="/wiki/Natanz" title="Natanz">Natanz</a> enrichment facility. The IAEA begins its meeting to decide whether or not to refer the matter to the <a href="/wiki/United_Nations_Security_Council" title="United Nations Security Council">United Nations Security Council</a>. <a class="external text" href="http://www.reuters.com/newsArticle.jhtml?type=worldNews&amp;storyID=6920959&amp;section=news" rel="nofollow">(Reuters)</a></li>
<li>A previously scheduled <a href="/wiki/European_Union" title="European Union">EU</a>–Russia <a href="/wiki/Summit_(meeting)" title="Summit (meeting)">summit</a> in <a href="/wiki/The_Hague" title="The Hague">The Hague</a> is overshadowed by the <a href="/wiki/Ukrainian_presidential_election,_2004" title="Ukrainian presidential election, 2004">Ukraine presidential election</a> crisis. <a class="external text" href="http://ec.europa.eu/comm/external_relations/russia/summit_11_04/" rel="nofollow">(official EU)</a> <a class="external text" href="http://news.bbc.co.uk/2/hi/europe/4040667.stm" rel="nofollow">(BBC)</a></li>
<li>Gang war between rival groups of <a href="/wiki/Camorra" title="Camorra">Camorra</a> continues in <a href="/wiki/Naples" title="Naples">Naples</a>, Italy. <a class="external text" href="http://www.swissinfo.org/sen/Swissinfo.html?siteSect=143&amp;sid=5362295" rel="nofollow">(SwissInfo)</a> <a class="external text" href="http://news.scotsman.com/latest.cfm?id=3786371" rel="nofollow">(Scotsman)</a> <a class="external text" href="http://news.bbc.co.uk/1/hi/world/europe/4037879.stm" rel="nofollow">(BBC)</a></li>
<li>The Indian <a href="/wiki/Political_party" title="Political party">political party</a> <a href="/wiki/Congress_Jananayaka_Peravai" title="Congress Jananayaka Peravai">Congress Jananayaka Peravai</a> merges into the <a href="/wiki/Indian_National_Congress" title="Indian National Congress">Indian National Congress</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-8"><a href="#cite_note-8">[8]</a></sup></li>
</ul>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="November_26.2C_2004_.28Friday.29">November 26, 2004 (Friday)</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Portal:Current_events/November_2004&amp;action=edit&amp;section=26" title="Edit section: November 26, 2004 (Friday)">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<ul>
<li>A <a href="/wiki/Wisconsin" title="Wisconsin">Wisconsin</a> girl becomes the first person to survive <a href="/wiki/Rabies" title="Rabies">rabies</a> without a <a href="/wiki/Vaccination" title="Vaccination">vaccination</a>, after an experimental treatment using an induced <a href="/wiki/Coma" title="Coma">coma</a> and a <a href="/wiki/Cocktail" title="Cocktail">cocktail</a> of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Virus_(biology)" title="Virus (biology)">anti-viral</a> drugs. <a class="external text" href="http://www.thedenverchannel.com/health/3947049/detail.html" rel="nofollow">(TheDenverChannel)</a></li>
<li>Pakistani President <a href="/wiki/Pervez_Musharraf" title="Pervez Musharraf">Pervez Musharraf</a> begins a tour of several <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/The_Americas" title="The Americas">American</a> and European countries to urge Western leaders to resolve the <a href="/wiki/Kashmir" title="Kashmir">Kashmir</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Arab-Israeli_conflict" title="Arab-Israeli conflict">Palestinian</a> disputes, which he sees as root causes of <a href="/wiki/Terrorism" title="Terrorism">terrorism</a> by Muslims. <a class="external text" href="http://www.reuters.com/newsArticle.jhtml?type=worldNews&amp;storyID=6929070&amp;section=news" rel="nofollow">(Reuters)</a></li>
<li><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Ukraine_presidential_election,_2004" title="Ukraine presidential election, 2004">Ukraine presidential election, 2004</a>:
<ul>
<li>The <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Luhans%27k_region" title="Luhans'k region">Luhans'k region</a> of Ukraine, the easternmost Russian-speaking region, has reportedly declared itself autonomous and requested recognition from the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Russian_Federation" title="Russian Federation">Russian Federation</a>. Several more regions, including <a href="/wiki/Donetsk" title="Donetsk">Donetsk</a>, have ruled to put autonomy on popular referendum.</li>
<li>Supporters of opposition leader <a href="/wiki/Viktor_Yushchenko" title="Viktor Yushchenko">Viktor Yushchenko</a> blockaded official buildings in <a href="/wiki/Kiev" title="Kiev">Kiev</a> Friday, in a direct challenge to the Moscow-backed government's control of the country. <a class="external text" href="http://reuters.myway.com/article/20041126/2004-11-26T122213Z_01_L2624987_RTRIDST_0_NEWS-UKRAINE-DC.html" rel="nofollow">(Reuters)</a></li>
<li>Russian President <a href="/wiki/Vladimir_Putin" title="Vladimir Putin">Vladimir Putin</a> said after a summit meeting with the <a href="/wiki/European_Union" title="European Union">European Union</a> that the results of the Ukrainian presidential elections are absolutely clear. <a class="external text" href="http://sg.news.yahoo.com/041125/1/3ot70.html" rel="nofollow">(AFP)</a></li>
<li>Ukrainian President <a href="/wiki/Leonid_Kuchma" title="Leonid Kuchma">Leonid Kuchma</a> began meeting with key European envoys, including <a href="/wiki/European_Union" title="European Union">European Union</a> foreign policy chief <a href="/wiki/Javier_Solana" title="Javier Solana">Javier Solana</a>, Polish president <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Aleksander_Kwasniewski" title="Aleksander Kwasniewski">Aleksander Kwasniewski</a>, <a href="/wiki/Lithuania" title="Lithuania">Lithuanian</a> president <a href="/wiki/Valdas_Adamkus" title="Valdas Adamkus">Valdas Adamkus</a> and Russian parliament speaker <a href="/wiki/Boris_Gryzlov" title="Boris Gryzlov">Boris Gryzlov</a>. Opposition leader Viktor Yushchenko has requested a new vote to be held on December 12 <a class="external text" href="http://news.bbc.co.uk/1/hi/world/europe/4045449.stm" rel="nofollow">(BBC)</a></li>
</ul>
</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Alberto_Abadie" title="Alberto Abadie">Alberto Abadie</a>, a professor at the <a href="/wiki/Harvard_University" title="Harvard University">Harvard University</a> <a href="/wiki/John_F._Kennedy_School_of_Government" title="John F. Kennedy School of Government">School of Government</a>, theorizes that the level of <a href="/wiki/Political_freedom" title="Political freedom">political freedom</a>, not <a href="/wiki/Poverty" title="Poverty">poverty</a>, explains <a href="/wiki/Terrorism" title="Terrorism">terrorism</a>. Areas with intermediate levels of political freedom experience the most terrorism, while societies with high levels of political freedom or <a href="/wiki/Authoritarianism" title="Authoritarianism">authoritarian regimes</a> have low levels of terrorism. <a class="external text" href="http://ksghome.harvard.edu/~.aabadie.academic.ksg/povterr.pdf" rel="nofollow">(PDF)</a> <a class="external text" href="http://www.news.harvard.edu/gazette/2004/11.04/05-terror.html" rel="nofollow">(Harvard Gazette)</a></li>
<li>People are evacuated from <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Manam" title="Manam">Manam</a> in northern <a href="/wiki/Papua_New_Guinea" title="Papua New Guinea">Papua New Guinea</a> during eruption of the island's volcano. <a class="external text" href="http://www.nzherald.co.nz/storydisplay.cfm?storyID=3604664&amp;thesection=news&amp;thesubsection=world" rel="nofollow">(New Zealand Herald)</a> <a class="external text" href="http://news.scotsman.com/latest.cfm?id=3807231" rel="nofollow">(Scotsman)</a> <a class="external text" href="http://www.swissinfo.org/sen/swissinfo.html?siteSect=143&amp;sid=5364823" rel="nofollow">(SwissInfo)</a></li>
<li>In one of Canada's largest <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Class-action_lawsuit" title="Class-action lawsuit">class-action lawsuits</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Court_of_Appeal_for_Ontario" title="Court of Appeal for Ontario">Court of Appeal for Ontario</a> upholds a lower court ruling whereby Canadians whose <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Gay_rights" title="Gay rights">same-sex partners</a> died after April 1985 are entitled to <a href="/wiki/Canada_Pension_Plan" title="Canada Pension Plan">Canada Pension Plan</a> survivors' benefits. <a class="external text" href="http://www.cbc.ca/canada/story/2004/11/26/cpp-ont041126.html" rel="nofollow">(CBC News)</a></li>
<li>The director for the western region of the <a href="/wiki/World_Health_Organization" title="World Health Organization">World Health Organization</a> says that an <a href="/wiki/Influenza" title="Influenza">influenza</a> <a href="/wiki/Pandemic" title="Pandemic">pandemic</a> is inevitable and plans to combat it are needed urgently. (In 1918–20, the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Spanish_Flu" title="Spanish Flu">Spanish Flu</a> killed up to <span class="nowrap">40 million</span> people.) The new virus is likely to develop out of <a href="/wiki/Avian_influenza" title="Avian influenza">avian influenza</a>. <a class="external text" href="http://story.news.yahoo.com/news?tmpl=story&amp;cid=570&amp;ncid=753&amp;e=2&amp;u=/nm/20041126/sc_nm/birdflu_dc" rel="nofollow">(Reuters)</a></li>
<li><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Conflict_in_Iraq" title="Conflict in Iraq">Conflict in Iraq</a>: In <a href="/wiki/Baghdad" title="Baghdad">Baghdad</a>, an American civilian contractor is shot near the <a href="/wiki/Green_Zone" title="Green Zone">Green Zone</a>. The largest <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Sunni" title="Sunni">Sunni</a> political party, <a href="/wiki/Iraqi_Islamic_Party" title="Iraqi Islamic Party">Iraqi Islamic Party</a>, calls for elections to be postponed for six months to allow better security and threatens a boycott. British troops join the operation to pacify the <a href="/wiki/Insurgency" title="Insurgency">insurgency</a> in the "<a href="/wiki/Sunni_Triangle" title="Sunni Triangle">Sunni Triangle</a>." <a href="/wiki/Iraq" title="Iraq">Iraqi</a> police state they have arrested five suspected foreign fighters in the south. The <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Iraqi_Minister_of_State&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Iraqi Minister of State (page does not exist)">Iraqi Minister of State</a> says <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Iraqi_National_Guard" title="Iraqi National Guard">Iraqi National Guard</a> discovered a small chemical and explosive lab in <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Falluja" title="Falluja">Falluja</a>. <a class="external text" href="http://reuters.com/newsArticle.jhtml?type=topNews&amp;storyID=6919217&amp;pageNumber=0" rel="nofollow">(Reuters)</a> <a class="external text" href="http://news.bbc.co.uk/2/hi/middle_east/4041235.stm" rel="nofollow">(BBC)</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Fatah" title="Fatah">Fatah</a> officially picks former Prime Minister <a href="/wiki/Mahmoud_Abbas" title="Mahmoud Abbas">Mahmoud Abbas</a>, already <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/PLO" title="PLO">PLO</a> chairman, as its candidate for January's presidential elections. <a class="external text" href="http://news.bbc.co.uk/2/hi/middle_east/4043065.stm" rel="nofollow">(BBC)</a> <a class="external text" href="http://www.reuters.com/newsArticle.jhtml?type=worldNews&amp;storyID=6921618" rel="nofollow">(Reuters)</a></li>
<li>The <a href="/wiki/President_of_Indonesia" title="President of Indonesia">President of Indonesia</a>, <a href="/wiki/Susilo_Bambang_Yudhoyono" title="Susilo Bambang Yudhoyono">Susilo Bambang Yudhoyono</a>, visits the province of <a href="/wiki/Aceh" title="Aceh">Aceh</a> for the first time, the location of a long <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Separatist" title="Separatist">separatist</a> movement. <a class="external text" href="http://news.bbc.co.uk/2/hi/asia-pacific/4043969.stm" rel="nofollow">(BBC)</a></li>
<li>Over 8,000 <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Landless&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Landless (page does not exist)">landless</a> activists, including the <a href="/wiki/Landless_Workers%27_Movement" title="Landless Workers' Movement">Landless Workers' Movement</a> (MST), march on <a href="/wiki/Bras%C3%ADlia" title="Brasília">Brasília</a>, Brazil, to demand the speeding up of <a href="/wiki/Land_reform" title="Land reform">land reform</a> promised by <a href="/wiki/President_of_Brazil" title="President of Brazil">President</a> <a href="/wiki/Luiz_In%C3%A1cio_Lula_da_Silva" title="Luiz Inácio Lula da Silva">Luiz Inácio Lula da Silva</a>. <a class="external text" href="http://www.reuters.com/newsArticle.jhtml?type=worldNews&amp;storyID=6922853" rel="nofollow">(Reuters)</a></li>
<li>The <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Pakistani_army" title="Pakistani army">Pakistani army</a> states they find no evidence <a href="/wiki/Osama_bin_Laden" title="Osama bin Laden">Osama bin Laden</a> is hiding in the mainly <a href="/wiki/Tribe" title="Tribe">tribal</a> border with <a href="/wiki/Afghanistan" title="Afghanistan">Afghanistan</a> after combing through the area. <a class="external text" href="http://reuters.com/newsArticle.jhtml?type=worldNews&amp;storyID=6920455&amp;section=news" rel="nofollow">(Reuters)</a></li>
<li>A man kills eight and injures four people with a knife at a Chinese high school in <a href="/wiki/Ruzhou" title="Ruzhou">Ruzhou</a>, <a href="/wiki/Henan" title="Henan">Henan</a>. <a class="external text" href="http://news.bbc.co.uk/2/hi/americas/4044047.stm" rel="nofollow">(BBC)</a> <a class="external text" href="http://news.xinhuanet.com/english/2004-11/26/content_2263815.htm" rel="nofollow">(Xinhua)</a></li>
</ul>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="November_27.2C_2004_.28Saturday.29">November 27, 2004 (Saturday)</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Portal:Current_events/November_2004&amp;action=edit&amp;section=27" title="Edit section: November 27, 2004 (Saturday)">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<ul>
<li>Prominent Chinese dissident <a href="/wiki/Liu_Jingsheng" title="Liu Jingsheng">Liu Jingsheng</a> is released. <a class="external text" href="http://news.bbc.co.uk/2/hi/asia-pacific/4048789.stm" rel="nofollow">(BBC)</a></li>
<li>Virginia Tech begins its reign of dominance over UVA, the Hokies clinch the Commonwealth Cup in a 24-10 win at Lane Stadium. The Hokies continue to hold the Commenwealth Cup for over 4000 days following this victory.</li>
<li><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Roman_Catholicism" title="Roman Catholicism">Roman Catholic</a> <a href="/wiki/Pope_John_Paul_II" title="Pope John Paul II">Pope John Paul II</a> presents <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Eastern_Orthodoxy" title="Eastern Orthodoxy">Eastern Orthodox</a> <a href="/wiki/Bartholomew_I_of_Constantinople" title="Bartholomew I of Constantinople">Patriarch Bartholomew I</a> with reliquaries containing the bones of 4th-century <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/List_of_Patriarchs_of_Constantinople" title="List of Patriarchs of Constantinople">Patriarchs</a> <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Gregory_Nazianzus" title="Gregory Nazianzus">Gregory Nazianzus</a> and <a href="/wiki/John_Chrysostom" title="John Chrysostom">John Chrysostom</a>, brought back to Rome as loot from <a href="/wiki/Constantinople" title="Constantinople">Constantinople</a> during the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Crusade" title="Crusade">Crusades</a>. The ceremony is applauded as a notable gesture of <a href="/wiki/Ecumenism" title="Ecumenism">ecumenism</a> between the <a href="/wiki/East%E2%80%93West_Schism" title="East–West Schism">divided</a> churches. <a class="external text" href="http://news.bbc.co.uk/2/hi/europe/4047327.stm" rel="nofollow">(BBC)</a> <a class="external text" href="http://www.reuters.com/newsArticle.jhtml?type=topNews&amp;storyID=6933821" rel="nofollow">(Reuters)</a></li>
<li>According to the chairman of the <a href="/wiki/Duma" title="Duma">Duma</a> commission investigating the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Beslan_school_massacre" title="Beslan school massacre">Beslan school massacre</a>, there is indirect evidence of involvement by a foreign intelligence agency; however, the agency remains unnamed. <a class="external text" href="http://www.interfax.ru/e/B/0/28.html?id_issue=10725087" rel="nofollow">(Interfax)</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Colombia" title="Colombia">Colombian</a> Defense Minister <a href="/wiki/Jorge_Alberto_Uribe" title="Jorge Alberto Uribe">Jorge Alberto Uribe</a> claims that <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Revolutionary_Armed_Forces_of_Colombia" title="Revolutionary Armed Forces of Colombia">FARC</a> rebels plotted to assassinate U.S. President <a href="/wiki/George_W._Bush" title="George W. Bush">George W. Bush</a> during his recent visit to the country. The <a href="/wiki/United_States_Secret_Service" title="United States Secret Service">U.S. Secret Service</a> declines to comment. <a class="external text" href="http://news.bbc.co.uk/2/hi/americas/4047199.stm" rel="nofollow">(BBC)</a>, <a class="external text" href="http://www.cnn.com/2004/WORLD/americas/11/27/bush-plot/index.html" rel="nofollow">(CNN)</a></li>
<li><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Ukraine_presidential_election,_2004" title="Ukraine presidential election, 2004">Ukraine presidential election, 2004</a>:
<ul>
<li><a href="/wiki/Verkhovna_Rada" title="Verkhovna Rada">Ukraine's parliament</a> votes for the annulment of the election results and asks <a href="/wiki/President_of_Ukraine" title="President of Ukraine">President</a> <a href="/wiki/Leonid_Kuchma" title="Leonid Kuchma">Leonid Kuchma</a> to dissolve the country's Central Election Committee. This is a non-binding request as the parliament cannot annul the results itself. <a class="external text" href="http://www.cnn.com/2004/WORLD/europe/11/27/ukraine/index.html" rel="nofollow">(CNN)</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Netherlands" title="Netherlands">Dutch</a> Foreign Minister <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Bernard_Bot" title="Bernard Bot">Bernard Bot</a> says that the <a href="/wiki/European_Union" title="European Union">EU</a> believes fresh elections are the best option for Ukraine. <a class="external text" href="http://www.swissinfo.org/sen/swissinfo.html?siteSect=143&amp;sid=5367505" rel="nofollow">(Reuters)</a></li>
</ul>
</li>
<li><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Lieutenant_General" title="Lieutenant General">Lieutenant General</a> <a href="/wiki/Joginder_Jaswant_Singh" title="Joginder Jaswant Singh">Joginder Jaswant Singh</a> is named the next chief of army staff of the <a href="/wiki/Indian_Army" title="Indian Army">Indian Army</a>. He will be the first <a href="/wiki/Sikh" title="Sikh">Sikh</a> to become the chief. <a class="external text" href="http://articles.timesofindia.indiatimes.com/2004-11-28/india/27161654_1_army-staff-vice-chief-indian-army" rel="nofollow">(Times of India)</a> <a class="external text" href="http://www.tribuneindia.com/2004/20041128/main2.htm" rel="nofollow">(The Tribune, India)</a></li>
</ul>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="November_28.2C_2004_.28Sunday.29">November 28, 2004 (Sunday)</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Portal:Current_events/November_2004&amp;action=edit&amp;section=28" title="Edit section: November 28, 2004 (Sunday)">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<ul>
<li>Swiss voters overwhelmingly approve government proposals to permit research using <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Stem_cells" title="Stem cells">stem cells</a> of human embryos. <a class="external text" href="http://news.bbc.co.uk/1/hi/world/europe/4049141.stm" rel="nofollow">(BBC)</a></li>
<li>An explosion in a <a href="/wiki/Coal_mining" title="Coal mining">coal mine</a> in the Chinese central province of <a href="/wiki/Shaanxi" title="Shaanxi">Shaanxi</a> leaves 187 men trapped underground. Official figures show 4,153 <a href="/wiki/Mining" title="Mining">mining</a> accident deaths in the last nine months, while 119 miners are still missing from a November 20 iron mine fire in <a href="/wiki/Hebei" title="Hebei">Hebei</a>. <a class="external text" href="http://news.bbc.co.uk/2/hi/asia-pacific/4049069.stm" rel="nofollow">(BBC)</a> <a class="external text" href="http://news.xinhuanet.com/english/2004-11/28/content_2269337.htm" rel="nofollow">(Xinhua)</a> <a class="external text" href="http://news.xinhuanet.com/english/2004-11/26/content_2265430.htm" rel="nofollow">(Xinhua)</a></li>
<li><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Conflict_in_Iraq" title="Conflict in Iraq">Conflict in Iraq</a>: 42 primarily <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Shi%27a" title="Shi'a">Shi'a</a> parties release a statement saying a postponement of elections would be illegal. The <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/United_States_military" title="United States military">U.S. military</a> reports a U.S. soldier is killed by a roadside bomb in <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Duluiya&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Duluiya (page does not exist)">Duluiya</a> north of <a href="/wiki/Baghdad" title="Baghdad">Baghdad</a> and that troops discover 17 more corpses in <a href="/wiki/Mosul" title="Mosul">Mosul</a>, raising the number found to at least 50 in two weeks. Hospital officials in <a href="/wiki/Ramadi" title="Ramadi">Ramadi</a> say two people are killed and three wounded when U.S. troops fire on suspected <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Iraqi_insurgency_(Iraq_War)" title="Iraqi insurgency (Iraq War)">insurgents</a>. <a class="external text" href="http://www.reuters.com/newsArticle.jhtml?type=worldNews&amp;storyID=6933225" rel="nofollow">(Reuters)</a> <a class="external text" href="http://news.bbc.co.uk/2/hi/middle_east/4048863.stm" rel="nofollow">(BBC)</a></li>
<li><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/2004_Ukrainian_presidential_election" title="2004 Ukrainian presidential election">2004 Ukrainian presidential election</a>:
<ul>
<li>Russia intimates that its opposition to fresh elections might not be unshakable. <a class="external text" href="http://news.bbc.co.uk/2/hi/europe/4048965.stm" rel="nofollow">(BBC)</a></li>
<li>The <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Donets%27ka_oblast%27" title="Donets'ka oblast'">Donetsk</a> regional council is to hold a referendum on 5 December on giving the region the status of a republic within <a href="/wiki/Ukraine" title="Ukraine">Ukraine</a>. <a class="external text" href="http://news.bbc.co.uk/1/hi/world/europe/4050281.stm" rel="nofollow">(BBC)</a></li>
</ul>
</li>
<li>An <a href="/wiki/Oil_tanker" title="Oil tanker">oil tanker</a>, the <i>Athos 1</i>, leaks approximately 30,000 US gallons (<span class="nowrap">100 m<sup>3</sup>)</span> of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Crude_oil" title="Crude oil">crude oil</a> into the <a href="/wiki/Delaware_River" title="Delaware River">Delaware River</a> in the eastern United States while pulling into a <a href="/wiki/Citgo" title="Citgo">Citgo</a> <a href="/wiki/Oil_refinery" title="Oil refinery">oil refinery</a>. The <a href="/wiki/United_States_Coast_Guard" title="United States Coast Guard">Coast Guard</a> closes part of the river to commercial traffic while cleanup begins. <a class="external text" href="http://www.reuters.com/newsArticle.jhtml?type=domesticNews&amp;storyID=6933782" rel="nofollow">(Reuters)</a></li>
</ul>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="November_29.2C_2004_.28Monday.29">November 29, 2004 (Monday)</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Portal:Current_events/November_2004&amp;action=edit&amp;section=29" title="Edit section: November 29, 2004 (Monday)">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<ul>
<li>The People's Republic of China and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/ASEAN" title="ASEAN">Association of South East Asian Nations</a> sign a trade pact that could eventually unite a quarter of the world's population in a free trade zone. <a class="external text" href="http://news.bbc.co.uk/2/hi/asia-pacific/4051653.stm" rel="nofollow">(BBC)</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Ukrainian_presidential_election,_2004" title="Ukrainian presidential election, 2004">2004 Ukrainian presidential election</a>: The <a href="/wiki/Supreme_Court_of_Ukraine" title="Supreme Court of Ukraine">Supreme Court</a> continues its public hearings of <a href="/wiki/Electoral_fraud" title="Electoral fraud">electoral fraud</a>. Outgoing <a href="/wiki/President_of_Ukraine" title="President of Ukraine">President</a> <a href="/wiki/Leonid_Kuchma" title="Leonid Kuchma">Leonid Kuchma</a> asks for a new election "to preserve peace and consensus and build this just democratic society". <a class="external text" href="http://www.reuters.com/newsArticle.jhtml?type=worldNews&amp;storyID=6945191" rel="nofollow">(Reuters)</a> <a class="external text" href="http://news.bbc.co.uk/1/hi/world/europe/4053067.stm" rel="nofollow">(BBC)</a></li>
<li><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Conflict_in_Iraq" title="Conflict in Iraq">Conflict in Iraq</a>:
<ul>
<li>Two U.S. soldiers are killed and three wounded when a roadside bomb in <a href="/wiki/Baghdad" title="Baghdad">Baghdad</a> detonates. Four <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Iraqi_National_Guard" title="Iraqi National Guard">Iraqi National Guard</a> are killed in an attack on a checkpoint in nearby <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Baghdadi,_Iraq" title="Baghdadi, Iraq">Baghdadi</a>. Six <a href="/wiki/Iraq" title="Iraq">Iraqis</a> are killed in a blast near a police station in <a href="/wiki/Ramadi" title="Ramadi">Ramadi</a>. The Iraqi <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Red_Crescent" title="Red Crescent">Red Crescent</a> establishes a relief center in <a href="/wiki/Fallujah" title="Fallujah">Fallujah</a>, while the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/International_Red_Cross" title="International Red Cross">International Red Cross</a> says the city remains under siege and workers are unable to freely administer aid. <a class="external text" href="http://www.reuters.com/newsArticle.jhtml?type=worldNews&amp;storyID=6945002" rel="nofollow">(Reuters)</a> <a class="external text" href="http://news.bbc.co.uk/1/hi/world/middle_east/4051391.stm" rel="nofollow">(BBC)</a></li>
<li>Deputy leader of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Al_Qaida" title="Al Qaida">al Qaida</a> <a href="/wiki/Ayman_al-Zawahiri" title="Ayman al-Zawahiri">Ayman al-Zawahiri</a> releases a videotape vowing to continue fighting "until the last hour" and urging the U.S. to cooperate with <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Muslims" title="Muslims">Muslims</a> and stop dealing "with them as free loot, robbed land and violated sanctity." <a class="external text" href="http://www.reuters.com/newsArticle.jhtml?type=worldNews&amp;storyID=6945467" rel="nofollow">(Reuters)</a></li>
</ul>
</li>
<li>Researchers from <a href="/wiki/South_Korea" title="South Korea">South Korea</a> have successfully used <a href="/wiki/Stem_cell" title="Stem cell">stem cell</a> therapy to allow a <a href="/wiki/Paralysis" title="Paralysis">paralyzed</a> woman with <a href="/wiki/Spinal_cord" title="Spinal cord">spinal cord</a> injury to walk again. <a class="external text" href="http://www.wpherald.com/storyview.php?StoryID=20041127-121143-6745r" rel="nofollow">(WPH)</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/President_of_the_United_States" title="President of the United States">U.S. President</a> <a href="/wiki/George_W._Bush" title="George W. Bush">George W. Bush</a> nominates <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Kellogg_Company" title="Kellogg Company">Kellogg Company</a> <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/CEO" title="CEO">CEO</a> <a href="/wiki/Carlos_Gutierrez" title="Carlos Gutierrez">Carlos Gutierrez</a> to be the next <a href="/wiki/United_States_Secretary_of_Commerce" title="United States Secretary of Commerce">Secretary of Commerce</a>. <a class="external text" href="http://www.usatoday.com/news/washington/2004-11-29-commerce_x.htm?POE=NEWISVA" rel="nofollow">(USA Today)</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Iran" title="Iran">Iranian</a>-born <a href="/wiki/Netherlands" title="Netherlands">Dutch</a> <a href="/wiki/Nationality" title="Nationality">national</a> <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Seyed_Mahmoud_Namini&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Seyed Mahmoud Namini (page does not exist)">Seyed Mahmoud Namini</a> is being <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Detain" title="Detain">detained</a> by the Canadian government as a potential security threat. He was arrested a month ago when 30 books related to <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Kurdish_people" title="Kurdish people">Kurdish</a> revolts in Iran were found in his bag. <a class="external text" href="http://www.thestar.com/NASApp/cs/ContentServer?pagename=thestar/Layout/Article_Type1&amp;call_pageid=971358637177&amp;c=Article&amp;cid=1101595809064" rel="nofollow">(Toronto Star)</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Aung_San_Suu_Kyi" title="Aung San Suu Kyi">Aung San Suu Kyi</a>, the leader of <a href="/wiki/Myanmar" title="Myanmar">Myanmar</a>'s <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Parliamentary_opposition" title="Parliamentary opposition">opposition</a> <a href="/wiki/National_League_for_Democracy" title="National League for Democracy">National League for Democracy</a>, will have her third period of <a href="/wiki/House_arrest" title="House arrest">house arrest</a> extended. <a class="external text" href="http://news.bbc.co.uk/2/hi/asia-pacific/4051235.stm" rel="nofollow">(BBC)</a></li>
<li>Five <a href="/wiki/Record_label" title="Record label">record labels</a> sue <a href="/wiki/Sharman_Networks" title="Sharman Networks">Sharman Networks</a>, the owner of <a href="/wiki/Peer-to-peer" title="Peer-to-peer">peer-to-peer</a> <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/File-sharing" title="File-sharing">file-sharing</a> system <a href="/wiki/Kazaa" title="Kazaa">Kazaa</a>, for facilitating <a href="/wiki/Copyright" title="Copyright">copyright</a> violations in an Australian court. <a class="external text" href="http://business.timesonline.co.uk/article/0,,9075-1380741,00.html" rel="nofollow">(The Times)</a> <a class="external text" href="http://news.ft.com/cms/s/2ce2bfca-423f-11d9-8e3c-00000e2511c8.html" rel="nofollow">(Financial Times)</a> <a class="external text" href="http://www.wired.com/news/digiwood/0,1412,65860,00.html?tw=wn_tophead_3" rel="nofollow">(Wired)</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Romania" title="Romania">Romania</a>'s ruling <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Social_Democratic_Party_of_Romania" title="Social Democratic Party of Romania">Social Democratic Party</a> claims victory in the country's <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Romanian_legislative_election,_2004" title="Romanian legislative election, 2004">legislative election</a>, and the simultaneous <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Romanian_presidential_election,_2004" title="Romanian presidential election, 2004">presidential election</a> goes to a second round with Prime Minister <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Adrian_Nastase" title="Adrian Nastase">Adrian Nastase</a> leading.</li>
<li>President of <a href="/wiki/Chile" title="Chile">Chile</a> <a href="/wiki/Ricardo_Lagos" title="Ricardo Lagos">Ricardo Lagos</a> proposes special lifetime pensions (approx. €150 a month) for 28,000 survivors of the <a href="/wiki/Augusto_Pinochet" title="Augusto Pinochet">Pinochet</a> <a href="/wiki/Military_dictatorship" title="Military dictatorship">regime</a>'s <a href="/wiki/Torture" title="Torture">torture</a> camps. <a class="external text" href="http://www.swissinfo.org/sen/swissinfo.html?siteSect=143&amp;sid=5369892" rel="nofollow">(SwissInfo)</a> <a class="external text" href="http://www.alertnet.org/thenews/newsdesk/N28367922.htm" rel="nofollow">(Reuters Alertnet)</a> <a class="external text" href="http://www.washingtonpost.com/wp-dyn/articles/A18924-2004Nov28.html" rel="nofollow">(Washington Post)</a></li>
<li>A <a href="/wiki/Richter_magnitude_scale" title="Richter magnitude scale">magnitude 7.0</a> <a href="/wiki/Earthquake" title="Earthquake">earthquake</a> hits <a href="/wiki/Hokkaido" title="Hokkaido">Hokkaido</a>, Japan. <a class="external text" href="http://abcnews.go.com/International/wireStory?id=288484" rel="nofollow">(ABC News)</a> <a class="external text" href="http://www.bloomberg.com/apps/news?pid=10000087&amp;sid=arZfQ_XUdmTU&amp;refer=top_world_news" rel="nofollow">(Bloomberg)</a> <a class="external text" href="http://www.swissinfo.org/sen/swissinfo.html?siteSect=143&amp;sid=5369843" rel="nofollow">(SwissInfo)</a> <a class="external text" href="http://earthquake.usgs.gov/eqinthenews/2004/usrjap/" rel="nofollow">(USGS)</a></li>
<li>A huge number of <a href="/wiki/Whale" title="Whale">whales</a> and <a href="/wiki/Dolphin" title="Dolphin">dolphins</a> are beached on the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/King_Island,_Australia" title="King Island, Australia">King Island</a> between the Australian mainland and <a href="/wiki/Tasmania" title="Tasmania">Tasmania</a>; rescue efforts are ongoing <a class="external text" href="http://www9.sbs.com.au/theworldnews/region.php?id=99966&amp;region=7" rel="nofollow">(SBS)</a> <a class="external text" href="http://www.swissinfo.org/sen/swissinfo.html?siteSect=143&amp;sid=5369873" rel="nofollow">(SwissInfo)</a> <a class="external text" href="http://www.nzherald.co.nz/index.cfm?ObjectID=8500821" rel="nofollow">(New Zealand Herald)</a></li>
<li>The <a href="/wiki/Supreme_Court_of_the_United_States" title="Supreme Court of the United States">U.S. Supreme Court</a> hears a landmark case to decide the rights of <a href="/wiki/U.S._state" title="U.S. state">states</a> to overrule <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Federal_Government_of_the_United_States" title="Federal Government of the United States">federal</a> restrictions on <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Medical_marijuana" title="Medical marijuana">medical marijuana</a> use. This case has important consequences for redefining the <a href="/wiki/Separation_of_powers" title="Separation of powers">separation and limitation of powers</a> between states and the federal government. <a class="external text" href="http://www.csmonitor.com/2004/1129/p02s01-usju.html" rel="nofollow">(CSM)</a></li>
<li>At the conclusion of <a href="/wiki/The_Greatest_Canadian" title="The Greatest Canadian">The Greatest Canadian</a> project, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Socialist" title="Socialist">socialist</a> politician <a href="/wiki/Tommy_Douglas" title="Tommy Douglas">Tommy Douglas</a> was announced as being voted as The Greatest Canadian of all. <a class="external text" href="http://www.thestar.com/NASApp/cs/ContentServer?pagename=thestar/Layout/Article_Type1&amp;c=Article&amp;cid=1101768608261&amp;call_pageid=968332188492&amp;col=968705899037&amp;DPL=IvsNDS/7ChAX&amp;tacodalogin=yes" rel="nofollow"><i>Toronto Star</i></a></li>
</ul>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="November_30.2C_2004_.28Tuesday.29">November 30, 2004 (Tuesday)</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Portal:Current_events/November_2004&amp;action=edit&amp;section=30" title="Edit section: November 30, 2004 (Tuesday)">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<ul>
<li><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/2004_U.S._presidential_election_controversy" title="2004 U.S. presidential election controversy">2004 U.S. presidential election controversy</a>:
<ul>
<li>Attorneys for <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Green_Party_(United_States)" title="Green Party (United States)">Green Party</a> presidential candidate <a href="/wiki/David_Cobb" title="David Cobb">David Cobb</a> asked a federal court to take jurisdiction of, and ultimately dissolve, a temporary restraining order issued by a <a href="/wiki/Delaware_County,_Ohio" title="Delaware County, Ohio">Delaware County, Ohio</a>, judge attempting to prevent Cobb from seeking a recount of the presidential ballots cast in that county.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-9"><a href="#cite_note-9">[9]</a></sup></li>
<li>Attorneys representing <a href="/wiki/John_Kerry" title="John Kerry">John Kerry</a> filed papers to join the Cobb/Badnarik Ohio recount case.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-10"><a href="#cite_note-10">[10]</a></sup></li>
<li>If the Ohio recount does not begin before the votes are certified, then <a href="/wiki/Electoral_college" title="Electoral college">electors</a> will be chosen before the recount begins.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-11"><a href="#cite_note-11">[11]</a></sup></li>
</ul>
</li>
<li>The U.S. <a href="/wiki/United_States_Department_of_Commerce" title="United States Department of Commerce">Department of Commerce</a> imposes heavy <a href="/wiki/Tariff" title="Tariff">tariffs</a> against shrimp imported to the U.S. from China and <a href="/wiki/Vietnam" title="Vietnam">Vietnam</a>. <a class="external text" href="http://www.bloomberg.com/apps/news?pid=10000080&amp;sid=aGA6kP1kjb5Q&amp;refer=asia" rel="nofollow">(Bloomberg)</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Ken_Jennings" title="Ken Jennings">Ken Jennings</a> ends his 75-episode streak on <i><a href="/wiki/Jeopardy!" title="Jeopardy!">Jeopardy!</a></i>, becoming the foremost <a href="/wiki/Game_show" title="Game show">game show</a> contestant in international television history.</li>
<li>In <a href="/wiki/Ottawa" title="Ottawa">Ottawa</a>, Canada, sporadic violence occurs in protests against U.S. President <a href="/wiki/George_W._Bush" title="George W. Bush">George W. Bush</a>'s first official visit to Canada. <a class="external text" href="http://www.cbc.ca/canada/story/2004/11/30/bush_arrives041130.html" rel="nofollow">(CBC)</a> <a class="external text" href="http://www.theglobeandmail.com/servlet/story/RTGAM.20041130.wshrub1130/BNStory/Front/" rel="nofollow">(Globe and Mail)</a></li>
<li>U.S. <a href="/wiki/United_States_Department_of_Homeland_Security" title="United States Department of Homeland Security">Department of Homeland Security</a> Secretary <a href="/wiki/Tom_Ridge" title="Tom Ridge">Tom Ridge</a> resigns. This is the latest in a string of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/George_W._Bush%27s_first_term_as_president_of_the_United_States#Post-election" title="George W. Bush's first term as president of the United States">resignations after the 2004 presidential election</a>. <a class="external text" href="http://www.cnn.com/2004/ALLPOLITICS/11/30/ridge/index.html" rel="nofollow">(CNN)</a> <a class="external text" href="http://story.news.yahoo.com/news?tmpl=story&amp;e=1&amp;u=/ap/20041130/ap_on_go_ca_st_pe/bush_cabinet" rel="nofollow">(Yahoo)</a></li>
<li>A report from the <a href="/wiki/International_Committee_of_the_Red_Cross" title="International Committee of the Red Cross">International Committee of the Red Cross</a>, recently leaked to the <i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/New_York_Times" title="New York Times">New York Times</a></i>, describes the treatment of prisoners at <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Camp_X-Ray" title="Camp X-Ray">the U.S. base in Guantánamo Bay, Cuba</a> as being "tantamount to <a href="/wiki/Torture" title="Torture">torture</a>". The <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/U.S._military" title="U.S. military">U.S. military</a> disputes this. <a class="external text" href="http://www.nytimes.com/2004/11/30/politics/30gitmo.html?ei=5006&amp;en=bba26d61a8097932&amp;ex=1102395600&amp;partner=ALTAVISTA1&amp;pagewanted=print&amp;position=" rel="nofollow">(New York Times)</a></li>
<li>More than 300 persons have died in flooding and <a href="/wiki/Landslide" title="Landslide">landslides</a> in <a href="/wiki/Quezon" title="Quezon">Quezon</a> Province, in the northern <a href="/wiki/Philippines" title="Philippines">Philippines</a>. Illegal logging is blamed. <a class="external text" href="http://www.alertnet.org/thenews/newsdesk/MAN198790.htm" rel="nofollow">(Reuters Alertnet)</a><a class="external text" href="http://www.abs-cbnnews.com/NewsStory.aspx?section=Headlines&amp;oid=64283" rel="nofollow">(ABS-CBN)</a> <a class="external text" href="http://www.swissinfo.org/sen/swissinfo.html?siteSect=143&amp;sid=5373660" rel="nofollow">(SwissInfo)</a> <a class="external text" href="http://www.abc.net.au/news/newsitems/200411/s1255101.htm" rel="nofollow">(ABC News)</a></li>
<li><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Traian_Basescu" title="Traian Basescu">Traian Basescu</a>, the leader of the <a href="/wiki/Romania" title="Romania">Romanian</a> opposition alliance <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Justice_and_Truth" title="Justice and Truth">Justice and Truth</a>, demands a re-run of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Romanian_legislative_election,_2004" title="Romanian legislative election, 2004">2004 legislative elections</a>, claiming that 160,000 void ballots were awarded to <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Adrian_Nastase" title="Adrian Nastase">Adrian Nastase</a> and his <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Social_Democratic_Party_of_Romania" title="Social Democratic Party of Romania">Social Democratic Party</a>. <a class="external text" href="http://news.bbc.co.uk/1/hi/world/europe/4055345.stm" rel="nofollow">(BBC)</a> <a class="external text" href="http://www.guardian.co.uk/international/story/0,3604,1362933,00.html" rel="nofollow">(Guardian)</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Portugal" title="Portugal">Portuguese</a> President <a href="/wiki/Jorge_Sampaio" title="Jorge Sampaio">Jorge Sampaio</a> dissolves the parliament after Prime minister <a href="/wiki/Pedro_Santana_Lopes" title="Pedro Santana Lopes">Pedro Santana Lopes</a> fails to present a plan to solve cabinet instability. The elections are expected to be scheduled to February 2005. <a class="external text" href="http://www.cnn.com/2004/WORLD/europe/11/30/portugal.ap/index.html" rel="nofollow">(CNN)</a> <a class="external text" href="http://news.bbc.co.uk/2/hi/europe/4056971.stm" rel="nofollow">(BBC)</a></li>
<li>U.K. <a href="/wiki/Home_Secretary" title="Home Secretary">Home Secretary</a> <a href="/wiki/David_Blunkett" title="David Blunkett">David Blunkett</a> defends his actions after newspaper allegations that he used his position to acquire a fast-track <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Visa_(document)" title="Visa (document)">visa</a> application for his former lover's nanny, ordering an independent enquiry into his own actions and denying any impropriety, whilst apologising for inadvertently misusing <a href="/wiki/Government" title="Government">government</a> funds to obtain her a first class train ticket. <a class="external text" href="http://news.bbc.co.uk/1/hi/uk_politics/4056987.stm" rel="nofollow">(BBC)</a></li>
<li>A South African court rules that the common law concept of marriage must be extended to include <a href="/wiki/Same-sex_marriage" title="Same-sex marriage">same-sex couples</a>. Although the ruling does not immediately permit <a href="/wiki/Same-sex_marriage_in_South_Africa" title="Same-sex marriage in South Africa">same-sex marriage in South Africa</a>, it is considered a major step in that direction. <a class="external text" href="http://www.365gay.com/newscon04/11/113004safWed.htm" rel="nofollow">(365gay.com)</a></li>
</ul>
